Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Sunnah Mu'akkadah before Zuhr and after Maghrib
Intra-Hanafi expansion on sunnah mu'akkadah counts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of sunnah mu'akkadah rak'ahs before Zuhr and the recommended method of performing the six rak'ahs after Maghrib, and explain the intra-madhhab difference with the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Only two rak'ahs before Zuhr are sunnah mu'akkadah; the six after Maghrib are independent and prayed with three taslims.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Ibn Nujaym unpacks a dispute within the Hanafi school about which supererogatory prayers are considered emphasized sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) and how they should be performed. The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq took one view, but later Hanafi authorities, including the Sahibayn, differed. This lesson will walk you through the evidence and the final mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issues
The passage discusses two questions: (a) Are the four rak'ahs before Zuhr sunnah mu'akkadah or mustahabb? (b) Should the six after Maghrib be prayed with one taslim or three? And are they counted as part of the sunnah or independent?
2
Follow the proof from the matn
The author of Kanz argues that the Prophet's constant practice (muwazabah) was on four before Zuhr based on Abu Dawud. The six after Maghrib are proven by a hadith.
Constant practice is a key evidence for sunnah mu'akkadah.
3
Examine the counter-evidence
The Ibn Umar hadith in Sahihayn shows only two rak'ahs, challenging the claim of constant practice on four. For the six, the hadith phrase 'did not speak evil between them' implies three taslims.
The counter-evidence is also from sound hadith, creating an intra-madhhab difference.
4
Understand the tarjih
The commentator (Ibn Nujaym) leans toward the view that the four are not sunnah mu'akkadah (only mustahabb) and the six should be with three taslims, citing many later sources.
Tarjih is based on reconciling hadiths and the principle that praying more than four with one taslim is less preferred.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative position for fatwa: two rak'ahs before Zuhr are sunnah mu'akkadah, and the six after Maghrib are a separate recommended prayer with three taslims.
This is the view of the Sahibayn and later Hanafi authorities.

المواظبة عليها في أبي داود فإنه نص في مواظبته على الأربع دون الست للمتأمل ا هـ. وقد يقال: إنما لم تكن الأربع سنة لما في الصـحـيـحـين عـن ابـن عـمـر قال : صليت مع رسول الله ركعتين قبل الظهر وركعتين بعدها وركعتين بعد المغرب وركعتين بعد العشاء وركعتين بعد الجمعة. وحدثتني حفصة بنت عمران النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يصلي ركعتين خفيفتين بعد ما يطلع الفجر ا هـ. فهو معارض لنقل المواظبة على الأربع فلذا التجنيس أنه . أن يستحب يصلي الست بثلاث تسليمات. ولم يذكر المصنف من المندوبات الأربع بعد الظهر. وصرح باستحبابها جماعة من المشايخ الحديث أبي داود والترمذي والنسائي. وحكى في فتح القدير اختلافاً بين أهل عصره في مسألتين: الأولى هل السنة المؤكدة محسوبة من المستحب في الأربع بعد الظهر وبعد العشاء وفي الست بعد المغرب أو لا. الثانية على تقدير الأولى هل يؤدي الكل بتسليمة واحدة أو بتسلمتين. واختار الأول فيهما وأطال الكلام وقبل العشاء بأربع فحسن لأن النبي الله لم يواظب عليها قوله : (فإنه نص في مواظبته على الأربع الخ) لأن مفاد الحديث أنه صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم تارة يصلي ستاً وتارة يقتصر على الأربع، وعلى كل فالأربع مواظب عليها لأنها بعض الستة قوله : (وقد يقال الخ) أي قد يقال في دفع المواظبة. أقول : ولي هنا نظر لأنه لا يخلو من أ يكون المراد من الركعتين في هذه المواضع المذكورة في حديث ابن عمر أنها الراتبة أو غير الراتبة، فإن كان الأول يرد مثل ما أورده في التي قبل الظهر والتي بعد الجمعة فإنه يقتضي عدم المواظبة على الأربع فيهما، وإن كان الثاني وهو الذي جمع به في الفتح بين هذا الحديث وحديث عائشة أنه الله تعالى كان يصلي أربعاً قبل الظهر بقوله إما بأن الأربع كان يصليها عليه السلام في بيته وما رآه ابن عمر تحية المسجد أو بأن ابن عمر كان تلك ورداً یری آخر سببه الزوال وهو مذهب بعض العلماء ا هـ . ثم بعد العشاء فيقتضي أن الأربع بعد الجمعة غير راتبه وأن الركعتين بعد العشاء الراتبة، وبه يتم ما ذكره المؤلف من الدفع لكن يحتاج إلى الجواب عن التي بعد الجمعة . نعم . ظاهر على رواية عن أبي حنيفة ذكرها في الذخيرة أنها ركعتان فلينأمل، وقد يقال : إنها الركعتان الزائدتان على الأربع كما هو قول أبي يوسف كما مر قوله : (واختار الأول فيهما أي اختار ما تضمنه الترديد الأول في كل من المسألتين لكن يرد عليه ما ذكروه في صلاة الست بعد المغرب فإن مقتضى كلامه أن الأولى فيها أن تكون بتسليمة واحدة، وقد صرح بأن الراتبة تحتسب منها والتصريح بخلاف كل ثابت . قال الشيخ إسماعيل : وفي المفتاح وندب ست ركعات بعد المغرب يعني غير سنة المغرب لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام من صلى بعد المغرب ست ركعات لم يتكلم فيما بينهن بسوء عدلن عبادة ثنتي عشرة سنة ) كذا في الإيضاح اهـ. الغرنوية : وصلاة الأوابين وهي ما بين العشاءين ست ركعات بثلاث تسليمات. قال أبو البقاء القرشي في شرحها : يصلي ست ركعات بنية صلاة الأوابين يقرأ في كل ركعة بعد الفاتحة «قل يا أيها الكافرون» مرة و قل هو الله أحد ثلاث مرات قاله الشيخ عبد الله البسطامي ا هـ . وكذلك صرح في التجنيس وغرر الأذكار بأنها بثلاث تسليمات ثم قال في الغرر الأذكارية وفسره يعني أنساً راوي الحديث بثلاث تسليمات ا هـ . کلام الشيخ إسماعيل ثم قال : أن الحديث يشير إلى ذلك حيث قال : لم يتكلم فيما بينهن بسوء إذ مفهومه أنه لو تكلم بخير استحق الموعود ا.هـ. فظهر أنها ست مستقلة كما هو صريح المفتاح وظاهر شرح الغزنوية وإنها بثلاث تسليمات وإن قال في الدرر والتنوير إنها بتسليمة واحدة. قال الرسلي : والذي يظهر لي في وجه الفرق بين هذه الست وبين الأربع في الظهر والعشاء أنها لما زادت عن الأربع وكان جمعها بتسليمة واحدة خلاف الأفضل لما تقرر أن الأفضل فيهما رباع عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله، ولو سلم على رأس الأربع لزم أن يسلم في الشفع الثالث على رأس الركعتين فيكون فيه من هذه الحيثية فكان المستحب فيه ثلاث تسليمات ليكون على نسق واحد. هذا ما ظهر لي من الوجه ولم أره لغيري فليتأمل ا هـ وهو حسن
Book of Prayer, Chapter of Witr and Supererogatory Prayers. The constant practice (muwazabah) upon them is in Abu Dawud, for it is explicit in his constant practice of four, not six, for the reflective person - end. It may be said: The four are not sunnah because of what is in the two Sahihs from Ibn Umar: he said, 'I prayed with the Messenger of Allah two rak'ahs before Zuhr and two after it, two after Maghrib, two after Isha, and two after Jumu'ah. And Hafsah bint Umar narrated to me that the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, used to pray two light rak'ahs after the dawn had risen.' So it contradicts the transmission of constant practice on the four, therefore they are not sunnah. As for the six after Maghrib, because Ibn Umar narrated that he, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever prays six rak'ahs after Maghrib is written among the Awwabin,' and recited His statement: 'Indeed, He is ever Forgiving to the often-returning [to Him]' [Al-Isra: 25]. And it is mentioned in al-Tajnīs that it is recommended to pray the six with three taslims. The author did not mention among the recommended the four after Zuhr, but a group of scholars explicitly stated its recommendation based on the hadith of Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and al-Nasa'i. And in Fath al-Qadir, a difference is narrated among his contemporaries on two issues: First, whether the sunnah mu'akkadah is counted from the mustahabb in the four after Zuhr and after Isha and in the six after Maghrib or not. Second, assuming the first, whether one performs the whole with one taslim or two taslims. And he chose the first in both and elaborated. And the four before Isha are good, because the Prophet did not constantly practice them...
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute over the status and performance of certain supererogatory prayers associated with the five daily prayers. The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq (the matn) initially states that the constant practice (muwazabah) of the Prophet was on four rak'ahs before Zuhr, not six, based on Abu Dawud. The commentator (Ibn Nujaym, author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) then raises an objection: the hadith in the Sahihayn from Ibn Umar reports that the Prophet prayed only two rak'ahs before and after Zuhr, which contradicts the claim of constant practice on four. Hence the four are not sunnah mu'akkadah but mustahabb. The commentator further discusses the six rak'ahs after Maghrib, citing the hadith that whoever prays six rak'ahs after Maghrib is recorded among the Awwabin (the often-returning). He cites al-Tajnīs that it is recommended to pray these six with three taslims. The passage then reports a dispute from Fath al-Qadir about two questions: (1) whether the sunnah mu'akkadah (the regular two rak'ahs) is counted as part of the recommended four (or six), and (2) whether to pray the entire set with one taslim or two. The commentator notes that the author of Kanz chose the first option in both (i.e., the sunnah is counted, and one taslim is used). However, the commentator then raises an objection: the six after Maghrib should be with three taslims because of the hadith and the principle that praying four with one taslim is less preferred at Abu Hanifa's view. He quotes various sources including al-Miftah, Sharh al-Ghaznawiyyah, and al-Durar wa al-Tanwir, concluding that the six are an independent prayer (not part of the sunnah) and should be with three taslims. The passage ends with a personal reflection by al-Rasli on the reasoning for distinguishing the six from the four in Zuhr and Isha.

Key Terms
المواظبة (al-muwāẓabah): The Prophet's constant practice of a particular prayer, used as evidence for sunnah mu'akkadah.
السنة المؤكدة (al-sunnah al-mu'akkadah): The emphasized sunnah that the Prophet constantly performed and rarely left, considered obligatory for some schools but a distinct category in Hanafi fiqh between fard and mustahabb.
تسليمة (taslīmah): A single taslim (saying 'al-salamu alaykum') to conclude a set of rak'ahs. The dispute is whether to pray multiple rak'ahs with one taslim or separate taslims for each two rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are the four rak'ahs before Zuhr not considered sunnah mu'akkadah?
A) Because the Prophet never prayed them
B) Because the hadith in the Sahihayn reports only two rak'ahs before Zuhr, contradicting constant practice on four
C) Because Abu Hanifa explicitly said so
D) Because they are only recommended for the imam

Key Takeaway
Within the Hanafi school, the sunnah mu'akkadah before Zuhr is two rak'ahs; the six after Maghrib are an independent recommended prayer performed with three taslims.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Salat al-Duha: Recommendation and Reconciliation of Hadith
Ruling on recommendation of Salat al-Duha with proof and reconciliation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on Salat al-Duha, reconcile the apparent contradiction in the hadith regarding the Prophet's practice, and state the minimum and maximum recommended rak'ahs.

Core Idea
Salat al-Duha is mustahabb (recommended) not sunnah mu'akkadah; Aisha's reports are reconciled by distinguishing personal observation from transmitted knowledge.

The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq omitted Salat al-Duha from the list of recommended prayers due to the scholarly disagreement about its status. In this passage, the commentator presents both sides of the dispute, citing the key hadith evidence, and then adopts the preponderant view that it is recommended. He carefully reconciles the apparent conflict between Aisha's statements, showing that the Hanafi position is well-founded.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Recognize that the author omitted Duha because of ikhtilaf; there are two views: one denying recommendation (Ibn Umar's stance) and one affirming it.
Ibn Umar's denial is based on his understanding; the commentator does not dismiss it outright but weighs the evidence.
2
Examine the proof for recommendation
The hadith in Sahih Muslim from Aisha that the Prophet prayed Duha four and more is the primary evidence. Understand why this is considered preponderant over the denial.
The commentator calls this view 'al-rajih' (preponderant).
3
Resolve the apparent contradiction
Analyze the two reports from Aisha: one denying she saw the Prophet pray it, one affirming she prays it. Apply the commentator's reconciliation: personal observation vs. transmitted report, or denial of constancy and openness.
The commentator offers multiple possibilities, all preserving the authenticity of both reports.
4
Derive the ruling parameters
From al-Munya and al-Tabarani's hadith, extract the minimum (2 rak'ahs) and maximum (12 rak'ahs) and the varying rewards.
The hadith lists increasing rewards for 2,4,6,8,12 rak'ahs.
5
State the Hanafi position
Confirm that the mufta bihi is mustahabb (sunnah ghayr muakkadah), not sunnah mu'akkadah, due to the ikhtilaf and the evidence.
Hanafi position: recommended, not emphasized sunnah.

Source Text

ولم يذكر المصنف من المندوبات صلاة الضحى للاختلاف فيها فقيل لا تستحب لما في صحيح البخاري من إنكار ابن عمر لها، وقيل مستحبة لما في صحيح مسلم عن عائشة أنه عليه السلام كان يصلي الضحى أربع ركعات ويزيد ما شاء، وهذا هو الراجح ولا يخالفه ما في الصحيحين عنها ما رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي سبحة الضحى قط وإني لأسبحها لاحتمال أنها أخبرت في النفي عن رؤيتها ومشاهدتها وفي الإثبات عن خبره عليه السلام أو خبر غيره عنه أو أنها أنكرتها مواظبة وإعلاناً. ويدل لذلك كله قولها وإني لأسبحها». وفي رواية الموطأ «وإني لأستحبها» من الاستحباب وهو أظهر في المراد وظاهر ما في المنية يدل على أن أقلها ركعتان وأكثرها ثنتا عشرة ركعة لما رواه الطبراني في الكبير عن أبي الدرداء قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم «من صلى ركعتين لم يكتب من الغافلين ومن صلى أربعاً كتب من العابدين ومن صلى ستاً كفي ذلك اليوم، ومن صلى ثمانياً كتبه الله من القانتين، ومن صلى اثنتي عشرة ركعة بنى الله له بيتاً في الجنة، وما من يوم وليلة إلا والله من يمن به على عباده وصدقة وما من الله على أحد من
The author did not mention among the recommended prayers Salat al-Duha because of the difference of opinion therein. It was said that it is not recommended, based on what is in Sahih al-Bukhari from Ibn Umar's denial of it. And it was said that it is recommended, based on what is in Sahih Muslim from Aisha that he, peace be upon him, used to pray Duha four rak'ahs and increase as he wished. This is the preponderant view. And it is not contradicted by what is in the two Sahihs from her: 'I never saw the Messenger of Allah pray the Duha supererogatory prayer at all, yet I do pray it.' This is because it is possible that she informed in the negative based on her own seeing, and in the positive based on his (the Prophet's) report or another's report, or that she denied it out of constancy and publicity. Evidence for all this is her saying 'And I do pray it.' And in the narration of al-Muwatta: 'And I do recommend it' from istihbab, which is more apparent in meaning. And the apparent meaning of what is in al-Munya indicates that the minimum is two rak'ahs and the maximum is twelve rak'ahs, based on what al-Tabarani narrated in al-Kabir from Abu al-Darda' who said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever prays two rak'ahs is not recorded among the heedless; whoever prays four is recorded among the worshippers; whoever prays six suffices for that day; whoever prays eight, Allah records him among the devout; whoever prays twelve rak'ahs, Allah builds for him a house in Paradise. And there is not a day or night except that Allah bestows upon His servants a gift and a charity, and He does not bestow upon anyone...'
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage addresses the recommendation of Salat al-Duha (the forenoon prayer), which the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq omitted due to scholarly disagreement. The commentator presents two views: (1) some scholars say it is not recommended, citing Ibn Umar's denial in Sahih al-Bukhari; (2) the preponderant view (al-rajih) is that it is recommended, based on the hadith in Sahih Muslim from Aisha that the Prophet used to pray Duha four rak'ahs and more. The commentator reconciles the apparent contradiction in Aisha's statements: she also said she never saw the Prophet pray Duha, yet she herself prayed it. The resolution is that her negative statement refers to her personal observation, while her positive statement refers to knowledge from the Prophet or others. Alternatively, she may have denied the Prophet's constant practice and open performance, not the recommendation itself. The hadith from al-Tabarani specifies the minimum (two rak'ahs) and maximum (twelve rak'ahs) with varying rewards. This establishes the ruling that Salat al-Duha is mustahabb, and the recommended number is up to twelve.

Key Terms
صلاة الضحى (ṣalāt al-ḍuḥā): The forenoon supererogatory prayer, performed after sunrise until before zawal.
الاستحباب (al-istiḥbāb): The legal recommendation, a level below sunnah mu'akkadah; performing it is rewarded, not performing it is not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the preponderant view on Salat al-Duha, and what is the primary evidence?
A) It is not recommended, based on Ibn Umar's denial
B) It is recommended, based on Aisha's hadith in Muslim
C) It is obligatory, based on Quranic verses
D) It is makruh, based on contradictory reports

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Duha is a recommended (mustahabb) prayer with a minimum of two and maximum of twelve rak'ahs, established by the preponderance of evidence and reconciliation of hadith.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Recommended Voluntary Prayers (Mandubat) in the Hanafi School
Commentary expanding on omitted recommended prayers with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Salat al-Duha, Tahiyyat al-Masjid, two rak'ahs after wudu, and Salat al-Istikharah, and explain the evidence for their recommendation.

Core Idea
Recommended prayers are established by the Sunnah; apparent contradictions in hadith are reconciled to confirm their desirability.

This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, which fills in the recommended prayers omitted by the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It addresses the disagreement over Salat al-Duha and presents the Hanafi methodology of reconciling conflicting hadith, then lists other recommended prayers with their established proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the omitted prayers
Note which recommended prayers the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq omitted from his discussion: Salat al-Duha, Tahiyyat al-Masjid, two rak'ahs after wudu, and Salat al-Istikharah.
The commentator explicitly points out these omissions.
2
Understand the dispute over Salat al-Duha
Recognize the two conflicting reports: Ibn Umar's denial vs. Aisha's affirmation. See how the Hanafi school reconciles them by interpreting Aisha's negative statement as referring to public regularity, not absolute negation.
The preponderant view (rajih) is that Duha is mustahabb.
3
Analyze the evidence for each prayer
For each recommended prayer, identify the specific hadith or principle cited. For Duha, the hadith from Abu Darda mentions rewards for different numbers of rak'ahs. For Istikharah, the full hadith from Jabir is given.
The commentator emphasizes that the imperative 'فليركع ركعتين' indicates recommendation, not obligation.
4
Apply the Hanafi ruling
Conclude that all these prayers are mustahabb (recommended) in the Hanafi school, with the general conditions of prayer applying.
The time for Duha is from sunrise to noon; for Istikharah, preferred when the day has risen.

صحيح مسلم عن عائشة أنه عليه السلام كان يصلي الضحى أربع ركعات ويزيد ما شاء، وهذا هو الراجح ولا يخالفه ما في الصحيحين عنها ما رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي سبحة الضحى قط وإني لأسبحها لاحتمال أنها أخبرت في النفي عن رؤيتها ومشاهدتها وفي الإثبات عن خبره عليه السلام أو خبر غيره عنه أو أنها أنكرتها مواظبة وإعلاناً. ويدل لذلك كله قولها وإني لأسبحها». وفي رواية الموطأ «وإني لأستحبها» من الاستحباب وهو أظهر في المراد وظاهر ما في المنية يدل على أن أقلها ركعتان وأكثرها ثنتا عشرة ركعة لما رواه الطبراني في الكبير عن أبي الدرداء قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم «من صلى ركعتين لم يكتب من الغافلين ومن صلى أربعاً كتب من العابدين ومن صلى ستاً كفي ذلك اليوم، ومن صلى ثمانياً كتبه الله من القانتين، ومن صلى اثنتي عشرة ركعة بنى الله له بيتاً في الجنة، وما من يوم وليلة إلا والله من يمن به على عباده وصدقة وما من الله على أحد من عباده أفضل من أن يلهمه ذكره قال المنذري : ورواته ثقات. ولم أر بيان أول وقتها وآخره لمشايخنا هنا ولعلهم تركوه للعلم به وهو أنه من ارتفاع الشمس إلى زوالها كما لا يخفى. ثم رأيت صاحب البدائع صرح به في كتاب الأيمان فيما إذا حلف ليكلمنه الضحى فقال إنه من الساعة التي تحل فيها الصلاة إلى الزوال وهو وقت صلاة الضحى ا هـ . ومن المندوبات تحية المسجد وقد قدمناها في أحكام المسجد قبيل باب الوتر، وصرح في الخلاصة باستحبابها وأنها ركعتان. ومن المندوبات ركعتان عقيب الوضوء كما في شرح النقاية والتبيين. ومن المندوبات صلاة الاستخارة وقد أفصحت السنة ببيانها فعن جابر قال : كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يعلمنا الاستخارة في الأمور كلها كما يعلمنا السورة من القرآن يقول : إذ هم أحدكم بالأمر فليركع ركعتين من غير الفريضة ثم ليقل: اللهم إني أستخيرك بعلمك، وأستقدرك بقدرتك، وأسألك من فضلك العظيم، فإنك تقدر ولا أقدر وتعلم ولا أعلم وأنت علام الغيوب. اللهم إن كنت تعلم أن هذا الأمر خير لي في ديني ومعاشي وعاقبة أمري أو قال عاجل أمري وآجله فقدر لي ويسره لي ثم بارك فيه، وإن كنت تعلم أن هذا الأمر شر لي في ديني ومعاشي وعاقبة أمري أو قال عاجله فاصرفه عني واصرفني عنه وقدر لي الخير حيث كان ثم رضني به. قلت : وفي شرح الشيخ إسماعيل عن الشريعة ويتحري لها وقت تعالي النهار حتى ترمض الفصال من الظهيرة قال : وفي شرحها تعالي النهار علوه وارتفاعه. وترمض من باب علم أي تحترق أخفاف الفصال جمع فصيل ولد الناقة إذا فصل عن أمه والظهيرة نصف النهار. هذا مأخوذ من قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام فيما أخرجه مسلم عن زيد بن أرقم كما ذكره في المشارق من قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «صلاة الأوابين إذا رمضت الفصال». قال الشيخ إسمعيل أقول : ومقتضاه أفضلية كونها أقرب إلى الظهيرة ا شرح المنية عن الحاوي : ووقتها المختار إذا مضى ربع النهار ثم ذكر الحديث. وذكر الشيخ إسماعيل عن الشرعة أنه يقرأ فيها سورتي الضحى أي سورة والشمس وضحاها وسورة «والضحى والليل» ا هـ . قلت : رأيت في التحفة لابن حجر الشافعي ما نصه قال بعضهم : ويسن قراءة والشمس والضحى لحديث فيه رواه البيهقي اهـ . قال : ولم يبين أنه يقرؤهما إذا زاد على ركعتين في كل ركعتين من ركعاتها أو في الأوليين فقط ، وعليه فما عداهما يقرأ فيه الكافرون» و «الإخلاص كما علم مما مرا ومراده بما مر بحثاً أنهما يسنان أيضاً في سائر السنن التي لم ترد لها قراءة مخصوصة قوله : (ومن المندوبات صلاة الاستخارة قال الشيخ إسماعيل : وفي شرح الشرعة : من هم بأمر وكان لا يدري عاقبته ولا يعرف أن الخير في تركه أو الإقدام عليه فقد أمره رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن يركع ركعتين يقرأ في الأولى فاتحة الكتاب وقل يا أيها الكافرون»، وفي الثانية (الفاتحة» و «قل هو الله أحد» فإذا فرغ قال اللهم الخ . ثم الحديث
In it is a good elaboration as is his habit, and its apparent meaning is that he did not come across it in the speech of those before him. The author did not mention from the recommended prayers the Duha prayer due to disagreement about it. It was said it is not recommended because of what is in Sahih al-Bukhari from Ibn Umar's rejection of it. And it was said it is recommended because of what is in Sahih Muslim from Aisha that the Prophet ﷺ used to pray Duha four rak'ahs and increase as he wished. This is the preponderant view. And it is not contradicted by what is in the two Sahihs from her: 'I never saw the Messenger of Allah ﷺ pray the Duha supererogatory prayer at all, yet I do perform it' — because it is possible that she reported in the negative based on her own sighting and witnessing, and in the positive based on his ﷺ report or someone else's report from him, or that she denied it as a regular practice and publicly. All of this is indicated by her saying 'and I indeed perform it'. And in the Muwatta transmission: 'and I indeed consider it recommended' from istihbab, which is more apparent in meaning. And the apparent meaning of what is in al-Munya indicates that its minimum is two rak'ahs and its maximum is twelve rak'ahs, because of what al-Tabarani narrated in al-Kabir from Abu Darda who said: the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said, 'Whoever prays two rak'ahs is not recorded among the heedless; whoever prays four is recorded among the devout; whoever prays six is sufficed for that day; whoever prays eight is recorded by Allah among the obedient; whoever prays twelve rak'ahs, Allah builds for him a house in Paradise. There is no day or night except that Allah bestows upon His servants and charity, and Allah has not bestowed upon any of His servants anything better than inspiring him with His remembrance.' Al-Mundhiri said: its narrators are trustworthy. I have not seen an explanation of its beginning and end time from our scholars here; perhaps they left it because it is known, which is from sunrise to zenith as is not hidden. Then I saw the author of al-Bada'i' explicitly stated it in the Book of Oaths regarding one who swore to speak to him at Duha: it is from the hour when prayer becomes lawful until noon, which is the time of Duha prayer. From the recommended prayers is Tahiyyat al-Masjid, and we have already presented it in the rulings of the mosque before the chapter on Witr. And it is explicitly stated in al-Khulasa that it is recommended and that it is two rak'ahs. From the recommended prayers are two rak'ahs after wudu, as in Sharh al-Nuqaya and al-Tabyin. From the recommended prayers is Salat al-Istikharah; the Sunnah has explained it clearly. From Jabir who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ used to teach us istikharah in all matters as he taught us a surah from the Quran. He said: When one of you contemplates a matter, let him pray two rak'ahs of non-obligatory prayer, then say: 'O Allah, I seek Your guidance by Your knowledge, and I seek Your power by Your power, and I ask You from Your great bounty, for You are able and I am not, You know and I do not, and You are the Knower of the unseen. O Allah, if You know that this matter is good for me in my religion, my livelihood, and my consequence, (or he said: my immediate and future affairs), then decree it for me, make it easy for me, and then bless me in it. And if You know that this matter is evil for me in my religion, my livelihood, and my consequence, (or he said: my immediate and future affairs), then turn it away from me and turn me away from it, and decree for me goodness wherever it is, and then make me content with it.' I say: In the commentary of Shaykh Isma'il from al-Shari'a: and one should seek the time when the day is elevated until the young camels feel the heat of the noon. He said: in its commentary: 'elevation of the day' is its height and rising; 'feel the heat' is from the root 'ilm meaning the hooves of the young camels burn; 'fisal' plural of fasil: the young camel when it is weaned from its mother; 'al-zahira' is midday. This is taken from his ﷺ statement in what Muslim narrated from Zayd ibn Arqam as mentioned in al-Mashariq: 'The prayer of the Awwabin (the oft-returning) is when the young camels feel the heat of the noon.' Shaykh Isma'il said: I say: its implication is that its superiority is in being closer to noon. In Sharh al-Munya from al-Hawi: its preferred time is when a quarter of the day has passed, then he mentioned the hadith. And Shaykh Isma'il mentioned from al-Shari'a that one recites in it Surah al-Duha, i.e., Surat al-Shams wa al-Duha, and Surat al-Duha wa al-Layl. I say: I saw in al-Tuhfa of Ibn Hajar al-Shafi'i the text: Some said: it is sunnah to recite 'al-Shams wa al-Duha' due to a hadith narrated by al-Bayhaqi. He said: and he did not explain whether one recites these two when exceeding two rak'ahs, in every two rak'ahs of its rak'ahs, or only in the first two; accordingly, in the remaining ones one recites Surat al-Kafirun and al-Ikhlas, as is known from what has passed. His intent by 'what has passed' is that these two are also sunnah in all other sunnah prayers that have no specific recitation prescribed. His statement: 'From the recommended prayers is Salat al-Istikharah.' Shaykh Isma'il said: In Sharh al-Shari'a: Whoever contemplates a matter and does not know its outcome nor knows whether good is in abandoning it or proceeding with it, the Messenger of Allah ﷺ commanded him to pray two rak'ahs, reciting in the first Fatiha and Qul ya ayyuha al-kafirun, and in the second Fatiha and Qul huwa Allahu ahad. Then when he finishes, he says 'Allahumma...' etc. Then the hadith.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapters of Witr and Nawafil from the book Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The commentator, Ibn Nujaym, begins by noting that the author omitted several recommended prayers (mandubat) due to differences of opinion. The first omitted prayer is Salat al-Duha. He presents the disagreement: some say it is not recommended based on Ibn Umar's rejection in Sahih al-Bukhari, while others say it is recommended based on Aisha's report in Sahih Muslim that the Prophet ﷺ prayed it. The preponderant view (rajih) is that it is recommended. He reconciles Aisha's hadith of negation with her positive report by explaining that she may have reported based on her own lack of sighting, or she denied public regularity. The minimum is two rak'ahs, maximum twelve, based on a hadith from Abu Darda narrated by al-Tabarani. The time is from sunrise to noon, as clarified by the author of al-Bada'i'. Next, Tahiyyat al-Masjid (two rak'ahs upon entering the mosque) is recommended, as is praying two rak'ahs after wudu. Finally, Salat al-Istikharah is discussed in detail, with the full hadith from Jabir and additional notes on preferred recitations and timing. The commentator emphasizes that the basis for all these is the Sunnah, and the Hanafi position is that they are mustahabb (recommended), though there is some debate over Duha.

Key Terms
مندوب (mandub): An act that is recommended but not obligatory; its performance is rewarded and its abandonment is not sinful.
صلاة الضحى (salat al-duha): A voluntary prayer performed after sunrise until noon, with minimum two and maximum twelve rak'ahs, recommended according to the preponderant Hanafi view.
صلاة الأوابين (salat al-awwabin): A voluntary prayer of six rak'ahs prayed in three sets of two, after Maghrib (between Maghrib and Isha), recommended for those who frequently repent.
صلاة الاستخارة (salat al-istikhara): A two-rak'ah prayer with a specific supplication for seeking guidance from Allah when making a decision.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Hanafi ruling on Salat al-Duha?
A) It is obligatory (wajib).
B) It is not recommended (makruh).
C) It is recommended (mustahabb) according to the preponderant view.
D) It is prohibited (haram) because it was rejected by Ibn Umar.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends Salat al-Duha, Tahiyyat al-Masjid, two rak'ahs after wudu, and Salat al-Istikharah based on authentic hadith and careful reconciliation of conflicting reports.

Salat al-Duha: Ruling, Time, and Preference
Describes the time of Salat al-Duha and its preferred time near noon

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Salat al-Duha (mandub), specify its time (from sunrise to zawal), and explain the evidence from the hadith supporting the preferred time near noon.

Core Idea
Salat al-Duha is recommended, time from sunrise to noon; preferred near noon as per the hadith of the young camels.

Salat al-Duha is a recommended prayer with a specific time window from sunrise until noon. The Hanafi school emphasizes a preferred time close to noon, derived from a prophetic hadith. In this lesson, you will learn its ruling, time boundaries, and the evidence that shapes the preferred time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage begins by listing Salat al-Duha among al-mandubat (recommended acts). Identify that the Hanafi school classifies it as mandub (recommended), which is a level below sunnah muakkadah.
Some scholars consider it sunnah muakkadah, but the text uses 'mandubat'.
2
Determine the time boundaries
The passage states the time is 'from the rising of the sun to its zenith (zawal)'. Confirm that this means the prayer can be performed any time after sunrise until the sun reaches its noon position.
The author notes that earlier scholars did not elaborate because it is well-known.
3
Locate the evidence (dalil)
The preferred time is derived from the hadith: 'The prayer of the penitent (awwabin) is when the young camels feel the heat.' Identify that this hadith indicates a time close to noon, when the heat intensifies.
The hadith is narrated by Muslim from Zayd ibn Arqam.
4
Understand the preferred time
The phrase 'when the young camels feel the heat' is metaphorical for high noon. The passage explains that the preferred time is when a quarter of the day has passed, i.e., closer to noon.
The 'chosen time' is after one quarter of the day has elapsed.
5
Note the recommended recitation
The passage concludes by recommending recitation of Surah al-Shams (91) and Surah al-Duha (93) during this prayer.
This is a sunnah for the prayer, not an obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن المندوبات صلاة الضحى، وأما وقتها فقالوا من ارتفاع الشمس إلى زوالها. ولم أر بيان أول وقتها وآخره لمشايخنا هنا ولعلهم تركوه للعلم به وهو أنه من ارتفاع الشمس إلى زوالها كما لا يخفى. ثم رأيت صاحب البدائع صرح به في كتاب الأيمان فيما إذا حلف ليكلمنه الضحى فقال إنه من الساعة التي تحل فيها الصلاة إلى الزوال وهو وقت صلاة الضحى. ويتحري لها وقت تعالي النهار حتى ترمض الفصال من الظهيرة. وتعالي النهار علوه وارتفاعه. وترمض أي تحترق أخفاف الفصال جمع فصيل ولد الناقة إذا فصل عن أمه والظهيرة نصف النهار. هذا مأخوذ من قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام فيما أخرجه مسلم عن زيد بن أرقم «صلاة الأوابين إذا رمضت الفصال». ومقتضاه أفضلية كونها أقرب إلى الظهيرة. ووقتها المختار إذا مضى ربع النهار. ويقرأ فيها سورتي الضحى أي «والشمس وضحاها» وسورة «والضحى والليل».
Among the recommended acts is Salat al-Duha. As for its time, they said: from the rising of the sun to its zenith. I have not seen an explanation of its beginning and end from our scholars here; perhaps they left it because it is known, i.e., it is from the rising of the sun to its zenith, as is not hidden. Then I saw that the author of al-Bada'i' explicitly stated in the book of oaths, concerning one who swore to speak to someone in the Duha time, that it is from the hour when prayer becomes permissible to the zenith, and that is the time of Salat al-Duha. And one should seek for it a time when the day is high until the young camels (fisal) feel the heat from the midday heat. And 'ta'ali al-nahar' means its height and elevation. 'Tarmadu' means the hooves of the fisal burn—fisal is plural of fasil, the young camel when weaned from its mother—and al-zahirah is midday. This is taken from his statement, peace be upon him, as narrated by Muslim from Zayd ibn Arqam: 'The prayer of the penitent (awwabin) is when the young camels feel the heat.' And its implication is the preference of it being closer to noon. And its chosen time is when a quarter of the day has passed. And in it one recites the two Suras of Duha, i.e., 'And the sun and its brightness' and 'By the forenoon and the night'.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling and time of Salat al-Duha. It first states that it is among the recommended prayers (mandubat). The time is from sunrise until zawal (zenith). The author notes that earlier scholars did not elaborate because it is well-known, and he cites al-Badai'i for confirmation. The preferred time is when the day is high, as indicated by the hadith about the young camels feeling the heat—this is near noon. The hadith (Muslim) calls it 'Salat al-Awwabin' (prayer of the penitent). The chosen time is after one quarter of the day has passed. Recommended recitation includes Surah al-Shams (91) and Surah al-Duha (93). This is a Hanafi ruling with proof from Sunnah.

Key Terms
صلاة الضحى (salat al-duha): A recommended prayer performed after sunrise until noon.
الأوابين (al-awwabin): The penitent; used in a hadith to refer to those who pray Salat al-Duha.
رمضت الفصال (ramidat al-fisal): The young camels feel the heat on their hooves; a metaphor for high noon heat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Sunrise
B) Mid-morning
C) Zawal (noon)
D) Afternoon

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Duha is a recommended prayer from sunrise to noon, with the best time close to noon as indicated by the hadith.

Salat al-Istikhara: Ruling and Supplication
Presents the hadith on Istikhara and its recommended recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Salat al-Istikhara and explain the procedure including the specific supplication.

Core Idea
Istikhara is a recommended two-rak'at prayer with a specific du'a to seek Allah's guidance in any permissible matter.

When faced with a decision and uncertain which path holds good, the Sunnah provides a beautiful prayer: Salat al-Istikhara. This lesson unpacks the hadith that establishes its recommendation and teaches its proper performance, so you can confidently turn to Allah when in doubt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage opens with 'Among the recommended acts is Salat al-Istikhara.' This tells us the legal classification: mandub (recommended), not obligatory.
The Arabic word 'مندوبات' is the plural of mandub, a fiqh term for a recommended act.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Jabir (Bukhari) as the proof. The Prophet ﷺ used to teach his Companions Istikhara 'as he taught them a Surah from the Quran.'
This indicates the importance of this practice.
3
Analyze the command in the hadith
The phrase 'When one of you intends to do something, let him pray two rak'ats' contains the command 'fal-yarka' (let him pray). In Hanafi usul, such a command indicates recommendation (nadb) when there is no qarina (evidence) for obligation.
The ruling is mandub, not wajib.
4
Extract the procedure
The hadith outlines: (1) two rak'ats of nafl, (2) a specific supplication after prayer. Sharh al-Shar'ah adds reciting Surah al-Kafirun in the first rak'ah and Surah al-Ikhlas in the second after al-Fatiha.
This is the established Hanafi practice.
5
Apply the ruling to a modern scenario
For example, if a student is unsure which university to choose, they may pray Istikhara and then proceed with the option that feels most comfortable, trusting Allah's decree.
Istikhara does not require a dream; it is about supplication and placing trust in Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن المندوبات صلاة الاستخارة وقد أفصحت السنة ببيانها فعن جابر قال : كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يعلمنا الاستخارة في الأمور كلها كما يعلمنا السورة من القرآن يقول : إذ هم أحدكم بالأمر فليركع ركعتين من غير الفريضة ثم ليقل: اللهم إني أستخيرك بعلمك، وأستقدرك بقدرتك، وأسألك من فضلك العظيم، فإنك تقدر ولا أقدر وتعلم ولا أعلم وأنت علام الغيوب. اللهم إن كنت تعلم أن هذا الأمر خير لي في ديني ومعاشي وعاقبة أمري أو قال عاجل أمري وآجله فقدر لي ويسره لي ثم بارك فيه، وإن كنت تعلم أن هذا الأمر شر لي في ديني ومعاشي وعاقبة أمري أو قال عاجله فاصرفه عني واصرفني عنه وقدر لي الخير حيث كان ثم رضني به. قال : ويسمي حاجته. رواه البخاري وغيره. وفي شرح الشرعة: من هم بأمر وكان لا يدري عاقبته ولا يعرف أن الخير في تركه أو الإقدام عليه فقد أمره رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن يركع ركعتين يقرأ في الأولى فاتحة الكتاب وقل يا أيها الكافرون، وفي الثانية الفاتحة وقل هو الله أحد فإذا فرغ قال اللهم الخ.
Among the recommended acts is Salat al-Istikhara, and the Sunnah has explained it clearly. Jabir reported: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to teach us Istikhara in all matters as he taught us a Surah from the Quran. He said: When one of you intends to do something, let him pray two rak'ats of non-obligatory prayer, then say: 'O Allah, I seek Your guidance through Your knowledge, and I seek Your power through Your power, and I ask You from Your great bounty, for You are able while I am not, and You know while I do not, and You are the Knower of the unseen. O Allah, if You know that this matter is good for me in my religion, my livelihood, and the outcome of my affairs – or he said: in my immediate and future affairs – then decree it for me, make it easy for me, and then bless it for me. And if You know that this matter is evil for me in my religion, my livelihood, and the outcome of my affairs – or he said: in my immediate affairs – then turn it away from me, turn me away from it, and decree for me the good wherever it is, then make me pleased with it.' He said: And he should mention his need. Narrated by Bukhari and others. And in Sharh al-Shar'ah: Whoever intends a matter and does not know its outcome, nor knows whether good lies in leaving it or embarking on it, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) commanded him to pray two rak'ats, reciting in the first Fatiha and 'Say: O disbelievers', and in the second Fatiha and 'Say: He is Allah, the One'. When he finishes, he says 'O Allah...' etc.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage covers Salat al-Istikhara, a recommended prayer for seeking guidance from Allah when facing a decision. The hadith from Jabir (Bukhari) establishes the practice: two rak'ats of nafl followed by a specific supplication. The recitation recommended in Sharh al-Shar'ah is Surah al-Kafirun and al-Ikhlas, which is common practice. The supplication asks Allah to decree what is good and turn away what is evil. The prayer is performed for any permissible matter where one is uncertain.

Key Terms
صلاة الاستخارة (salat al-istikhara): A two-rak'at prayer with a specific supplication to seek Allah's guidance.
استخارة (istikhara): Seeking the better choice from Allah.
مندوب (mandub): A recommended act, rewarded if done, not sinful if omitted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the hadith command immediately before saying the du'a in Salat al-Istikhara?
A) Fast three days
B) Pray two rak'ats of non-obligatory prayer
C) Give charity
D) Make wudu

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Istikhara is a recommended two-rak'at prayer with a specific du'a, established by authentic hadith, to seek Allah's guidance in any permissible matter.

Salat al-Haja: The Preferred Two Rak'ats
Presents multiple narrations on rak'ats for Salat al-Haja

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Salat al-Haja, identify the primary evidence (dalil) from the Tirmidhi hadith, and explain why the two-rak'at version is the mufta bihi despite other narrations.

Core Idea
Salat al-Haja is recommended; the most authentic practice is two rak'ats, though other valid narrations exist.

This passage introduces Salat al-Haja (Prayer of Need), a recommended act of worship. Different sources mention varying numbers of rak'ats, from two to twelve. The Hanafi school, relying on a sound hadith from Tirmidhi, establishes two rak'ats as the preferred practice, while acknowledging the flexibility of other narrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and its Ruling Level
Recognize that Salat al-Haja is classified as a recommended (mandub/sunnah muakkadah) act. The passage states it is 'among the recommended acts' (ومن المندوبات).
2
Locate the Primary Dalil
Find the primary evidence: the hadith from Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa narrated by Tirmidhi, which explicitly commands performing two rak'ats after thorough wudu.
The hadith is quoted in the text: 'من كانت له إلى الله حاجة...فليتوضأ وليحسن الوضوء ثم ليصل ركعتين'.
3
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah
Understand that the imperative 'falyusalli rak'atayn' (then let him pray two rak'ats) indicates recommendation (nadb) in Hanafi usul, not obligation, due to the context and other evidences.
The command is interpreted as istihbab (recommendation) because the act is a means to request a need, not a required duty.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Observe that other sources mention different rak'ats: al-Hawi mentions twelve, al-Tajnis and others mention four after Isha. These represent variant narrations within the Hanafi tradition.
The existence of multiple narrations does not invalidate the two-rak'at version; they are considered legitimate but less authentic.
5
Determine the Tarjih
Recognize that the two-rak'at version from Tirmidhi is the mufta bihi (operative position) due to its authentic chain and stronger evidence, as upheld by Sharh Munyat al-Musalli and most fatwa collections.
The tarjih authority is the later Hanafi masters who prefer the sound hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن المندوبات صلاة الحاجة وهي ركعتان كما ذكره في شرح منية المصلي مع ما قبله من الاستخارة والأحاديث بها مذكورة في الترغيب والترهب. ذكرها في التجنيس والملتقط وخزانة الفتاوي وكثير من الفتاوي وفي الحاوي وشرح المنية. أما في الحاوي فذكر أنها ثنتا عشرة ركعة وبين كيفيتها بما فيه كلام، وأما في التجنيس وغيره فذكر أنها أربع ركعات بعد العشاء وأن في الحديث المرفوع يقرأ في الأولى فاتحة الكتاب مرة وثلاث مرات آية الكرسي وفي الثانية فاتحة الكتاب مرة وقل هو الله أحد مرة وقل أعوذ برب الفلق مرة وقل أعوذ برب الناس مرة وفي الثالثة والرابعة كذلك، ثم قال: كن له مثل أجر ليلة القدر. قال مشايخنا: صلينا هذه الصلاة فقضيت حوائجنا. وأما في شرح المنية فذكر أنها ركعتان وأخرج الترمذي عن عبد الله بن أبي أوفى قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من كانت له إلى الله حاجة أو إلى أحد من بني آدم فليتوضأ وليحسن الوضوء ثم ليصل ركعتين ثم ليثن على الله وليصل على النبي ثم ليقل لا إله إلا الله الحليم الكريم سبحان الله رب العرش العظيم الحمد لله رب العالمين أسألك رحمتك وعزائم مغفرتك والغنيمة من كل بر والسلامة من كل إثم لا تدع لي ذنبا إلا غفرته ولا هما إلا فرجته ولا حاجة هي لك رضا إلا قضيتها يا أرحم الراحمين.
Among the recommended acts is Salat al-Haja (Prayer of Need). It is two rak'ats as mentioned in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli along with what preceded of Istikhara, and the hadith about it are mentioned in al-Targhib wa al-Tarhib. It is mentioned in al-Tajnis, al-Multaqat, Khizanat al-Fatawa, many fatwa collections, al-Hawi, and Sharh al-Munya. In al-Hawi, it is mentioned as twelve rak'ats with a description that has some discussion. In al-Tajnis and others, it is mentioned as four rak'ats after Isha, and that in the marfu' hadith, one recites in the first rak'ah Fatiha once and Ayat al-Kursi three times, in the second rak'ah Fatiha once and Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad once, Qul A'udhu bi Rabbi al-Falaq once, and Qul A'udhu bi Rabbi al-Nas once, and similarly for the third and fourth. Then it says: 'They will have the equivalent of Laylat al-Qadr.' Our scholars said: We prayed this prayer and our needs were fulfilled. As for Sharh al-Munya, it mentions two rak'ats and cites the hadith of Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa (narrated by Tirmidhi): Whoever has a need from Allah or from any person should perform wudu well, then pray two rak'ats, then praise Allah and send blessings upon the Prophet, then say: 'La ilaha illallah al-Halim al-Karim, Subhan Allah Rabbi al-Arsh al-Azim, al-Hamdulillahi Rabb al-Alamin, I ask You for Your mercy and Your firm forgiveness, and the gain of every good, and safety from every sin. Do not leave any sin of mine except that You forgive it, nor any worry except that You relieve it, nor any need which pleases You except that You fulfill it, O Most Merciful of the merciful.'
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage discusses Salat al-Haja (Prayer of Need), a recommended prayer for fulfilling needs. The number of rak'ats varies in different sources: some say two rak'ats (based on a hadith from Tirmidhi), others say four rak'ats after Isha, and al-Hawi mentions twelve rak'ats. The Hanafi scholars mention that these different narrations allow for flexibility; the essential is to pray sincerely with the prescribed supplications. The most common and authentic is the two-rak'at version from Tirmidhi. The text also includes a report that scholars practiced it and found their needs fulfilled.

Key Terms
صلاة الحاجة (salat al-haja): A prayer performed to request the fulfillment of a specific need from Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith in Tirmidhi cited in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli, what should one do before praying Salat al-Haja?
A) Fast
B) Give charity
C) Perform wudu well
D) Read Quran

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds Salat al-Haja as recommended, with the two-rak'at version from Tirmidhi being the operative practice due to its authentic chain, while other narrations show flexibility.

Virtue and Hanafi Ruling on Night Prayer
Discusses the virtue of night prayer and the debate on its status (sunnah vs. nafl)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on night prayer (sunnah muakkadah) and cite the primary hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Night prayer is the best prayer after fard — strongly recommended, not obligatory.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the virtue of night prayer (salat al-layl) and the debate on its precise status — whether it is sunnah muakkadah or nafl. The text presents multiple hadiths that encourage it and notes a discussion in Fath al-Qadir on the classification of tahajjud. Understanding this ruling helps you appreciate its spiritual rank while avoiding the mistake of treating it as obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being discussed (night prayer / qiyam al-layl) and its initial classification as one of the 'mandubat' (recommended acts).
The passage opens with 'Among the recommended acts is night prayer.'
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the strongest hadith quoted: 'The best prayer after the obligatory is night prayer.' Note its sources (Muslim, Ibn Khuzaymah).
This hadith is the central proof for the virtue of night prayer.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Examine how the dalil proves a strong recommendation but not obligation. The word 'afdal' (better/best) indicates superiority, not compulsion.
In Hanafi usul, 'afdal' implies recommendation (mandub/sunnah), not wujub.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi debate
Recognize the hesitation in Fath al-Qadir about whether tahajjud is sunnah or merely nafl. Understand that this is a nuanced discussion among later Hanafi scholars.
The passage says: 'In Fath al-Qadir, there is hesitation... whether it is sunnah in our case or nafl.'
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
Despite the debate, the relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah and later fatwa) is that night prayer is sunnah muakkadah. Identify the authority (al-Marghinani, later works).
The hadith 'The best prayer after the fard is night prayer' firmly places it above other nafl prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن المندوبات صلاة الليل حثت السنة الشريفة عليها كثيراً وأفادت أن لفاعلها أجراً كبيراً فمنها ما في صحيح مسلم مرفوعاً أفضل الصيام بعد رمضان شهر الله المحرم، وأفضل الصلاة بعد الفريضة صلاة الليل. وروى ابن خزيمة مرفوعاً «عليكم بقيام الليل فإنه دأب الصالحين قبلكم وقربة إلى ربكم ومكفرة للسيئات ومنهاة عن الإثم». وروى الطبراني مرفوعاً «لا بد من صلاة بليل ولو حلب شاة وما كان بعد صلاة العشاء فهو من الليل». وقد تردد في فتح القدير في صلاة التهجد أهي سنة في حقنا أم تطوع وأطال الكلام على وجه التحقيق منه ما ذكره في أواخر شرح منية المصلي.
Among the recommended acts is night prayer (salat al-layl). The noble Sunnah has greatly encouraged it and indicated that the one who performs it has a great reward. Among that is what is in Sahih Muslim, raised: 'The best fasting after Ramadan is the month of Allah, al-Muharram, and the best prayer after the obligatory is night prayer.' Ibn Khuzaymah narrated, raised: 'Adhere to night prayer, for it is the practice of the righteous before you, a means of nearness to your Lord, an expiation of sins, and a prevention from sin.' Tabarani narrated, raised: 'There must be prayer at night, even if it is (the time of) milking a sheep; and whatever is after Isha prayer is from the night.' In Fath al-Qadir, there is hesitation regarding Tahajjud prayer: whether it is sunnah in our case or nafl (supererogatory), and he spoke at length about its verification, including what is mentioned in the end of Sharh Munyat al-Musalli.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage covers the recommendation and virtue of night prayer (qiyam al-layl/tahajjud). Multiple authentic hadiths extol its virtue: it is the best prayer after the obligatory, it is the practice of the righteous, it expiates sins. The text also notes a discussion from Fath al-Qadir about whether tahajjud is sunnah (established) or just nafl (voluntary) for us. This is a subtle intra-Hanafi discussion about the status; the stronger view is that it is sunnah muakkadah. The hadith 'There must be prayer at night' indicates its emphasis.

Key Terms
صلاة الليل (salat al-layl): Night prayer, including tahajjud, performed after Isha until Fajr.
التهجد (tahajjud): Specific name for night prayer performed after sleeping.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith in Muslim, what is the best prayer after the obligatory prayers?
A) Duha
B) Tahajjud
C) Night prayer (salat al-layl)
D) Istikhara

Key Takeaway
Night prayer is a highly recommended sunnah muakkadah, not obligatory, supported by authentic hadith.

Hukm Salat al-Hajah: A Recommended Prayer of Need
Classical Hanafi commentary on the prayer of need

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Salat al-Hajah in the Hanafi madhhab and identify the key proof (dalil) and its implications.

Core Idea
Salat al-Hajah is a recommended (mandub) prayer of two rak'at, supported by a hadith from Tirmidhi.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the status of Salat al-Hajah, addressing variations in the number of rak'at and affirming the two-rak'ah version as the preferred Hanafi view. The commentator presents evidence from multiple sources, then settles on the two-rak'at version based on a sound hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text explicitly calls Salat al-Hajah 'min al-mandubat' (from the recommended acts). Determine the hukm level: this is a sunnah ghayr muakkadah.
Mandub is synonymous with mustahabb and sunnah ghayr muakkadah in the Hanafi madhhab.
2
Note the intra-madhhab variation
The commentator reports different numbers of rak'at from various sources: twelve (al-Hawi), four (al-Tajnis), and two (Sharh al-Munyah). Recognize that this is a valid difference within the Hanafi school.
The existence of multiple narrations does not invalidate any; the mufta bihi is the well-authenticated version.
3
Examine the primary dalil
The text quotes a marfu' hadith from Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa via Tirmidhi. Identify the proof type: ahad hadith, zanni al-thubut but qati' al-dalalah in indicating recommendation.
The imperative 'فليصل' is understood as recommendation (nadb) due to the context of du'a and absence of qarinah for wujub.
4
Extract the mufta bihi ruling
Despite variations, the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is two rak'at with the specific supplication. This is based on the strength of the Tirmidhi hadith and the tarjih of later Hanafi authorities.
The commentator does not explicitly say 'wa bihi na'khudh', but the structure of argumentation gives preference to the two-rak'at version.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسمي به . قال : حاجته. رواه البخاري وغيره. ومن المندوبات صلاة الحاجة وهي ركعتان كما ذكره في شرح منية المصلي مع ما قبله من الاستخارة والأحاديث بها مذكورة في الترغيب والترهب. ومن المندوبات صلاة الليل حثت السنة الشريفة عليها كثيراً وأفادت أن لفاعلها أجراً كبيراً فمنها ما في صحيح مسلم مرفوعاً أفضل الصيام بعد رمضان شهر الله المحرم، وأفضل الصلاة بعد الفريضة صلاة الليل وروى ابن خزيمة مرفوعاً «عليكم بقيام الليل فإنه دأب الصالحين قبلكم وقربة إلى ربكم ومكفرة للسيئات ومنهاة عن الإثم» وروى الطبراني مرفوعاً لا بد من صلاة بليل ولو حلب شاة وما كان بعد صلاة العشاء فهو من الليل كما هو دأبه وأوسع المسموع من المشايخ ينبغي أن ينام على الطهارة مستقبل القبلة بعد قراءة الدعاء المذكور فإن رأى في منامه بياضاً أو خضرة فذلك الأمر خير، وإن رأى فيه سواداً أو حمرة فهو شر ينبغي أن يجتنب عنه ا هـ قوله : (ومن المندوبات صلاة الحاجة الخ) قال الشيخ إسماعيل : ذكرها في التجنيس والملتقط وخزانة الفتاوي وكثير من الفتاوي وفي الحاوي وشرح المنية. أما في الحاوي فذكر أنها ثنتا عشرة ركعة وبين كيفيتها بما فيه كلام، وأما في التجنيس وغيره فذكر أنها أربع ركعات بعد العشاء وأن في الحديث المرفوع يقرأ في الأولى فاتحة الكتاب مرة وثلاث مرات آية الكرسي وفي الثانية فاتحة الكتاب مرة «وقل هو الله أحد» مرة «وقل أعوذ برب الفلق» مرة و قل أعوذ برب الناس مرة وفي الثالثة والرابعة كذلك، كن له مثلهن من ليلة القدر. قال مشايخنا: صلينا هذه الصلاة فقضيت حوائجنا مذكور في الملتقط والتجنيس وكثير من الفتاوى كذا في الفتاوى كذا في خزانة الفتاوي. وأما في شرح المنية فذكر أنها ركعتان وأخرج الترمذي عن الله بن أبي أوفى قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من كانت له إلى الله حاجة أو إلى أحد من بني آدم فليتوضأ وليحسن الوضوء ثم ليصل ركعتين ثم ليثن على الله تعالى وليصل على النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم ثم ليقل لا إله إلا الله الحليم الكريم سبحان الله رب العرش العظيم الحمد لله رب العالمين، أسألك رحمتك وعزائم مغفرتك والغنيمة من كل بر والسلامة من كل إثم لا تدع لي ذنباً إلا غفرته، ولا هماً إلا فرجته، ولا حاجة هي لك رضا إلا قضيتها يا أرحم الراحمين ا هـ .
And he names it? He said: his need. Al-Bukhari and others narrated it. Among the recommended acts is Salat al-Hajah, and it is two rak'at as mentioned in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli along with what preceded it of Istikhara, and the hadiths about it are mentioned in al-Targhib wa al-Tarhib. Among the recommended acts is Salat al-Layl; the noble Sunnah strongly encouraged it and indicated that its performer has a great reward. Among them is what is in Sahih Muslim raised: 'The best fasting after Ramadan is the month of Allah, al-Muharram, and the best prayer after the obligatory prayer is the night prayer.' And Ibn Khuzaymah narrated raised: 'Upon you is Qiyam al-Layl, for it is the practice of the righteous before you, a means of nearness to your Lord, an expiation of sins, and a restrainer from sin.' And al-Tabarani narrated raised: 'There must be prayer at night, even if only the milking of a goat, and what is after Isha prayer is part of night prayer as is his [the Prophet's] practice.' And the broadest heard from the scholars is that one should sleep in a state of purity facing the Qibla after reciting the mentioned supplication. If he sees in his dream whiteness or greenness, that matter is good; if he sees blackness or redness, it is evil and he should avoid it. End. His statement: 'Among the recommended acts is Salat al-Hajah etc.'—Shaykh Ismail said: It is mentioned in al-Tajnis, al-Multaqat, Khazanat al-Fatawa, many fatawa works, al-Hawi, and Sharh al-Munyah. In al-Hawi, it is mentioned that it is twelve rak'at, and he explained its manner with something to be questioned. In al-Tajnis and others, it is mentioned that it is four rak'at after Isha, and in the marfu' hadith one recites in the first rak'ah al-Fatiha once and Ayat al-Kursi three times; in the second rak'ah al-Fatiha once, Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad once, Qul A'udhu bi Rabbi al-Falaq once, and Qul A'udhu bi Rabbi al-Nas once; and likewise in the third and fourth; 'they will have the like of them from Laylat al-Qadr.' Our mashayikh said: We prayed this prayer and our needs were fulfilled—mentioned in al-Multaqat, al-Tajnis, and many fatawa works, similarly in al-Fatawa, similarly in Khazanat al-Fatawa. As for Sharh al-Munyah, it mentioned that it is two rak'at, and al-Tirmidhi narrated from 'Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa that the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) said: 'Whoever has a need from Allah or from any of the children of Adam, let him perform wudu well, then pray two rak'at, then praise Allah and send blessings upon the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him), then say: La ilaha illa Allah al-Halim al-Karim, Subhan Allah Rabbi al-'Arsh al-'Azim, al-Hamdu lillahi Rabb al-'Alamin. I ask You for Your mercy and decisive forgiveness, the gain from every good, and safety from every sin. Do not leave any sin for me without forgiving it, nor any worry without relieving it, nor any need that is pleasing to You without fulfilling it, O Most Merciful of the merciful.' End.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the recommended prayer of need (Salat al-Hajah). It begins by stating that among the recommended acts is this prayer, which is two rak'at, as mentioned in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli alongside the earlier discussion of Istikhara. The author then quotes hadiths on the virtue of night prayer, which are relevant as context. The commentator, Shaykh Ismail, then reports that the prayer of need is mentioned in multiple sources, but there is a difference in the number of rak'at: in al-Hawi it is twelve, in al-Tajnis and others it is four after Isha with specific recitations, and in Sharh al-Munyah it is two. A hadith from al-Tirmidhi is then quoted, detailing the procedure: wudu, two rak'at, praise, blessings, and a specific supplication. The Hanafi position considers this prayer recommended (mandub), and the various narrations show scholarly flexibility. The text also includes a footnote reference to the hadith's source. The overall ruling is that Salat al-Hajah is a sunnah prayer, and the Hanafi madhhab accepts the two-rak'at version as authentic, though other numbers are also mentioned from other sources.

Key Terms
مندوبات (mandubat): Recommended acts that are not obligatory; synonymous with sunnah ghayr muakkadah in this context.
صلاة الحاجة (Salat al-Hajah): A voluntary prayer performed to request the fulfillment of a need from Allah, consisting of two rak'at with specific supplication.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the number of rak'at for Salat al-Hajah as preferred in the Hanafi madhhab?
A) Twelve rak'at
B) Four rak'at
C) Two rak'at
D) Three rak'at

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Hajah, as a recommended (mandub) prayer, is two rak'at in the Hanafi madhhab, supported by a sound hadith, and other reported numbers are not the operative ruling.

intermediate

Legal Nature of Salat al-Layl (Night Prayer)
Ruling with proof on the nature of night prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the nature of night prayer for the community and explain the evidence from abrogation.

Core Idea
Night prayer for us is mandub because the Prophet's obligation was abrogated.

Night prayer (Salat al-Layl) is a highly virtuous act, but what is its exact legal status for the Muslim community? Scholars have differed: is it a sunnah (emphasized) or merely recommended? In this passage, the commentator draws on a key distinction between the Prophet's duty and our own, resolving the matter through the principle of abrogation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal question
The passage begins with a hesitation from Fath al-Qadir: whether night prayer for us is sunnah or mustahabb depends on its nature for the Prophet (ﷺ). If it was obligatory for him, it is mandub for us; if it was voluntary for him, it is sunnah for us.
2
Examine the two possibilities
If the Prophet's night prayer was fard (obligatory) on him, then for us it is only mandub, because verbal evidences (adillah qawliyyah) indicate recommendation, and his continuous practice (muwazabah) does not transfer obligation to us. If it was voluntary (tatawwu') for him, then it would be sunnah for us.
The key is the nature of the Prophet's act: fard or nafl.
3
Apply the evidence of abrogation
The passage concludes that the obligatory nature was abrogated (mansukhah), citing the hadith of A'isha (RA) narrated by Muslim, Abu Dawud, and al-Nasa'i. Thus, for us, night prayer is not obligatory; it is mandub (recommended).
The abrogation is key to the Hanafi position.
4
State the Hanafi ruling
Night prayer is mandub (sunnah ghayr muakkadah) for the community. It is not wajib or sunnah muakkadah. One may perform it or leave it without sin, but it carries great reward.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وقد تردد في فتح القدير الخ) حيث قال : بقي أن صفة صلاة الليل في حقنا السنة أو الاستحباب يتوقف على صفتها في حقه صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم، فإن كانت فرضاً في حقه فهي مندوبة في حقنا لأن الأدلة القولية فيها إنما تفيد الندب والمواظبة الفعلية ليست على تطوع لتكون سنة في حقنا، وإن كانت تطوعاً فسنة لنا. وقد اختلف العلماء في ذلك ثم ذكر الأدلة للفريقين والذي حط عليه كلامه أن الفرضية منسوخة كما قالته عائشة رضي الله تعالى عنها في حديث رواه مسلم وأبو داود والنسائي قوله : (ومن هنا يعلم الخ) قال الشيخ إسماعيل : وقد ذكر الغزنوي صلاة الرغائب ثنتي عشرة ركعة بين العشاءين بست تسليمات، وصلاة الاستفتاح عشرين ركعة في النصف من رجب وصلاة ليلة النصف من شعبان مائة ركعة بخمسين تسليمة، وينبغي حمله على الانفراد كما مر وصلاة ليلة النصف ذكرها الغافقي المحدث في لمحات الأنوار وصاحب أنس المنقطعين وأبو طالب المكي في القوت عبدالعزيز الديريني في طهارة القلوب، وابن الجوزي في كتاب النور والغزالي في الإحياء. وقال الحافظ الطبري : جرت العادة في كل قطر من أقطار المكلفين بتطابق الكافة على صلاة مائة ركعة في ليلة النصف من شعبان بألف قل هو الله أحد، وتروى في صحتها آثار وأخبار ليس عليها الاعتماد ولا نقول إنها موضوعة كما قال الحافظ ابن الجوزي فإن الحكم بالوضع أمره خطير وشأنه كبير مع أنها أخبار ترغيب والعامل عليها بنيته يثاب ويصدق عزمه وإخلاصه في ابتهاله يجاب والأولى تلقيها بالقبول من غير حكم بصحتها ولا
His statement: 'And he hesitated in Fath al-Qadir etc.' where he said: It remains that the nature of night prayer in our case being sunnah or mustahabb depends on its nature in his (the Prophet's) case. If it was obligatory for him, then it is recommended (mandub) for us because the verbal evidences only indicate recommendation, and the actual continuous practice is not for supererogatory acts to become sunnah for us. But if it was voluntary for him, then it is sunnah for us. Scholars have differed on this, then he mentioned the proofs for the two groups, and the conclusion of his statement is that the obligation is abrogated, as A'isha (may Allah be pleased with her) said in a hadith narrated by Muslim, Abu Dawud, and al-Nasa'i. His statement: 'From here it is known etc.' — Shaykh Ismail said: Al-Ghaznawi mentioned the prayer of al-Ragha'ib: twelve rak'at between Maghrib and Isha with six taslims, and the prayer of al-Iftitah: twenty rak'at in mid-Rajab, and the prayer of mid-Sha'ban: one hundred rak'at with fifty taslims, and it should be taken as performed individually as previously mentioned. The prayer of mid-Sha'ban was mentioned by al-Ghafiqi, the muhaddith, in Lamahat al-Anwar, the author of Uns al-Munqati'in, Abu Talib al-Makki in al-Qut, 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Dayrini in Taharat al-Qulub, Ibn al-Jawzi in Kitab al-Nur, and al-Ghazali in al-Ihya'. Al-Hafiz al-Tabari said: The common practice in every region of the responsible people is unanimous agreement on praying one hundred rak'at on the night of mid-Sha'ban with one thousand 'Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad' [sura al-Ikhlas]. Reports and traditions are narrated about its validity, but they are not relied upon, nor do we say they are fabricated as al-Hafiz Ibn al-Jawzi said, because judging fabrication is a serious matter with great consequence, especially since these are traditions of encouragement (targhib), and one who acts upon them with his intention will be rewarded and his resolve and sincerity in his supplication will be answered. It is better to accept them without judging them authentic or fabricated, and
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on two issues: first, the nature of night prayer (Salat al-Layl) for the Muslim community—whether it is sunnah or mustahabb—and second, the ruling on reviving specific nights with congregational prayers, particularly Salat al-Ragha'ib and the prayer of mid-Sha'ban. The author begins by citing a hesitation from Fath al-Qadir about whether the Prophet's night prayer was obligatory for him or voluntary, and thus whether for us it is recommended or sunnah. The conclusion is that the obligatory nature was abrogated (based on hadith from A'isha), so for us it is mandub (recommended). Then the text moves to the practice of praying on specific nights. The commentator, Shaykh Ismail, mentions that al-Ghaznawi described prayers for Rajab (al-Ragha'ib and al-Iftitah) and mid-Sha'ban (one hundred rak'at). The text notes that these prayers should be performed individually, not congregationally. A quote from al-Hafiz al-Tabari states that the practice of one hundred rak'at on mid-Sha'ban with recitation of al-Ikhlas is widespread, and although the hadiths about it are not strictly authentic, they are traditions of encouragement (targhib). The author advises accepting them without judging authenticity or fabrication, and one who acts upon them with sincere intention will be rewarded. The Hanafi ruling is that congregational prayers for these occasions are disliked (makruh), as per the earlier passage about إحياء الليالي, and that is reaffirmed here.

Key Terms
صلاة الليل (Salat al-Layl): Night prayer; voluntary prayers performed during the night, especially after Isha.
نسخ (Naskh): Abrogation; the removal of a previously established ruling by a later revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for the Hanafi ruling that night prayer is mandub (recommended) rather than sunnah muakkadah?
A) The Prophet never prayed at night.
B) The obligation was abrogated based on the hadith of A'isha.
C) The verbal evidences indicate obligation.
D) The community cannot perform the same prayers as the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
Night prayer is mandub for the community because the Prophet's obligation was abrogated; it is not a sunnah muakkadah.

Ruling on Reviving Specific Nights (Salat al-Ragha'ib and Mid-Sha'ban)
Ruling on reviving specific nights with individual prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi ruling that specific night prayers like Salat al-Ragha'ib and mid-Sha'ban should be performed individually, not congregationally, and explain the basis for accepting targhib traditions.

Core Idea
Congregational prayer on specific nights is makruh; individual prayer with sincere intention is rewarded.

Many Muslims eagerly revive blessed nights like mid-Sha'ban and the first Friday of Rajab with special prayers. But how should these be performed? The commentator, drawing from earlier Hanafi rulings, clarifies that such prayers should be done individually to avoid innovation, while still acknowledging the virtue of the acts based on traditions of encouragement (targhib).

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prayers mentioned
The passage lists: (1) Salat al-Ragha'ib: 12 rak'at between Maghrib and Isha with 6 taslims; (2) Salat al-Iftitah: 20 rak'at in mid-Rajab; (3) Prayer of mid-Sha'ban: 100 rak'at with 50 taslims, reciting Surah al-Ikhlas 1000 times.
These are specific practices mentioned by al-Ghaznawi and others.
2
Note the condition: individual performance
Shaykh Ismail states: 'And it should be taken as performed individually as previously mentioned' (ينبغي حمله على الانفراد كما مر). This refers to the earlier ruling that congregating for these nights is makruh.
Congregational gathering for these prayers is not allowed.
3
Examine the authority of the traditions
The passage cites al-Hafiz al-Tabari: the common practice (jarat al-'adah) is to pray 100 rak'at on mid-Sha'ban with 1000 Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad. Reports about its virtue are not fully authentic (laysa 'alayha al-i'timad), but they are traditions of encouragement (akhbar targhib). The commentator advises accepting them without judging authenticity or fabrication, because acting on them with sincere intention brings reward.
The Hanafi approach: for fada'il al-a'mal, weak hadith can be acted upon.
4
State the Hanafi ruling
Performing these prayers individually is mustahabb (recommended) based on targhib traditions. Congregational performance is makruh. One should not reject these practices entirely nor insist on their authenticity; rather, accept them with good intention.
This balances avoiding bid'ah (innovation) with encouraging virtue.

Maximum Rak'at in Voluntary Prayers: Daytime and Nighttime Limits
Ruling on the maximum number of rak'at in voluntary prayers by day and night

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the maximum number of rak'at for nafl prayers with one taslim and explain the evidence (qiyas and nass).

Core Idea
Voluntary prayers follow obligatory ones: daytime limit four, nighttime eight, but nass allows nighttime expansion.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the Hanafi position on how many rak'at can be prayed in voluntary (nafl) prayers with a single taslim. The author first states the ruling: it is disliked to exceed four by day and eight by night. Then he explains the underlying logic: voluntary prayers are followers (tawābi‘) of obligatory prayers, so they should not contradict them in number. However, for the night prayer, a textual exception allows up to eight rak'at, based on the Prophet’s practice. An intra-madhhab difference is noted: Imam al-Sarakhsi saw no dislike for exceeding eight at night.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
Recognize that the Hanafi school considers voluntary prayers as followers (tawābi‘) of obligatory prayers (fara'id). This principle drives the default limit.
The principle is stated in the text: 'النوافل شرعت توابع للفرائض'.
2
Apply qiyas to daytime
By analogy with obligatory prayers (e.g., Zuhr has four rak'at), the daytime voluntary prayer should not exceed four rak'at with one taslim.
Daytime obligatory prayers are four rak'at (Zuhr, Asr, 'Isha). This qiyas is strong.
3
Identify the nass exception for night
The text cites narrations that the Prophet prayed up to thirteen rak'at at night. After subtracting witr and Fajr sunnah, the remaining voluntary rak'at are up to eight, which is allowed without dislike.
This exception is based on ahadith, which are zanni al-thubut but qati' al-dalala in this context.
4
Note the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Scholars differed on exceeding eight at night. Imam al-Sarakhsi held no dislike, reasoning it is simply connecting acts of worship. The text says his view is 'with verification' (مع التصحيح).
This ikhtilaf shows that within Hanafi school, there is a valid alternative opinion.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that exceeding four by day and eight by night is makruh tahrimi, but al-Sarakhsi's view is also recognized, especially for those following his tarjih.
In practice, many Hanafis avoid exceeding these limits to avoid dislikedness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وكره الزيادة على أربع في نفل النهار وعلى ثمان (ليلاً) أي بتسليمة والأصل فيه أن النوافل شرعت توابع للفرائض والتبع لا يخالف الأصل فلو زيدت على الأربع في النهاية لخالفت الفرائض، وهذا هو القياس في الليل إلا أن الزيادة على الأربع إلى الثماني عرفناه بالنص وهو ما روي عن النبي الله أنه كان يصلي بالليل خمس ركعات، سبع ركعات، تسع رکعات إحدى عشرة ركعة ثلاث عشرة ركعة والثلاث من كل واحد من هذه الأعداد الوتر وركعتان سنة الفجر فيبقى ركعتان وأربع وست وثمان فيجوز إلى هذا القدر بتسليمة واحدة من غير كراهة واختلف المشايخ في الزيادة على الثماني بتسليمة واحدة . اختلاف مع التصحيح فصحح الإمام السرخسي عدم الكراهة معللاً بأن فيه وصل العبادة بالعبادة وهو
His statement: 'And it is disliked to increase beyond four in daytime voluntary prayer and beyond eight at night (i.e., with one taslim). The basis for this is that voluntary prayers were legislated as followers of obligatory prayers, and the follower does not oppose the original. So if one increased beyond four, it would oppose the obligatory prayers. This is the analogy (qiyas) for night, except that the increase from four to eight is known to us by text (nass): what is narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he used to pray at night five, seven, nine, eleven, or thirteen rak'at, and the three from each of these numbers are witr, and two rak'at are sunnah of Fajr, leaving two, four, six, and eight. So it is permissible up to this amount with one taslim without dislike. The mashayikh differed regarding increasing beyond eight with one taslim. There is a difference with verification: Imam al-Sarakhsi ruled no dislike, reasoning that it is connecting worship to worship, and
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage explains the Hanafi ruling on the maximum number of rak'at for voluntary prayers (nafl) with a single taslim (one set of salutations). The ruling: it is makruh (disliked) to exceed four rak'at in daytime nafl and eight at night with one taslim. The reasoning is based on qiyas (analogy) with obligatory prayers, which have a maximum of four rak'at (except Friday, etc.). Since night prayers have textual evidence (nass) from the Prophet's practice of praying up to thirteen rak'at, the allowance is extended to eight rak'at with one taslim. Beyond eight, there is a difference among Hanafi scholars: Imam al-Sarakhsi held no dislike, reasoning that it is simply connecting acts of worship. The text notes that the mashayikh differed but al-Sarakhsi's view is related as 'with verification' (مع التصحيح). The passage is cut off, but the general Hanafi ruling is that one should not exceed eight rak'at at night with one taslim to avoid dislikedness, though there is a view allowing more. The daytime limit of four is stricter due to stronger qiyas. The key point is that the maximum for voluntary prayers is set in analogy to the obligatory, with nighttime exceptions from the Sunnah.

Key Terms
نفل النهار (nafl al-nahar): Voluntary prayers performed during the daytime (after sunrise until before Maghrib).
تسليمة (taslimah): One set of salutations (saying 'Assalamu alaykum') ending a prayer; 'with one taslim' means one salutation at the end of a sequence of rak'at.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what is the maximum number of rak'at that can be prayed with one taslim in daytime voluntary prayer without dislike?
A) Two rak'at
B) Four rak'at
C) Six rak'at
D) Eight rak'at

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, daytime voluntary prayers should not exceed four rak'at with one taslim, and nighttime prayers eight; beyond eight there is a valid difference of opinion.
