Maximum Rak'ahs in Nafl Prayers: Day and Night
Stating the ruling and evidence for nafl rak'ah limits with intra-school dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on maximum rak'ahs for daytime and nighttime nafl prayers with one taslimah, explain the analogy and hadith evidence, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute about exceeding eight at night.

Core Idea
Daytime nafl is capped at 4 rak'ahs; nighttime at 8 with one taslimah, based on analogy and prophetic practice.

The passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains why the Hanafi school restricts supererogatory prayers (nafl) to four rak'ahs by day and eight by night with a single taslimah. It grounds the ruling in the principle that voluntary acts follow obligatory ones, then carves out an exception for night based on the Prophet's ﷺ practice. The text also introduces an internal disagreement among later Hanafi scholars about exceeding the nighttime limit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its limits
Note the explicit statement: daytime nafl is capped at four rak'ahs, nighttime at eight, with one taslimah. The core ruling is that exceeding these amounts is disliked (makruh).
The term 'بتسليمة' means all rak'ahs are connected with a single final salutation.
2
Understand the analogy (qiyas)
The author explains that nafl prayers are subordinate to fard prayers. Since obligatory prayers do not exceed four rak'ahs in one sequence (except for four-rak'ah fard which are separated by tashahhud), daytime nafl should not exceed four. The same logic applies to night, but an exception is made.
This analogy is the default rule; the exception for night is based on specific evidence.
3
Examine the hadith evidence for the night exception
The passage cites the Prophet's ﷺ practice of praying various odd numbers at night (5, 7, 9, 11, 13 rak'ahs). After subtracting witr and the sunnah of Fajr, the remaining rak'ahs (2, 4, 6, 8) show that up to eight rak'ahs per taslimah are permissible without dislike.
The hadith is from Sahih Muslim, Sunan Abi Dawud, and Sunan al-Nasa'i.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
The text mentions that scholars differed about increasing beyond eight at night. Imam al-Sarakhsi held no dislike (no karahah), while the majority (including the author's view) considered it disliked. The passage does not give a final tarjih.
Dispute is within the Hanafi school, not with other madhahib.
5
Synthesize the evidentiary structure
The ruling combines analogy (qiyas) for the daytime limit and a prophetic exception (text) for the nighttime up to eight. For exceeding eight at night, the evidence is inconclusive, leading to ikhtilaf.
The dalil for the night exception is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalalah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وكره الزيادة على أربع في نفل النهار وعلى ثمان (ليلاً) أي بتسليمة والأصل فيه أن النوافل شرعت توابع للفرائض والتبع لا يخالف الأصل فلو زيدت على الأربع في النهاية لخالفت الفرائض، وهذا هو القياس في الليل إلا أن الزيادة على الأربع إلى الثماني عرفناه بالنص وهو ما روي عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه كان يصلي بالليل خمس ركعات، سبع ركعات، تسع ركعات إحدى عشرة ركعة ثلاث عشرة ركعة والثلاث من كل واحد من هذه الأعداد الوتر وركعتان سنة الفجر فيبقى ركعتان وأربع وست وثمان فيجوز إلى هذا القدر بتسليمة واحدة من غير كراهة واختلف المشايخ في الزيادة على الثماني بتسليمة واحدة . اختلاف مع التصحيح فصحح الإمام السرخسي عدم الكراهة معللاً بأن فيه وصل العبادة بالعبادة وهو والمواظبة الفعلية ليست على تطوع لتكون سنة في حقنا، وإن كانت تطوعاً فسنة لنا. وقد اختلف العلماء في ذلك ثم ذكر الأدلة للفريقين والذي حط عليه كلامه أن الفرضية منسوخة كما قالته عائشة رضي الله تعالى عنها في حديث رواه مسلم وأبو داود والنسائي
His statement: (And it is disliked to increase beyond four in supererogatory prayers of the day and beyond eight at night) i.e., with one taslimah. The basis is that voluntary prayers were legislated as followers of the obligatory prayers, and a follower does not oppose the original. So if one increased beyond four in the day, it would oppose the obligatory prayers, and this is the analogy at night as well. However, the increase from four to eight we know by text, which is what was narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he used to pray at night five rak'ahs, seven rak'ahs, nine rak'ahs, eleven rak'ahs, thirteen rak'ahs. The three in each of these numbers is the witr, and two rak'ahs are the sunnah of Fajr, leaving two, four, six, and eight. So it is permissible up to this amount with one taslimah without dislike. The scholars differed regarding the increase beyond eight with one taslimah. They differed with verification. Imam al-Sarakhsi corrected the absence of dislike, justifying that it is connecting worship to worship, and the actual consistent practice is not a voluntary act so as to be a sunnah for us, even if it is voluntary, it is a sunnah for us. The scholars differed in that, then he mentioned the proofs for both groups. The crux of his statement is that the obligation is abrogated, as 'A'ishah (may Allah be pleased with her) said in a hadith narrated by Muslim, Abu Dawud, and al-Nasa'i.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This is a ruling passage from the sharh of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The author explains the meaning of the matn's statement about disliked increases in supererogatory prayers. By day, the maximum is four rak'ahs with one taslimah; by night, it is eight, based on the analogy that voluntary prayers should follow the pattern of obligatory ones. The exception for night up to eight is proven by hadith evidence of the Prophet's practice. The passage then introduces an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam al-Sarakhsi holds that increasing beyond eight at night is not disliked, while others consider it disliked. The author presents the evidence but does not give a final tarjih here. The hadith of 'A'ishah is referenced as proof for the permissibility or abrogation of an earlier obligation.

Key Terms
نفل النهار (nafl al-nahar): Supererogatory prayers performed during the daytime.
بتسليمة (bi taslimah): With one salutation; meaning all rak'ahs are performed consecutively with a single final taslim.
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed at night, included in the counted rak'ahs.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school restricts daytime nafl to four rak'ahs per taslimah and nighttime nafl to eight, with a minority view allowing more at night.

Congregational Prayers on Virtuous Nights: The Hanafi Ruling
Stating that gathering in congregation for specified prayers on blessed nights is disliked and considered innovation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that congregational performance of specified night prayers (Salat al-Ragha'ib, mid-Sha'ban) is makruh tahrimi and bid'ah, and differentiate between individual and congregational performance.

Core Idea
Congregational prayer on Ragha'ib and mid-Sha'ban nights is bid'ah; perform these nafl prayers individually.

While many Muslims pray extra rak'ahs on blessed nights like the first Friday of Rajab or mid-Sha'ban, the Hanafi school views organizing these in congregation as a disliked innovation. The source passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that such prayers should be performed individually (infirad), not as a congregation. It also addresses the authenticity of the reports recommending these prayers, advising acceptance for motivational purposes without declaring them fabricated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Prayers
Locate the three specific prayers mentioned: Salat al-Ragha'ib (12 rak'ahs), Salat al-Istiftah (20 rak'ahs), and the prayer of mid-Sha'ban (100 rak'ahs). Note the taslim counts.
These are nafl prayers with specific numbers.
2
Determine the Ruling on Congregation
The text states 'ينبغي حمله على الانفراد' meaning they should be performed individually. The author earlier established the dislike (كراهة) of congregational gatherings for such prayers.
Congregation in this context means organized group prayer.
3
Understand the Basis
The ruling derives from the principle that acts of worship not established in the Sunnah should not be performed in a manner resembling obligatory or sunnah prayers in congregation. These prayers are later practices, so congregation is bid'ah.
The school distinguishes between the prayer itself (permissible) and the method (disliked).
4
Assess Authenticity Considerations
The passage discusses hadith authenticity: reports exist but are not reliable. However, declaring them fabricated is too harsh. The recommended approach is to accept them as motivational, without ruling on authenticity, and to act on them individually.
This nuance avoids both strict rejection and full endorsement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومن هنا يعلم الخ) قال الشيخ إسماعيل : وقد ذكر الغزنوي صلاة الرغائب ثنتي عشرة ركعة بين العشاءين بست تسليمات، وصلاة الاستفتاح عشرين ركعة في النصف من رجب وصلاة ليلة النصف من شعبان مائة ركعة بخمسين تسليمة، وينبغي حمله على الانفراد كما مر وصلاة ليلة النصف ذكرها الغافقي المحدث في لمحات الأنوار وصاحب أنس المنقطعين وأبو طالب المكي في القوت عبدالعزيز الديريني في طهارة القلوب، وابن الجوزي في كتاب النور والغزالي في الإحياء. وقال الحافظ الطبري : جرت العادة في كل قطر من أقطار المكلفين بتطابق الكافة على صلاة مائة ركعة في ليلة النصف من شعبان بألف قل . هو الله أحد، وتروى في صحتها آثار وأخبار ليس عليها الاعتماد ولا نقول إنها موضوعة كما قال الحافظ ابن الجوزي فإن الحكم بالوضع أمره خطير وشأنه كبير مع أنها أخبار ترغيب والعامل عليها بنيته يثاب ويصدق عزمه وإخلاصه في ابتهاله يجاب والأولى تلقيها بالقبول من غير حكم بصحتها ولا في حرج في العمل بها ا.هـ.
His statement: (From here it is known...). Sheikh Isma'il said: Al-Ghaznawi mentioned the Salat al-Ragha'ib as twelve rak'ahs between the two evening prayers with six taslims, and the prayer of opening as twenty rak'ahs in the middle of Rajab, and the prayer of the night of mid-Sha'ban as one hundred rak'ahs with fifty taslims. It should be performed individually as mentioned. The prayer of the night of mid-Sha'ban was mentioned by al-Ghafiqi the muhaddith in Lamahat al-Anwar, and the author of Uns al-Munqati'in, and Abu Talib al-Makki in al-Qut, and Abd al-Aziz al-Dayrini in Taharat al-Qulub, and Ibn al-Jawzi in Kitab al-Nur, and al-Ghazali in al-Ihya'. Al-Hafiz al-Tabari said: The custom in all the climes of the obligated people is that everyone agrees on praying one hundred rak'ahs on the night of mid-Sha'ban with one thousand 'Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad'. Reports about its authenticity are narrated, but not relied upon. We do not say they are fabricated as al-Hafiz Ibn al-Jawzi said, for declaring something fabricated is a serious matter. These are motivational reports, and the one who acts on them with sincerity will be rewarded and his determination and sincerity in supplication will be answered. It is better to accept them without ruling on their authenticity or finding difficulty in acting upon them.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage clarifies the ruling on specific supererogatory prayers associated with virtuous nights. The author, citing Sheikh Isma'il, mentions various prayers reported in later works: Salat al-Ragha'ib on the first Friday night of Rajab, Salat al-Istiftah on the 15th of Rajab, and the prayer of mid-Sha'ban (100 rak'ahs). The ruling is that these should be performed individually, not in congregation (الانفراد). The passage then discusses the authenticity of these practices, noting that the reports are not reliable but also not fabricated. The preferred approach is to accept them without judgment, as they are motivational. The overall principle is that organizing congregational gatherings for these prayers is disliked (makruh) and considered an innovation (bid'ah), as stated earlier in the text.

Key Terms
صلاة الرغائب (Salat al-Ragha'ib): A specific prayer performed on the first Friday night of Rajab, consisting of 12 rak'ahs with 6 taslims.
الانفراد (al-infirad): Performing a prayer individually, not in congregation.
بدعة (bid'ah): An innovation in religious practice that was not part of the original Sunnah.

Key Takeaway

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Increasing Nafl Rak'ahs at Night
Continuing the intra-Hanafi dispute on increasing nafl at night beyond eight rak'ahs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority position on increasing nafl at night beyond eight rak'ahs with one taslimah and evaluate the evidence from the hadith of Aisha.

Core Idea
The Hanafi majority holds that increasing beyond eight rak'ahs with one taslimah is makruh tahrimi; the hadith of nine rak'ahs is interpreted as including obligatory prayers.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether one may pray more than eight rak'ahs at night with a single taslimah. The majority, including Abu Hanifa and his two students, consider it makruh tahrimi, while Imam al-Sarakhsi and the author of al-Khulasa argue it is permissible based on a hadith from Aisha. You will learn how the Hanafi response refutes that proof by showing the hadith is ambiguous and contradicted by more explicit reports.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi majority position
Identify the ruling according to Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani as presented in the passage.
Look for the phrase 'مكروهة بالإجماع' in the text.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
Find the position of Imam al-Sarakhsi and the author of al-Khulasa, and note the hadith they cite from Sahih Muslim.
The hadith mentions nine rak'ahs with one taslimah.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response to the opposing proof
Understand how al-Tahawi and Ghayat al-Bayan respond to the hadith, arguing that it is ambiguous and can be interpreted as including obligatory prayers.
Note the reference to the al-Zuhri narration clarifying the Prophet's practice.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical difference: one view allows the act, the other considers it makruh tahrimi.
5
Conclude with the tarjih
Identify which position is stronger and why, based on consensus and clearer textual evidence.
The passage states: 'وبه يضعف قول السرخسي' and 'وهو أصح القولين'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أفضل. ورده في البدائع بأنه يشكل بالزيادة على الأربع في النهار قال: والصحيح أنه يكره لأنه لم يرو عن النبي انتهى . وفي منية المصلي أن الزيادة المذكورة مكروهة بالإجماع أي بإجماع أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه وبه يضعف قول السرخسي، وصحح في الخلاصة ما ذهب إليه السرخسي ويشهد له ما في صحيح مسلم عن عائشة رضي الله عنها في حديث طويل إنه كان يصلي تسع ركعات لا يجلس فيهن إلا في الثامنة فيذكر الله تعالى ويحمده ويدعوه، ثم ينهض ولا يسلم فيصلي التاسعة ثم يقعد فيذكر الله تعالى ويحمده ويدعوه ثم يسلم تسليماً يسمعنا» إلا أن هذا يقتضي عدم جواز القعود فيها أصلاً إلا بعد الثامنة وجواز التنفل بالوتر من الركعات وكلمتهم على وجوب القعدة على رأس الركعتين من النفل مطلقاً، وإنما الخلاف الفساد بتركها وعلى كراهة التنفل بالوتر من الركعات ومن العجب ما ذكره الطحاوي من رده استدلالهم على إباحة الثماني بتسليمة واحدة بما ثبت عن عائشة من رواية الزهري أنه كان يسلم من كل اثنتين منهن ولم نجد عنه من فعله ولا من قوله أنه أباح أن يصلي في الليل بتكبيرة أكثر من ركعتين وبذلك نأخذ وهو أصح القولين في ذلك انتهى . وذكر في غاية البيان أن الحق ما قاله الطحاوي لأن استدلالهم استدلال بالمحتمل فلا يكون حجة، وهذا لأنه يحتمل أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يصلي أربع ركعات فرض العشاء وأربع ركعات سنة العشاء وثلاث ركعات الوتر فيكون المجموع إحدى عشرة ركعة وليس في حديث عائشة قيد التطوع حتى يدل على إباحة الثماني على أن عائشة في رواية الزهري عن عروة فسرت الإجمال وأزالت الاحتمال فلم يدل على إباحة ثماني ركعات بتسليمة انتهى
Better. It was objected in al-Bada'i' that it is problematic with the increase beyond four in the day. He said: The correct view is that it is disliked because it has not been narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) — end. In Munyat al-Musalli, that increase is disliked by consensus, i.e., by the consensus of Abu Hanifa and his two companions, and this weakens the statement of al-Sarakhsi. However, in al-Khulasa, what al-Sarakhsi held was corrected, supported by what is in Sahih Muslim from 'A'ishah (may Allah be pleased with her) in a long hadith: 'He used to pray nine rak'ahs, not sitting in them except in the eighth, remembering Allah, praising Him, and supplicating, then he would stand up without saying salam, then pray the ninth, then sit, remember, praise, and supplicate, then say salam audibly to us.' Except that this necessitates not allowing sitting at all except after the eighth, and allowing voluntary prayer with the witr of rak'ahs. Their consensus is on the obligation of sitting at the head of every two rak'ahs in voluntary prayers absolutely, rather the dispute is on its corruption by leaving it, and on the dislike of performing voluntary witr from the rak'ahs. It is strange what al-Tahawi mentioned: his refutation of their proof for permitting eight with one taslimah by what is established from 'A'ishah via al-Zuhri's narration: 'He used to say salam after every two of them, and we have not found from his action or statement that he permitted praying at night with one takbir more than two rak'ahs. This is what we adopt, and it is the more correct of the two opinions on this' — end. It is mentioned in Ghayat al-Bayan that the truth is what al-Tahawi said, because their proof is based on probability and thus not a proof. This is because it is possible that he (peace be upon him) was praying four rak'ahs for obligatory 'Isha', four rak'ahs for the sunnah of 'Isha', and three rak'ahs for witr, totaling eleven rak'ahs. The hadith of 'A'ishah does not contain the condition of voluntary prayer to indicate the permissibility of eight. Moreover, 'A'ishah in al-Zuhri's narration from 'Urwah interpreted the ambiguity and removed the probability, so it does not prove the permissibility of eight rak'ahs with one taslimah.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage continues the intra-Hanafi dispute over increasing nafl at night beyond eight rak'ahs. It presents two opposing views: (1) The majority view (as in al-Bada'i' and Munyat al-Musalli) that it is disliked (makruh) by consensus of Abu Hanifa and his two students, using the principle that no report shows the Prophet doing so. (2) The view of Imam al-Sarakhsi and the author of al-Khulasa, who cite the hadith of 'A'ishah about the Prophet praying nine rak'ahs with one taslimah. Al-Tahawi argues against this, noting that the hadith is ambiguous and other narrations show the Prophet prayed in sets of two. The passage concludes with Ghayat al-Bayan supporting al-Tahawi's position. The crux is that the hadith can be interpreted as including the obligatory prayer and its sunnah, not pure voluntary prayer. The relied-upon view is that increasing beyond eight with one taslimah is makruh.

Key Terms
الإجماع (al-ijma'): Consensus of the Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) on the dislike of the increase.
القعود على رأس الركعتين (al-qu'ud 'ala ra's al-rak'atayn): Sitting (for tashahhud) after every two rak'ahs in voluntary prayers.
التنفل بالوتر من الركعات (al-tanafful bil-witr min al-rak'at): Performing the witr prayer as part of the voluntary rak'ahs without a separate sitting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Aisha's report via al-Zuhri that the Prophet prayed in sets of two.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi majority considers it makruh tahrimi to join more than eight rak'ahs at night without sitting after every two; the opposing view is weaker.

Eight Rak'ahs with One Taslim: Dispute and Proof
Discusses permissibility of eight rak'ahs with one taslim and refutes Tahawi's objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying eight rak'ahs with one taslim, explain the intra-madhhab disagreement, and evaluate the evidentiary basis of each position.

Core Idea
Eight rak'ahs with one taslim: makruh tahrimi by day, debated by night; the hadith of nine rak'ahs allows it, but may be abrogated or specific.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq tackles a nuanced issue in supererogatory prayer: the validity of linking many rak'ahs with a single taslim. While the majority Hanafi position prohibits this beyond four rak'ahs in daytime, later scholars like al-Sarakhsi differ based on a Sahih Muslim hadith. The text critically examines the proofs, including the famous hadith of Aisha about the Prophet's night prayer, and the counter-arguments from al-Tahawi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act under discussion? Praying eight rak'ahs of supererogatory prayer with only one taslim at the end. State the Hanafi hukm: makruh tahrimi for daytime, but disagreed for night.
The passage focuses on night prayer but the principle applies to daytime as agreed.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the proof cited for permissibility: the hadith in Sahih Muslim from Aisha that the Prophet prayed nine rak'ahs (eight + one witr) without sitting except in the eighth.
This is the primary textual evidence used by al-Sarakhsi and others who allow eight with one taslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves the point: The Prophet's action of not sitting in the first seven rak'ahs indicates that linking eight rak'ahs without sitting is permissible. The sitting only in the eighth shows the pattern.
However, the text notes that this could be interpreted otherwise, as al-Tahawi does.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Intra-Hanafi: Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn – makruh; al-Sarakhsi – permitted. Also al-Tahawi's objection: the authentic narration from Aisha (via al-Zuhri) says the Prophet made taslim after every two rak'ahs.
The disagreement stems from different understandings of the same events and preferences for different narrations.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Analyze the response from later authorities: The hadith of sitting after every two is either abrogated (نسخ) or a specific trait of the Prophet (خصائص). The consensus of the imams on the obligation of sitting after every two is given weight.
The text ultimately leans towards al-Sarakhsi's view but acknowledges the majority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أفضل. ورده في البدائع بأنه يشكل بالزيادة على الأربع في النهار قال: والصحيح أنه يكره لأنه لم يرو عن النبي انتهى . وفي منية المصلي أن الزيادة المذكورة مكروهة بالإجماع أي بإجماع أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه وبه يضعف قول السرخسي، وصحح في الخلاصة ما ذهب إليه السرخسي ويشهد له ما في صحيح مسلم عن عائشة رضي الله عنها في حديث طويل إنه كان يصلي تسع ركعات لا يجلس فيهن إلا في الثامنة فيذكر الله تعالى ويحمده ويدعوه، ثم ينهض ولا يسلم فيصلي التاسعة ثم يقعد فيذكر الله تعالى ويحمده ويدعوه ثم يسلم تسليماً يسمعنا» إلا أن هذا يقتضي عدم جواز القعود فيها أصلاً إلا بعد الثامنة وجواز التنفل بالوتر من الركعات وكلمتهم على وجوب القعدة على رأس الركعتين من النفل مطلقاً، وإنما الخلاف في الفساد بتركها وعلى كراهة التنفل بالوتر من الركعات ومن العجب ما ذكره الطحاوي من رده استدلالهم على إباحة الثماني بتسليمة واحدة بما ثبت عن عائشة من رواية الزهري أنه كان يسلم من كل اثنتين منهن ولم نجد عنه من فعله ولا من قوله أنه أباح أن يصلي في الليل بتكبيرة أكثر من ركعتين وبذلك نأخذ وهو أصح القولين في ذلك انتهى. وذكر في غاية البيان أن الحق ما قاله الطحاوي لأن استدلالهم استدلال بالمحتمل فلا يكون حجة، وهذا لأنه يحتمل أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يصلي أربع ركعات فرض العشاء وأربع ركعات سنة العشاء وثلاث ركعات الوتر فيكون المجموع إحدى عشرة ركعة وليس في حديث عائشة قيد التطوع حتى يدل على إباحة الثماني على أن عائشة في رواية الزهري عن عروة فسرت الإجمال وأزالت الاحتمال فلم يدل على إباحة ثماني ركعات بتسليمة انتهى . لأن ما ذكرناه عن في حرج في العمل بها ا.هـ. قوله : ( وفي الفتاوي البزازية أي وأوضحه في الفتاوي البزازية قوله : يشكل بالزيادة الخ) يفيد أن الزيادة في نفل النهار متفق عليها وبه صرح في النهر فقال : وكره الزيادة على أربع بتسليمة في نفل النهار باتفاق الروايات لأنه لم يرد أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام زاد على ذلك ولولا الكراهة لزاد تعليماً للجواز كذا قالوا وهذا يفيد أنها تحريمية ا هـ . لكن في هذه الإفادة نظر لتوقفها على ثبوت أن كل ما كان جائزاً كان يفعله عليه الصلاة والسلام تعليماً للجواز، وإن كل شيء لم يفعله عليه الصلاة والسلام يكون غير جائز وليس بالواقع والكراهة التحريمية لا بد لها من دليل خاص تأمل. قوله : (إلا أن هذا يقتضي الخ) قال في البرهان مجيباً عن هذا الإشكال : اتفاق الأئمة على القعود على رأس كل شفع لما روينا دليل انتساخه أو أنه . من خصائصه صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم. كذا في حاشية نوح أفندي على الدرر قوله : (لأن ما ذكرناه الخ) قال في أمداد الفتاح عن البرهان بعد ما أورد على الطحاوي حديث مسلم : إلا أن اتفاق الأئمة على القعود على رأس كل شفع لما روينا دليل انتساخه أو أنه من خصائصه صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم ا هـ . وأجاب في الأمداد عن الطحاوي بأنه ليس مراده نفي الوجدان من أصله بل وجدان ما ليس معارضاً ولا حاضراً ولا صحیح مسلم صريح في رد كلام الطحاوي ومن تبعه لأن الثماني كانت نفلاً بتسليمة واحدة
... And he rejected it in al-Bada'i' with that it is problematic with the increase beyond four in the daytime. He said: The correct is that it is disliked because it has not been narrated from the Prophet. End. In Munyat al-Musalli, that stated increase is disliked by consensus, i.e., consensus of Abu Hanifa and his companions, and by that the saying of al-Sarakhsi is weakened. In al-Khulasa, what al-Sarakhsi went to is declared correct, and it is supported by what is in Sahih Muslim from A'isha in a long hadith: He used to pray nine rak'ahs, not sitting in them except in the eighth, then he would mention Allah, praise Him, and supplicate, then rise without salutation, and pray the ninth, then sit, mention Allah, praise Him, and supplicate, then make salutation so we could hear. Except that this implies the impermissibility of sitting in them at all except after the eighth, and permissibility of supererogatory witr from the rak'ahs. And their unanimous view is the obligation of sitting at the head of two rak'ahs in supererogatory prayer absolutely, but the disagreement is over invalidation by omission, and the dislike of supererogatory witr from the rak'ahs. And astonishing is what al-Tahawi mentioned in rejecting their deduction for permissibility of eight with one taslim by what is confirmed from A'isha from the narration of al-Zuhri that he used to make salutation after every two of them, and we have not found from him in action or saying that he permitted praying at night with one takbir more than two rak'ahs. And that is what we adopt, and it is the more correct of the two sayings in that. End. In Ghayat al-Bayan, it is stated that the truth is what al-Tahawi said, because their deduction is with probability, so it is not proof. And this is because it is probable that he was praying four fard of Isha, four sunnah of Isha, and three witr, total eleven, and there is no restriction of supererogatory in A'isha's hadith to indicate permissibility of eight, while A'isha in the narration of al-Zuhri from Urwa explained the summary and removed probability, so it does not indicate permissibility of eight rak'ahs with one taslim. End. Because what we mentioned about ... in harm in acting upon it. His saying: (And in al-Fatawa al-Bazzaziyya, i.e., it was clarified in al-Fatawa al-Bazzaziyya, his saying: it is problematic with the increase, etc.) indicates that the increase in daytime supererogatory is agreed upon, and it is declared in al-Nahr: And increase beyond four with one taslim in daytime supererogatory is disliked by agreement of the narrations because it has not been narrated that he increased beyond that, and were it not disliked, he would have increased to teach its permissibility. So they said, and this indicates it is prohibitive dislike. But there is consideration in this indication because it depends on establishing that everything permissible he would do to teach permissibility, and that everything he did not do is not permissible, which is not the reality, and prohibitive dislike requires specific evidence. Reflect. His saying: (Except that this implies, etc.) He said in al-Burhan answering this objection: The agreement of the imams on sitting at the head of every pair because what we narrated is evidence of its abrogation or that it is from his specific qualities. Similarly in the gloss of Nuh Afandi on al-Durar. His saying: (Because what we mentioned etc.) He said in Imdad al-Fattah from al-Burhan after he objected to al-Tahawi with the hadith of Muslim: Except that the agreement of the imams on sitting at the head of every pair because what we narrated is evidence of its abrogation or that it is from his specific qualities. End. He answered in al-Imdad concerning al-Tahawi that his intention is not to deny existence entirely, but existence of that which is not opposed nor present nor ... and Sahih Muslim is explicit in refuting al-Tahawi and those who follow him, because the eight were supererogatory with one taslim.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of praying eight rak'ahs with one taslim, particularly in the context of night prayer. It begins by noting a dispute: some say increasing beyond four in daytime is disliked, and there is a consensus of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on dislike. However, al-Sarakhsi differs, and his view is supported by a hadith from Sahih Muslim where the Prophet prayed nine rak'ahs (eight plus one witr) without sitting except in the eighth. The author then discusses a counter-argument: the hadith might imply no sitting except after the eighth, which contradicts the established rule that one must sit after every two rak'ahs in supererogatory prayer. The text then presents al-Tahawi's view that the Prophet always made salutation after every two rak'ahs, thus rejecting the permissibility of eight with one taslim. A response from al-Burhan says that the hadith of sitting after every two may be abrogated or a specific trait of the Prophet. The final note states that Sahih Muslim explicitly refutes al-Tahawi because the eight rak'ahs were supererogatory with one taslim. The passage ultimately shows the complexity of deriving rulings from contradictory hadith reports.

Key Terms
مكروه (makruh): In this passage, it refers to a ruling of dislike, likely prohibitive (makruh tahrimi) due to contradicting a sunnah practice.
القعود (al-qu'ud): Sitting after two rak'ahs in supererogatory prayer; its obligation is discussed.
الخصائص (al-khasa'is): Specific traits or practices unique to the Prophet; not applicable to the ummah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn), what is the ruling on praying more than four rak'ahs with one taslim in daytime supererogatory prayer?
A) Permitted (mubah)
B) Recommended (mustahab)
C) Disliked (makruh)
D) Forbidden (haram)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prioritizes the established practice of sitting after every two rak'ahs, viewing the hadith of nine rak'ahs as either abrogated or specific to the Prophet, thus ruling eight with one taslim as makruh tahrimi during daytime.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Preferred Rak'ahs in Supererogatory Prayers: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Explains Abu Hanifa's view that four rak'ahs with one taslim is best in both night and day.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Sahibayn positions on the preferred number of rak'ahs in night supererogatory prayer and evaluate the evidence for each view.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: four rak'ahs with one taslim is best; Sahibayn: two-by-two at night.

In the Hanafi school, even within the same madhhab, there can be scholarly disagreement about what is most virtuous. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents Abu Hanifa's view that four rak'ahs with one taslim is best in both night and day supererogatory prayers, while his two main students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, argue that at night two rak'ahs is superior. Let's examine the proofs and understand the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
The issue is not the permissibility of praying four rak'ahs with one taslim—all agree it is permissible—but rather which form is more virtuous (afdal).
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
Abu Hanifa holds that four rak'ahs with one taslim is best in both night and day. His evidence comes from the hadith of A'isha describing the Prophet's night prayer: he prayed four, then four, then three. Also the forenoon prayer of four without separating with taslim.
The key phrase: 'صلى أربعاً فلا تسأل عن حسنهن وطولهن'.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that at night it is better to pray two rak'ahs by two (مثنى مثنى). Their evidence is the famous hadith: 'Night prayer is two by two, then if you fear dawn, pray witr with one.'
This hadith is in Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Sahibayn's evidence
The Hanafi response, as detailed in Fath al-Qadir, is that the command 'two by two' may indicate virtue for those who find four too long, or it may be abrogated by the Prophet's actual practice. The hadith of A'isha shows consistent action, which trumps a general command.
The text also argues that the sahihayn hadith does not prohibit four, as there is consensus that four is permissible.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah) and operative opinion
The practical difference: one who follows Abu Hanifa will pray four rak'ahs with one taslim for night prayer, while one who follows the Sahibayn will pray two rak'ahs. The text notes that some later authorities give fatwa according to the Sahibayn (following the hadith), but others like Shaykh Qasim uphold Abu Hanifa. The author leans towards accepting both as valid, with denial of the Prophet praying four being far-fetched.
Modern practice often follows the Sahibayn for the first part of the night, but Abu Hanifa's view is also widely accepted.

Source Text

قوله : (والأفضل فيهما الرباع) أي الأفضل في الليل والنهار أربع ركعات بتسليمة واحدة عند أبي حنيفة وقالا في الليل ركعتان الحديث الصحيحين عن أبي عمر أن رجلاً قال : يا رسول الله كيف صلاة الليل؟ قال : مثنى مثنى، فإذا خفت الصبح فأوتر بواحدة . ولأبي حنيفة ما في الصحيحين عن عائشة رضي الله عنها : ما كان يزيد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في رمضان ولا في غيره على إحدى عشرة ركعة يصلي أربعاً فلا تسأل عن حسنهن وطولهن، ثم يصلي أربعاً فلا تسأل عن حسنهن وطولهن ثم يصلي ثلاثاً. وما روي عن عائشة الله رضي عنها أنها قالت: كان عليه الصلاة والسلام يصلي الضحى أربعاً ولا يفصل بينهن بسلام. وما تقدم من حديث أبي أيوب وغيره في سنة الظهر والجمعة . ثم الجواب عن دليلهما كما أفاده المحقق في فتح القدير مختصراً أن مقتضى لفظ الحديث إما مثنى في حق الفضيلة بالنسبة إلى ما هو أخف منه، أو أنه منسوخاً ويكون المروي في مسلم محتملاً لبيان الصحة لو فعل لا ندب الفعل، ولذا قال في الاختيار وصلاة الليل ركعتان بتسليمة أو أربع أو ست أو ثمان وكل ذلك نقل في تهجده صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم اهـ. والشأن في بيان الأفضل انتهى. لكن لا يخفى عليك أن قول الطحاوي لم نجد أنه أباح الخ. ينافيه ما ذكره من التأويل لحديث مسلم وما نقله عن الاختيار. والحاصل أن إنكار كونه عليه الصلاة والسلام يصلي أربعاً بعيد جداً ولذا قال في فتح القدير : لا يخفى أنه صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم كان يصلي أربعاً كما كان يصلي ركعتين، فرواية بعض فعله أعني فعل الأربع لا يوجب المعارضة ا هـ . وأبعد منه ما قاله في غاية البيان إذ لا يخفى أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يتهجد من الليل بل كان فرضاً عليه والكلام في نسخ الفرضية كما مر على أنه يلزم عليه أنه ما كان في بعض الأوقات يصلي الوتر لما أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يصلي خمس ركعات ركعات الحديث. وفي التاتارخانية : وما روي أنه صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم صلى إحدى عشرة ركعة فثلاث منها كان وتراً وثماني ركعات صلاة الليل وما روي أنه صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم صلى ثلاث عشرة ركعة فثلاث منها كان وتراً وثماني ركعات صلاة الليل وركعتان للفجر قال الشيخ أبو بكر محمد بن الفضل التفسير منقول عن النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم غير مستخرج من أنفسنا قوله : (وقالا) في الليل (ركعتين قال في النهر قال في العيون وبقولهما يفتي اتباعاً للحديث . في المعراج، ورده الشيخ قاسم بما استدل به المشايخ للإمام من حديث الصحيحين قوله : (ولأبي حنيفة الخ) وجه الاستدلال أنه لو لم يكن كل أربع بتسليم لقالت كان يصلي ركعتين أو كان يصلي ثمانياً قوله : ( إن مقتضى لفظ الحديث (الخ) يعني أن مقتضى لفظ الحديث حصر المبتدأ في الخبر وليس بمراد للاتفاق على جواز الأربع أيضاً وعلى كراهة الواحدة والثلاث في غير الوتر، وإذا انتفى كون المراد لا تباح الاثنتين أو لا تصح لزم كون الحكم ،بمثنى ، أما في حق الفضيلة الخ ما ذكره هنا وذكر في الفتح
His saying: (And the preferred in both of them is four). That is, the preferred in night and day is four rak'ahs with one taslim according to Abu Hanifa. And the two said: at night, two rak'ahs, according to the hadith in the two Sahihs from Abu Umr that a man said: O Messenger of Allah, how is the night prayer? He said: Two by two, and if you fear the dawn, pray witr with one. And for Abu Hanifa is what is in the two Sahihs from A'isha: The Messenger of Allah never increased in Ramadan or otherwise beyond eleven rak'ahs; he prayed four, do not ask about their beauty and length, then he prayed four, do not ask about their beauty and length, then he prayed three. And what is narrated from A'isha that she said: He used to pray the forenoon prayer four and did not separate them with a salutation. And what preceded from the hadith of Abu Ayyub and others regarding the sunnah of Zuhr and Jumu'ah. Then the answer to their evidence as the investigator stated in Fath al-Qadir briefly: That the implication of the wording of the hadith is either two-by-two regarding virtue compared to what is lighter, or that it is abrogated, and what is narrated in Muslim is likely for proving validity if done, not desirability of the action. Hence he said in al-Ikhtiyar: Night prayer is two rak'ahs with one taslim, or four, or six, or eight, and all that is transmitted in his night prayer. And the matter is in clarifying the preferred. But it is not hidden from you that the statement of al-Tahawi 'we did not find that he permitted' contradicts what he mentioned of interpretation of the Muslim hadith and what he quoted from al-Ikhtiyar. In summary, denying that he prayed four is very far. Hence he said in Fath al-Qadir: It is not hidden that he used to pray four as he used to pray two, so the narration of some of his actions, i.e., the action of four, does not cause opposition. And farther than that is what was said in Ghayat al-Bayan, for it is not hidden that he used to pray during the night, rather it was obligatory upon him, and the discussion is about abrogation of obligation, as it follows that at some times he did not pray witr because he used to pray five rak'ahs... in the hadith. And in al-Tatarkhaniyya: And what is narrated that he prayed eleven rak'ahs, three of which were witr and eight rak'ahs of night prayer, and what is narrated that he prayed thirteen rak'ahs, three of which were witr, eight rak'ahs of night prayer, and two for Fajr. Shaykh Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl said: The interpretation is transmitted from the Prophet, not extracted from ourselves. His saying: (And they two said) at night (two rak'ahs). He said in al-Nahr: He said in al-Uyun: And by their two sayings fatwa is given following the hadith. In al-Mi'raj, Shaykh Qasim refuted it with what the mashayikh argued for the Imam from the hadith of the two Sahihs. His saying: (And for Abu Hanifa etc.) The aspect of deduction is that if he had not been praying each four with taslim, she would have said he prayed two or he prayed eight. His saying: (Indeed the implication of the wording of the hadith etc.) means that the implication of the wording of the hadith is the restriction of the subject in the predicate, but it is not intended due to agreement on the permissibility of four as well, and on the dislike of one and three in other than witr. And when it is negated that the meaning is that two are not permitted or not valid, it follows that the ruling is 'two-by-two' regarding virtue etc., as mentioned here and in al-Fath.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the preferred number of rak'ahs in supererogatory prayers at night and day. Abu Hanifa holds that four rak'ahs with one taslim is best in both, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that at night two rak'ahs is best, based on the hadith 'مثنى مثنى' (two by two). Abu Hanifa's evidence comes from hadiths in the Sahihayn where A'isha describes the Prophet praying four and four, then three, and also the forenoon prayer four. The author then presents the response from Fath al-Qadir: the command 'مثنى' may be for virtue, not obligation, or it is abrogated, and the hadith of A'isha shows actual practice. The text also notes that Tahawi's denial of the permission of four is contradicted by evidence. Finally, the passage mentions that some authorities give fatwa according to the Sahibayn, following the hadith, while others like Shaykh Qasim uphold Abu Hanifa's position. The key point is that all agree four is permissible, and the dispute is over what is more virtuous (afdal).

Key Terms
الأفضل (al-afdal): The most virtuous or preferred practice, not obligatory.
الشَّفْع (al-shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs; often used in the context of praying in even numbers.
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer (usually one or three rak'ahs) performed after night prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the preferred (afdal) number of rak'ahs in night supererogatory prayer?
A) Two rak'ahs with one taslim
B) Four rak'ahs with one taslim
C) Eight rak'ahs with one taslim
D) One rak'ah

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, both four rak'ahs with one taslim and two-by-two are valid for night prayer; the dispute is over which is more virtuous, not over permissibility.

Preference of Long Standing Over Many Prostrations
Ruling that long standing is more beloved than many prostrations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the preference of long standing over many rak'ahs and identify the supporting hadith.

Core Idea
In prayer, quality of standing exceeds quantity of rak'ahs.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses a key Hanafi preference: prolonging the standing (qiyam) in prayer is more beloved than increasing the number of rak'ahs. The author cites a hadith and clarifies that 'qunut' here means standing. The commentary also addresses a transmission difference from Imam Muhammad, but the mufta bihi is clear.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the form of prayer: long standing (ṭūl al-qiyām) vs. many prostrations (kathrat al-sujūd). The ruling is a preference (mustahabb): long standing is more beloved.
The text says 'Aḥabbu' indicating comparative preference.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith narrated by Jabir: 'Afḍal al-ṣalāh ṭūl al-qunūt' (The best prayer is long qunut). The author also cites a variant: 'Afḍal al-ṣalāh ṭūl al-qiyām'.
The hadith is found in Muslim, Ahmad, Abu Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit phrase 'afḍal' (best) indicates that long standing is the most virtuous form of prayer. Thus, it is preferred over increasing the number of rak'ahs.
The word 'qunut' is interpreted as standing (qiyam) by Hanafis.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is a transmission from Imam Muhammad (via al-Mujtaba) that may favor many rak'ahs. This view is attributed by some to al-Shafi'i. However, the relied-upon view is long standing.
The disagreement is about which aspect is more virtuous.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The text (from al-Bada'i') corrects the view that long standing is better. The hadith is the primary evidence, and the transmission favoring many rak'ahs is considered weak or out of context.
The mufta bihi is the preference for long standing.

قوله : (وطول القيام أحب من كثرة السجود) أي أفضل من عدد الركعات. وقد اختلف النقل عن محمد في هذه المسألة فنقل الطحاوي عنه في شرح الآثار كما في الكتاب وصححه في البدائع ونسب ما قابله إلى الشافعي ووجهه ما رواه مسلم عن جابر رضي الله عنه أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «أفضل الصلاة طول القنوت» والمراد بالقنوت القيام بدليل ما رواه أحمد وأبو داود مرفوعاً: «أفضل الصلاة طول القيام». ولأن ذكر القراءة وذكر الركوع والسجود التسبيح ونقل عنه في المجتبي أن كثرة جواباً آخر وهو أن مثنى مثنى عبارة عن قوله: أربع صلاة على حدة أربع صلاة على حدة، لأن مثنى معدول عن العدد المكرر وهو اثنان اثنان، فمراده حينئذ اثنان اثنان صلاة على حدة، ثم اثنان اثنان صلاة على حدة وهلم جراً بخلاف ما إذا لم يتكرر لأن معناه حينئذ الصلاة اثنين اثنين. وسبب العدول عن أربع أربع مع أنه أكثر استعمالاً وأشهر لإفادة كون الأربع مفصولة بغير السلام وهو التشهد فقط وإلا كان كل صلاة ركعتين ركعتين وقد كانت أربعاً قال : وقد وقع في بعض الألفاظ ما يحسن تفسيراً على ما قلنا وهو ما أخرجه الترمذي والنسائي عن الفضل ابن العباس أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال الصلاة مثنى مثنى بتشهد في كل ركعتين (۱) ا هـ مختصراً. وكان المؤلف لم يذكره لأن هذا التأويل ينافيه حديث عائشة الذي تقدم عن الطحاوي أنه عليه السلام كان يسلم من كل اثنين، وحينئذ فيكون مثنى الثانية تأكيداً للأولى. وقد يجاب بأن ذلك لا ينافي الحمل المذكور إذ لا ينكر أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان في بعض الأوقات يصلي كل ركعتين بتسليمة، وإنما الكلام في الأفضلية كما مر، وظاهر حديث عائشة أنه كان عامة أحواله صلاة الأربع بتسليمة لقولها : ما كان يزيد في رمضان ولا في غيره. فالأولى حمل حديث «مثنى مثنى» عليه جمعاً وأيسر) قلت : يحتاج إلى الجواب أيضاً عن الست بعد المغرب فإن الأفضل فيها أن تكون بثلاث تسليمات كما تقدم، فالأولى التعليل باتباع الآثار الواردة في كل من صلاة التراويح وصلاة الأوابين
He said: '(And long standing is more beloved than many prostrations)' meaning it is better than the number of rak'ahs. And the transmission from Muhammad differed on this issue: al-Tahawi transmitted from him in Sharh al-Athar as in the book, and al-Bada'i' corrected it, and attributed the opposite to al-Shafi'i, and its justification is what Muslim narrated from Jabir that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'The best prayer is long qunut (standing).' And what is meant by qunut is standing, as evidenced by what Ahmad and Abu Dawud narrated in marfu' form: 'The best prayer is long standing.' And because the dhikr of recitation and the dhikr of bowing and prostrating are tasbih. And it was transmitted from him in al-Mujtaba that 'kathra' (many) is another answer: that 'muthanna muthanna' is an expression of 'four prayers separately, four prayers separately.'...
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling that long standing (qiyam) in prayer is more beloved and better than performing many rak'ahs (i.e., many prostrations). The proof is from the hadith: 'The best prayer is long qunut (standing)' and 'The best prayer is long standing'. The commentary then digresses into a discussion about the interpretation of 'muthanna muthanna' and the transmission from Imam Muhammad regarding whether many rak'ahs or long standing is better. It also touches on the six rak'ahs after Maghrib, stating that the best is to pray them with three taslims (two by two), following the reported practices of Tarawih and Salat al-Awwabin. The overall point is that quality of standing (long recitation) is prioritized over quantity of rak'ahs.

Key Terms
طول القيام (ṭūl al-qiyām): Prolonging the standing portion of prayer, especially through longer recitation.
القنوت (al-qunūt): In this context, it means standing (qiyam) in prayer, not the specific supplication.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Supplication (du'a)
B) Standing (qiyam)
C) Prostration (sujud)
D) Recitation (qira'ah)

Key Takeaway
Long standing in prayer, through extended recitation, is more beloved than performing many rak'ahs, as proven by the hadith.

Fard Elements in Nafl and Witr; Nafl Becomes Binding Once Started
Ruling: fard elements and lizum of nafl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fard elements in nafl and witr, and apply the principle that nafl becomes binding upon commencement.

Core Idea
Sujood and qira'ah are fard in every rak'ah of nafl and witr; starting a nafl makes it wajib to complete.

This passage from the Hanafi matn establishes two core rules: first, that prostration (sujood) and Qur'anic recitation (qira'ah) are obligatory (fard) in every rak'ah of voluntary (nafl) and witr prayers, just as they are in the first two rak'ahs of fard prayers. Second, it introduces the distinctive Hanafi principle that a nafl prayer becomes binding (lazim) once commenced – meaning it must be completed, and if broken, requires qada. These are foundational for correct prayer practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two obligations
Find the two actions explicitly declared fard in the passage: sujood and qira'ah.
They are fard in the two rak'ahs of fard, and in every rak'ah of nafl and witr.
2
Scope of each obligation
Note that for fard prayers, the obligation applies only to the first two rak'ahs; for nafl and witr, it applies to every rak'ah.
3
Recognize the principle of lizum
Identify the phrase 'لزم النفل بالشروع' – the nafl becomes binding (wajib) once begun.
This means you cannot exit a nafl without sin; you must complete it or later make it up.
4
Understand the legal consequence
If a nafl is broken intentionally or by forgetfulness, what is required? The principle implies sin and necessity of qada (making up).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السجود والقراءة فرض في ركعتي الفرض وكل النفل والوتر ولزم النفل بالشروع ولو
Sujood and recitation are obligatory in the two rak'ahs of the fard prayer and in every nafl and witr, and the nafl becomes binding upon commencement, even if...
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This is a concise ruling stating the foundational elements of prayer obligations. It establishes that sujood (prostration) and qira'ah (Qur'anic recitation) are fard (obligatory) in each rak'ah of the obligatory prayer's two rak'ahs (the first two rak'ahs of fard and all rak'ahs of nafl and witr). This means that in every rak'ah of voluntary and witr prayers, recitation and prostration are mandatory; omission invalidates the rak'ah. Additionally, the ruling 'لزم النفل بالشروع' means that once a person begins a nafl prayer, it becomes wajib (necessary) to complete it. If one breaks it without a valid excuse, it must be made up (qada). This is a key principle distinguishing nafl from purely optional acts: the act of commencing changes its legal status.

Key Terms
لزم النفل بالشروع (lazima al-nafl bi al-shurūʿ): The nafl prayer becomes obligatory to complete once commenced; it cannot be broken without sin and requires qada if broken.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling if a person begins a nafl prayer and then breaks it without a valid excuse?
A) No sin, no qada needed
B) Sinful, and must be made up (qada)
C) Permissible but disliked
D) Prayer is invalid but no qada

Key Takeaway
Sujood and qira'ah are fard in every rak'ah of nafl and witr, and commencing a nafl makes it wajib to complete.

Obligation of Sujud and Qira'ah and Virtue of Four Rak'ahs in Nafl
Commentary on the obligation of sujud and qira'ah and the preferred number of rak'ahs in nafl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that sujud and qira'ah are fard in the first two rak'ahs of fard and all nafl, and explain why four rak'ahs with one taslim are more virtuous than two.

Core Idea
Sujud and qira'ah are fard in every rak'ah of nafl and first two of fard; four rak'ahs bring greater reward.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the commentator clarifies the obligation of prostration and recitation in prayer, and then discusses the preference for four rak'ahs over two in voluntary prayers. The key distinction is that the number of rak'ahs in nafl is not fixed, but more rak'ahs bring more reward due to greater hardship, as indicated by a hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? Sujud and qira'ah are ruled as fard (obligatory) in the two rak'ahs of fard and in every rak'ah of nafl and witr.
Note that the passage says 'كل النفل' meaning every nafl rak'ah.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentator cites the hadith: 'Indeed your reward is according to your hardship' to support the virtue of four rak'ahs over two.
This hadith is a dalil naqli (transmitted evidence).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith implies that more hardship (longer standing with more rak'ahs) yields more reward, so four rak'ahs are more virtuous than two.
This is an implicit indication (dalala zanni) but sufficient for preference.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no dispute on the obligation of sujud and qira'ah where stated; the difference is on the virtue of four vs two rak'ahs, resolved by the hadith.
Ikhtilaf here is on virtue, not obligation.
5
Evaluate the application
The commentator applies this to vows: if one vows four rak'ahs with one taslim and prays two taslims, the vow is not fulfilled; but if he vows with two taslims and prays one, it is sufficient. Also, tarawih is done two by two for ease.
The application shows that the specific manner matters in vows, but in general, four with one taslim is superior.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السجود والقراءة فرض في ركعتي الفرض وكل النفل والوتر ولزم النفل بالشروع ولو . الأربع أو في حق الإباحة بالنسبة إلى الفرد وترجيح أحدهما بمرجح وفعله ورد على كلا النحوين لكن عقلنا زيادة فضيلة الأربع لأنها أكثر مشقة على النفس بسبب طول تقييدها في مقام الخدمة، ورأيناه صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : إنما أجرك على قدر نصبك فحكمنا بأن المراد الثاني لا واحدة أو ثلاث ولهذا ذكر في زيادات الزيادات أن من نذر أن يصلي أربعاً بتسليمة فصلاها بتسليمتين لم يجزه، ولو نذر أن يصلي أربعاً بتسلمتين فصلاها بتسليمة واحدة جاز عن نذره، وفي المحيط : وإنما اخترنا في التراويح مثنى مثنى لأنها تؤدى بالجماعة وأداؤها على الناس مثنى مثنى أخف وأيسر .
Prostration and recitation are obligatory in the two rak'ahs of the obligatory prayer and in every voluntary prayer and the witr prayer, and the voluntary prayer becomes binding upon commencing it. ... The four (rak'ahs) or in terms of permissibility for the individual and preferring one over the other with a preferable, and doing it is reported on both ways, but we have understood the increase in virtue of the four because it is more burdensome to the soul due to the length of its restriction in the station of service, and we saw that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Your reward is according to your hardship.' So we ruled that the intended is the second, not one or three. Therefore it is mentioned in Ziyadat al-Ziyadat that if one vows to pray four (rak'ahs) with one taslim and prays them with two taslims, it is not sufficient; and if he vows to pray four with two taslims and prays them with one taslim, it is sufficient for his vow. And in al-Muhit: 'We have chosen in the tarawih prayers (to be) two by two, because it is performed in congregation and performing it for the people two by two is lighter and easier.'
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn line 'Sujud and recitation are obligatory in the two rak'ahs of the obligatory prayer and in every voluntary and witr prayer, and the voluntary prayer becomes binding upon commencing it.' The commentator explains that the ruling applies to both fard and nafl. He then discusses the virtue of praying four rak'ahs with one taslim versus two taslims, citing a hadith about reward being proportional to hardship. He mentions from Ziyadat al-Ziyadat a case of a vow: if one vows four rak'ahs with one taslim and prays them with two taslims, the vow is not fulfilled; conversely, if he vows four with two taslims and prays with one taslim, it is sufficient. This indicates that the intended number of rak'ahs is what matters. The author then quotes from al-Muhit that tarawih is best done two by two because it is easier for the congregation. Throughout, the commentator follows the Hanafi school and uses both hadith and qiyas to support his points.

Key Terms
السجود (al-sujud): Prostration, a pillar of prayer; obligatory in every rak'ah.
القراءة (al-qira'ah): Recitation of Qur'an in prayer; obligatory in the first two rak'ahs of fard and all nafl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is fard
C) It is wajib
D) It is makruh

Key Takeaway
Sujud and qira'ah are fard in the first two rak'ahs of fard and all nafl; four rak'ahs with one taslim are more virtuous due to greater hardship.

Preference Between Length of Standing and Number of Rak'ahs in Nafl
Commentary on the matn line about preferring long standing over many prostrations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi debate on whether long standing or many rak'ahs is more virtuous in nafl prayers and state the preferred position according to the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Core Idea
Standing is a means to prostration; the means cannot surpass the end, so many rak'ahs are better.

This lesson examines a nuanced debate within and outside the Hanafi school: is it better to lengthen your standing by reciting more Quran, or to perform more rak'ahs? The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that length of standing is more beloved, but the commentator of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq argues that many rak'ahs are superior, supported by hadith and legal reasoning. We will trace the arguments and see why the author sides with the latter.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and the matn's initial claim
Identify what the matn says: length of standing is more beloved than many prostrations. This sets the baseline for the discussion.
The matn represents the transmitted school position, but the commentator challenges it.
2
Identify the opponent and their proof
Determine who prefers long standing (Imam al-Shafi'i and some Hanafi transmissions) and their primary evidence: the hadith 'The best of prayer is length of standing' (أفضل الصلاة طول القنوت).
This hadith is sound (Muslim) and seems to directly favor long standing.
3
Follow the Hanafi response to that proof
Examine how the author reinterprets or counters the hadith. He argues that the hadith can be interpreted as referring to the entire prayer, and that the hadith about many prostrations are more specific. Also, the means cannot be better than the end.
The author uses the principle that standing is a means (wasila) to prostration, which is the goal.
4
Analyse the author's preferred position and his dalil
Understand why the author opts for many rak'ahs: he cites the hadith 'You must have many prostrations' (عليك بكثرة السجود), the principle that the closest a servant is to Allah is while prostrating, and the analogy of the sick person who can stand but cannot prostrate—with the ruling that standing is dropped because the purpose is prostration.
The author also notes that recitation is a pillar with some disagreement on its obligation, while rukuh and sujud are unanimously obligatory, making them more worthy.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: a person performing nafl prayer can choose between long recitation in few rak'ahs or many rak'ahs with short recitation; according to the author's view, the latter is superior.
This does not affect validity but does affect which act is more rewarding.

الرائق ج ۲/ م ٧
His statement: 'And length of standing is more beloved than many prostrations' i.e., better than many rak'ahs. And the transmission from Muhammad differed on this issue: al-Tahawi transmitted from him in Sharh al-Athar as in the book and he corrected it in al-Bada'i' and attributed the opposite to al-Shafi'i and his proof is what Muslim narrated from Jabir (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The best of prayer is length of standing' and what is meant by standing is evidenced by what Ahmad and Abu Dawud narrated as marfu'... (continued with the discussion on tashahhud, then the hadith on prostration, the opinion of Ahmad, Abu Yusuf, and the author's conclusion that many rak'ahs are better, followed by comments from al-Nahr and the author's response about the hadith evidence and the correct position).
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage is a lengthy commentary on the matn line 'Length of standing is more beloved than many prostrations.' The commentator first notes that there is a difference in transmission from Imam Muhammad. Al-Tahawi reports that Imam Muhammad considered length of standing better, citing the hadith 'The best of prayer is length of standing.' Others report that he considered many prostrations better. The commentator then discusses the meaning of 'muthanna muthanna' (two by two) from hadith, and how it relates to praying four rak'ahs with one taslim. He also addresses the hadith 'Prayer is two by two with a tashahhud after every two rak'ahs' and its interpretation. Then he moves to the arguments for preferring prostrations, citing hadith like 'You must have many prostrations' and 'The closest a servant is to his Lord is while prostrating.' Due to conflicting evidence, Imam Ahmad remained silent. Abu Yusuf made a distinction: if one has a set nightly recitation, more rak'ahs are better; otherwise long standing is better. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq concludes that many rak'ahs are better because standing is a means to prostration, and the means cannot be better than the end. He supports this with the case of a sick person who can stand but cannot prostrate: the obligation of standing is dropped because the purpose is prostration. He also argues that recitation is an additional pillar with some disagreement on its obligation, whereas prostration and bowing are universally agreed upon, so they are more worthy. Then the commentator al-Nahr raises three objections, and the author responds by arguing that the hadith supporting long standing are clear texts that cannot be interpreted away, and that the hadith about many prostrations may be interpreted metaphorically as referring to the prayer itself. He ends by noting that the relied-upon position in the matn is the one that prefers many rak'ahs, and he criticizes Muhammad al-Ghazzi for following his teacher contrary to the matn.

Key Terms
طول القيام (tawl al-qiyam): Length of standing during prayer, particularly in recitation.
كثرة السجود (kathrat al-sujud): Many prostrations, i.e., many rak'ahs of prayer.
مثنى مثنى (muthanna muthanna): Two by two; referring to praying in units of two rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, what is the primary reason many rak'ahs are better than long standing?
A) Because recitation is more rewarding
B) Because standing is a means to prostration, and the means cannot be better than the end
C) Because the Prophet forbade long standing
D) Because the community prefers it

Key Takeaway
In nafl prayers, increasing the number of rak'ahs (prostrations) is superior to lengthening the standing because standing is a means to prostration, the ultimate purpose of prayer.

Recitation in the First Two Rak'ahs: Fard or Wajib?
Commentary on the obligation of recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the fard obligation of recitation and the wajib obligation of specifying the first two rak'ahs in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Recitation is fard; the first two rak'ahs are wajib — a Hanafi distinction that saves the prayer's validity.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi distinction regarding recitation in obligatory prayers. While the act of reciting is considered fard (obligatory), the specific requirement to recite in the first two rak'ahs is only wajib. Understanding this nuance is crucial for correct prayer practice and for appreciating the Hanafi methodology of weighing obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage discusses recitation (al-qira'ah) in the two rak'ahs of the fard prayer. First, note the overall ruling: recitation is fard (obligatory). Then, locate the specific qualification: it is described as 'fard 'amali' (practical obligation) due to scholarly disagreement.
2
Distinguish between fard and wajib in the specification
The author clarifies that specifying the first two rak'ahs for recitation is not fard but wajib according to the well-known (mashhur) position. This means if one recites in the last two rak'ahs instead, the prayer is still valid but requires sajdah al-sahw.
This distinction is a hallmark of Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi difference
Some scholars (unnamed) held that recitation could be in any two rak'ahs, not necessarily the first two. The author cites al-Bada'i' as correcting that the specific place is the first two rak'ahs in the four-rak'ah prayer.
This is an expansion (probe) of the matn's claim.
4
Consider the cross-madhhab perspective
Imam al-Shafi'i considers recitation fard in every rak'ah, without the fard/wajib distinction. The Hanafi position rests on the practical obligation (fard 'amali) and the consensus of the companions on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ.
The thamarah (practical consequence) is that a Shafi'i who omits recitation in any rak'ah must repeat the prayer.

Source Text

قوله : ( والقراءة فرض في ركعتي الفرض أي فرض عملي كما في السراج الوهاج للاختلاف فيه بين العلماء، ولم يعيد الركعتين بالأوليين لأن تعيينهما للقراءة ليس بفرض وإنما هو واجب على المشهور في المذهب وصرح به المصنف في عد الواجبات وصحح في البدائع أن محلها الركعتان الأوليان عيناً في الصلاة الرباعية. وقال بعضهم: ركعتان منها غير
His statement: 'And recitation is obligatory in the two rak'ahs of the obligatory prayer' i.e., it is a practical obligation as in al-Siraj al-Wahaj due to the disagreement among scholars. And he did not repeat the two rak'ahs with the first two because specifying them for recitation is not obligatory but rather it is wajib according to the well-known position in the school, and the author stated it in the count of obligations, and he corrected in al-Bada'i' that their place is the first two rak'ahs specifically in the four-rak'ah prayer. And some said: two rak'ahs of it other than...
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn line 'And recitation is obligatory in the two rak'ahs of the obligatory prayer.' The commentator explains that this is a practical obligation (fard 'amali) because there is disagreement among scholars about whether it is fard or wajib. He further notes that specifying the first two rak'ahs for recitation is not a fard condition; rather, it is wajib according to the well-known position in the Hanafi school. The author of the matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) listed it in the count of obligations (wajibat). Al-Bada'i' confirms that the specific place for recitation in the four-rak'ah prayer is the first two rak'ahs. This distinction is important: the obligation itself is fard, but the designation of which rak'ahs is only wajib, meaning that if one recites in the last two rak'ahs instead, the prayer is still valid but one should perform sajdah al-sahw. The text then starts a differing opinion ('And some said: two rak'ahs of it other than...') but is cut off.

Key Terms
فرض عملي (fard 'amali): A practical obligation, meaning the obligation is established by practice and consensus, but there is theoretical disagreement on its status.
تعيين الركعتين (ta'yin al-rak'atayn): Specification of the two rak'ahs for recitation (the first two).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) It is makruh

Key Takeaway
Recitation is a fard obligation in two rak'ahs, but the specific requirement to recite in the first two rak'ahs is a wajib that does not affect prayer validity if missed, only requiring sajdah al-sahw.

Preferring Many Rak'ahs over Long Qiyam in Supererogatory Prayers
Debate on whether multiplying rak'ahs or lengthening qiyam is more virtuous in nafl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the virtue of increasing rak'ahs versus lengthening qiyam in nafl prayers and evaluate the supporting proofs and internal disagreements.

Core Idea
Standing is a means; prostration is the end — thus many rak'ahs are better than long qiyam.

This lesson explores a nuanced debate within the Hanafi school regarding the most virtuous form of supererogatory prayer. While some might assume that longer standing with more Qur'an recitation is superior, the Hanafi position — based on hadith and rational analysis — holds that increasing the number of rak'ahs is better. We will examine the proofs, the internal disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf, and how later scholars resolved the issue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and base ruling
Understand that the debate is about the relative virtue of two aspects of supererogatory prayer: increasing the number of rak'ahs vs. lengthening the qiyam (standing) with more recitation. The base ruling from Imam Abu Hanifa is that many rak'ahs are better.
This is a matter of mandub (recommended) and not wajib.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Examine the hadiths cited: 'You must perform many prostrations' and 'The closest a servant is to his Lord is while prostrating.' Also note the rational argument that standing is a means to the end of ruku' and sujud, as evidenced by the ruling for the sick who drop standing but not prostration.
The hadiths are from Sahih Muslim.
3
Analyze the internal ikhtilaf
Study Imam Abu Yusuf's distinction: if one has a fixed nightly recitation portion, lengthening qiyam is better; otherwise, many rak'ahs are better. Understand why he made this distinction.
Abu Yusuf's view is recorded in al-Mujtaba and al-Bada'i.
4
Evaluate the tarjih and criticisms
Read the author's preference for Abu Hanifa's view and the objections raised by al-Nahr. The author counters that the hadiths about standing are explicit, while 'many prostrations' might mean prayer in general. Understand why the author sides with the texts.
The author criticizes al-Ghazzi for following his shaykh against the established texts.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Conclude that the relied-upon position is that many rak'ahs are better, as supported by the texts of the school and the majority of later Hanafi scholars.
This is the position of Ibn Nujaym and aligns with the matns of the school.

الركوع والسجود أفضل لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام للسائل كما في صحيح مسلم «عليك بكثرة السجود» ولآخر «أعني على نفسك بكثرة السجود»، وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «أقرب ما يكون العبد من ربه وهو ساجد» ولأن السجود غاية التواضع والعبودية، ولتعارض الأدلة توقف الإمام أحمد في هذه المسألة ولم يحكم فيها بشيء، وفصل الإمام أبو يوسف كما في المجتبي والبدائع فقال : إذا كان له ورد في الليل بقراءة من القرآن فالأفضل أن يكثر الركعتين فترجح هذا القول بما ذكرنا بعد تعارض الدلائل المتقدمة . قوله : ( والذي ظهر للعبد الضعيف الخ قال في النهر : فيه نظر من وجوه : أما أولاً فلأن القيام وإن كان وسيلة إلا أن أفضلية طوله إنما كانت بكثرة القراءة فيه وهي وإن بلغت كل القرآن تقع فرضاً بخلاف التسبيحات فإنها وإن كثرت لا تزيد على السنة . وأما ثانياً فلأن كون القراءة ركناً زائداً مما لا أثر له في الفضيلة بخلاف الركوع والسجود وأما Ruku' and prostration are better because of his statement, peace be upon him, to the questioner as in Sahih Muslim: 'You must perform many prostrations' and to another: 'Help me against yourself by many prostrations,' and his statement, peace be upon him, 'The closest a servant is to his Lord is while he is prostrating,' and because prostration is the ultimate humility and servitude. Due to the contradictory evidences, Imam Ahmad refrained in this issue and did not decide anything. Imam Abu Yusuf made a distinction, as in al-Mujtaba and al-Bada'i': he said: If one has a nightly portion of Qur'an recitation, then the best is to increase the number of rak'ahs; otherwise, lengthening the standing is better because the standing in the first does not vary and it includes additional ruku' and prostration. End. What appears to this weak servant is that many rak'ahs are better than long standing because standing is legislated only as a means to ruku' and prostration, as they stated in the prayer of the sick: if he can stand but cannot do ruku' and prostration, standing is dropped from him despite his ability because of his inability to do what is intended; so the means cannot be better than the intended end. And as for its necessity due to much recitation, that does not give preference either, because recitation is an additional pillar as they stated, despite the disagreement on its fundamental pillar status, unlike ruku' and prostration on whose pillar status and fundamentality there is consensus, as we have stated, along with the fact that standing is omitted from recitation in obligatory prayers beyond the first two rak'ahs. So this view is preferred by what we have mentioned after the previous contradictory evidences. His statement: 'What appears to this weak servant...' al-Nahr said: In it there are objections from several aspects: First, standing, though a means, its virtue in length is due to much recitation in it, and even if it reaches the entire Qur'an, it falls as obligatory, unlike the tasbihat which, even if abundant, do not exceed the sunnah. Second, that recitation is an additional pillar has no effect on virtue, unlike ruku' and prostration. Third, that standing is omitted from recitation in obligatory prayers is not part of the subject here, because the subject matter is about supererogatory prayers, in which recitation is obligatory in all of it. I have not seen in their statements, for example, if a mute person prays supererogatorily, is long standing better for him than for one who recites? So ponder. End. And I say: The hadiths indicating the superiority of standing are explicit in what is required and cannot be interpreted otherwise, unlike others, because it is possible that the meaning of 'many prostrations' is engaging much in prayer by using part for the whole, as prostration is used to mean prayer, as in His statement 'al-rukka' al-sujud' and 'taqallubaka fi al-sajidin.' This supports what is in the texts, which is the statement of the Imam, authenticated by al-Bada'i'. Amazing how Shaykh Muhammad al-Ghazzi followed his shaykh and opposed the texts, and in the text of al-Tanwir he followed what his shaykh chose here, while the texts are meant to transmit the school.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a debate within the Hanafi school about what is more virtuous in supererogatory (nafl) prayers: increasing the number of rak'ahs or lengthening the standing (qiyam) with more recitation. The author begins by presenting the view that ruku' and sujud (bowing and prostration) are better than standing, citing hadiths that encourage many prostrations and that the servant is closest to Allah while prostrating. He notes that due to conflicting evidences, Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal refrained from giving a definitive ruling. Then he mentions Imam Abu Yusuf's distinction: if a person has a fixed portion of Qur'an recitation at night, then increasing rak'ahs is better; otherwise, lengthening standing is better. However, the author (the weak servant) prefers the view that many rak'ahs are better, because standing is only a means to the end of ruku' and sujud. He supports this with the reasoning from the prayer of the sick: if one can stand but cannot perform ruku' and sujud, the standing is dropped, showing that the end (ruku' and sujud) is more important. He also argues that recitation is an additional pillar, but ruku' and sujud are the core pillars with consensus. Then he addresses al-Nahr's criticism, which raises three objections: (1) standing's virtue comes from recitation, which is obligatory, unlike tasbihat in sujud; (2) recitation being an extra pillar does not affect virtue; (3) the rule about standing being omitted in obligatory prayers does not apply here because we are discussing nafl where recitation is required in every rak'ah. The author responds by saying the hadiths about standing are clear and cannot be reinterpreted, while the hadiths about prostration might mean prayer in general. He concludes by criticizing al-Ghazzi for following his shaykh against the established texts of the school. The relied-upon position is that increasing rak'ahs is better, as per Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
السجود (al-sujud): The act of prostration, considered the ultimate expression of humility and the closest state of the servant to Allah; a fundamental pillar of prayer upon which there is consensus.
الركوع (al-ruku'): The act of bowing in prayer, also a pillar of prayer.
القيام (al-qiyam): The standing posture in prayer, which is a means to perform ruku' and sujud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Lengthening qiyam with more recitation
B) Increasing the number of rak'ahs
C) Reciting the entire Qur'an in one rak'ah
D) Performing the prayer silently

Key Takeaway
In supererogatory prayers, increasing the number of rak'ahs is more virtuous than lengthening the standing, because ruku' and sujud are the ultimate ends of prayer.

Place of Obligatory Recitation: First Two Rak'ahs or Any Two?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the specific place of recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two Hanafi views on the specific place of recitation in salah and explain the practical consequence for sajda sahw.

Core Idea
Recitation is fard in two rak'ahs; the dispute is whether the first two are specified as a wajib or as a practical fard.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi disagreement: is the obligatory recitation (qira'ah) in prayer specifically tied to the first two rak'ahs, or can it be performed in any two? The apparent contradiction between the authenticated view in al-Bada'i' and the view of al-Quduri is resolved by understanding the nature of the requirement—whether it is a fard 'amali (practical fard) or a wajib. The practical result is the same (sajda sahw is required), but the cause differs, and this distinction affects the level of sin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting positions
State the authenticated view (first two rak'ahs specifically) and the opposing view (any two rak'ahs, but preference for the first two). Note the authorities: al-Bada'i' vs. al-Quduri.
Both views are within the Hanafi school.
2
Analyze the proofs for each view
The authenticated view relies on the original text (al-Asl) of Imam Muhammad and the practice of the Prophet. The opposing view cites the general verse (Muzzammil 20) and the absence of explicit specification.
The verse is general; the disagreement is whether the Sunnah specifies it.
3
Understand the practical consequence (thamara)
Both views require sajda sahw if one recites only in the last two rak'ahs. The difference is the cause: on the first view, it is changing the fard from its place (recitation in the last two is qada); on the second, it is leaving a wajib (the designation is a wajib, not fard).
The ruling is the same, but the underlying legal reason differs.
4
Resolve the apparent contradiction with 'fard amali'
The commentator explains that the authenticated view considers the specification a 'practical fard' (certain in practice but speculative in evidence). This is why the prayer is not invalidated if omitted—it is treated like a wajib in terms of consequence.
This resolves the doubt: why isn't the prayer batil if a 'fard' is missed?
5
Synthesize the tarjih (preferred view)
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the first two rak'ahs are specifically designated as a wajib (or practical fard). This is supported by the majority of later scholars and aligns with the original text.
The view of al-Quduri is considered weak in comparison.
