قوله : ( والقراءة فرض في ركعتي الفرض أي فرض عملي كما في السراج الوهاج للاختلاف فيه بين العلماء، ولم يعيد الركعتين بالأوليين لأن تعيينهما للقراءة ليس بفرض وإنما هو واجب على المشهور في المذهب وصرح به المصنف في عد الواجبات وصحح في البدائع أن محلها الركعتان الأوليان عيناً في الصلاة الرباعية. وقال بعضهم: ركعتان منها غير عين مع اتفاقهم على أنه لو قرأ في الأخريين فقط فإنها صحيحة وأنه يجب عليه سجود السهو إن كان ساهياً على كلا القولين المذكورين، ففائدة الاختلاف إنما هو في سبب سجود السهو، فعلى ما صححه سببه تغيير الفرض عن محله وتكون قراءته في الأخريين قضاء عن قراءته في الأوليين، وعلى قول البعض سببه ترك الواجب وقراءته في الأخريين أداء لا قضاء والأمر سهل. وما في غاية البيان من أن تعيين القراءة في الأوليين أفضل إن شاء قرأ فيهما وإن شاء قرأ في الأخريين أو في إحدى الأوليين وإحدى الأخريين ضعيف لتصريح الجم الغفير بالوجوب في الأوليين لا بالأفضلية وإنما كانت فرضاً في ركعتين لقوله تعالى فاقرؤوا ما تيسر من القرآن [المزمل : ٢٠] وهو لا يقتضي التكرار فكان مؤداه افتراضها في ركعة إلا أن مر بعضهم الخ) يوهم أنه قول آخر غير القولين السابقين مع أنه عين الأول المعبر عنه بالمشهور قوله : (ففائدة الاختلاف الخ) قال في النهر : لكن سيأتي في السهو أن تأخير الفرض فيه ترك واجب أيضاً، ويمكن أن يظهر في اختلاف مراتب الإثم، فعلى الأولى يأثم إثم تارك الواجب، وعلى الثاني إثم تارك الفرض العملي الذي هو أقوى نوعي الواجب على ما . تحقيقه ا هـ . قلت : لي هنا شبهة أشكلت علي وذلك أنه لا خلاف عندنا في فرضية القراءة في الصلاة وإنما الخلاف في تعيين محلها، وحينئذ فمعنى القول الذي صححه في البدائع أن القراءة فرض وكونها في الأوليين فرض آخر، ومقتضى هذا بطلان الصلاة بتركها في الأوليين وعدم اعتبار كونها قضاء في الأخريين لأنه إذا قرأ في الأخريين فقد أتى بفرض القراءة، وأما فرض كونها في الأوليين فقد فات ولا يمكن تداركه كما لو أتى بتكبيرة الافتتاح بعد القراءة ولم يقرأ بعدها وليس هذا كتأخير سجدة إلى آخر الصلاة فإنه وإن كان فيه تأخير فرض لكن عدم التأخير ليس بفرض وإنما هو واجب وما نحن فيه فرض وكونه فرضاً عملياً لا يقتضي عدم البطلان لأنه ما يفوت الجواز بفواته كمسح الرأس فهو في قولة القطعي في العمل كما مر صدر الكتاب اللهم إلا أن يقال : إنه وإن كان في قولة القطعي لكنه ظني وكان مقتضى تركه الفساد لكنه لم يحكم به احتياطاً لكونه فصلاً مجتهداً فيه على نحو ما سيأتي في المسائل الثمانية في تخريج قول الإمام تأمل والذي يظهر لي أن ما في البدائع من أن محلها الركعتان الأوليان عيناً أراد به التعيين على سبيل الوجوب لا الافتراض، وإن ما قاله بعضهم من أن محلها ركعتان غير عين مراده أن تعيين الأوليين أفضل وهو ما سيأتي عن غاية البيان ففي المسألة قولان لا ثلاثة، يدل على ذلك ما ذكره في شرح ابن أمير حاج على المنية عند ذكر فرائض الصلاة حيث قال قال في شرح الطحاوي للأسبيجابي قال أصحابنا : القراءة فرض في ركعتين بغير أعيانهما وأفضلها في الأوليين وإليه ذهب القدوري أيضاً لكن نص في التحفة والبدائع على أن الصحيح من مذهب أصحابنا أن محل القراءة المفروضة الركعتان الأوليان عيناً وإليه أشار في الأصل حيث قال : إذا ترك القراءة في الأوليين يقضيها في الأخريين، وعليه مشى في الذخيرة والمحيط الرضوي وغيرهما، ثم ذكر في شرح المنية عند واجبات الصلاة أن ثمرة الخلاف في وجوب سجود السهو وعدمه لو تركها في الأوليين أو
His statement: 'And the recitation is fard in two rak'ahs of the obligatory prayer' i.e., practical fard as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj due to disagreement among scholars. He does not repeat the two rak'ahs with the first two because their designation for recitation is not fard but rather wajib according to the well-known view in the school, and the author stated it in the list of wajibats. In al-Bada'i', it is authenticated that its place is specifically the first two rak'ahs in the four-rak'ah prayer. And some said: two rak'ahs of it are unspecified. There is agreement that if he recites only in the last two, the prayer is valid and he must perform sajda sahw if he was forgetful, on both mentioned views. So the fruit of the disagreement is only in the cause of sajda sahw: according to the authenticated view, its cause is changing the fard from its place, and his recitation in the last two is a make-up for his recitation in the first two; according to the other view, its cause is leaving the wajib, and his recitation in the last two is performance, not make-up. What is in Ghayat al-Bayan that the designation of recitation in the first two is recommended—if he wishes he recites in them, or in the last two, or in one of the first two and one of the last two—is weak because the great majority explicitly state obligation in the first two, not recommendation. Rather, recitation is fard in two rak'ahs due to His statement 'So recite what is easy of the Qur'an' which does not necessitate repetition, so its import is the obligation of it in one rak'ah except that... (some said) gives the impression that it is another view besides the two previous, while it is the same as the first expressed as the well-known. His statement: 'The fruit of the disagreement...' al-Nahr said: But it will come in the chapter on forgetfulness that delaying the fard is also leaving a wajib, and it can appear in the difference in levels of sin: according to the first, he sins the sin of one leaving a wajib; according to the second, the sin of one leaving a practical fard which is the stronger of the two types of wajib according to its verification. End. I said: I have a doubt here that puzzled me: There is no disagreement among us about the obligatoriness of recitation in prayer; rather, the disagreement is about designating its place. In that case, the meaning of the view authenticated in al-Bada'i' is that recitation is fard, and its being in the first two is another fard. The implication of this is the invalidity of the prayer if it is left in the first two, and its recitation in the last two is not considered a make-up because if he recites in the last two, he has performed the fard of recitation, but the fard of being in the first two has been missed and cannot be made up, like if he performed the opening takbir after recitation and did not recite after it. This is not like delaying a prostration to the end of the prayer, for although it includes delaying a fard, not delaying is not a fard but rather wajib. Our case is fard, and being a practical fard does not negate invalidity, because what causes permissibility to be lost is its loss, like wiping the head. So it is in the category of certain in practice as passed at the beginning of the book, unless it is said that although it is in the category of certain, it is speculative, and its omission would necessitate corruption, but it was not ruled as such out of precaution because it is a matter of ijtihad, similar to what will come in the eight issues in deriving the statement of the Imam. Contemplate. What appears to me is that what is in al-Bada'i' that its place is specifically the first two rak'ahs intended designation by way of obligation (wujub), not fard. And what some said that its place is two rak'ahs unspecified, what is meant is that designation of the first two is better. This is what will come from Ghayat al-Bayan. So there are only two views, not three. This is supported by what was mentioned in Sharh Ibn Amir Hajj on al-Munya when mentioning the obligations of prayer, where he said: In Sharh al-Tahawi for al-Ispijabi, he said: Our companions said: Recitation is fard in two rak'ahs without specifying them, and the best is in the first two. Al-Quduri also inclined to this. But in al-Tuhfa and al-Bada'i', it is stated that the correct position of our school is that the place of obligatory recitation is specifically the first two rak'ahs. The original work indicated this where it said: If he leaves recitation in the first two, he makes it up in the last two. This is followed in al-Dhakhira and al-Muhit al-Radawi and others. Then he mentioned in Sharh al-Munya when discussing the obligatory elements of prayer that the fruit of the disagreement is in the obligation of sajda sahw or not if he leaves recitation in the first two or
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether the obligatory recitation (qira'ah) in prayer is specifically required in the first two rak'ahs (the opinion authenticated in al-Bada'i' and preferred by many later scholars) or may be performed in any two rak'ahs (the opinion of some Hanafis, including al-Quduri). The disagreement revolves around the nature of the requirement: is it fard (obligatory) to recite in the first two rak'ahs specifically, or is it merely wajib? The practical consequence (thamara) is seen in the cause of the sajda sahw when one mistakenly recites only in the last two rak'ahs. According to the first view, the sajda sahw is required because the fard has been moved from its proper place, and the recitation in the last two is considered a make-up (qada) for the missed recitation in the first two. According to the second view, the sajda sahw is also required, but because a wajib (the designation) was omitted, and the recitation in the last two is considered proper performance (ada), not a make-up. The author then addresses a doubt: if recitation in the first two is fard, why does the school not rule the prayer invalid if omitted? He explains that this fard is 'practical fard' (fard 'amali), meaning it is certain in practice but speculative in evidence, so out of precaution, the prayer is not invalidated. He concludes that there are only two views, not three, and that the preferred view (mufta bihi) is that the first two rak'ahs are specifically designated for recitation as a wajib, not fard. He supports this by citing earlier Hanafi authorities.

Key Terms
فرض عملي (fard amali): A ruling that is certain in practice (cutth) but based on speculative evidence (zanni), making it function like a fard in terms of implementation but not as strong as a theoretical fard; omission does not invalidate the act but may require compensation.
سجود السهو (sajdat al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for mistakes (sahw) in prayer, such as omission or delay of a wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the authenticated view in al-Bada'i', if a person forgetfully recites only in the last two rak'ahs of the Fajr prayer, what is the ruling regarding the sajda sahw?
A) No sajda sahw is required because the prayer is incomplete and must be repeated.
B) Sajda sahw is required because the fard of recitation was changed from its place.
C) Sajda sahw is required because a wajib (the designation) was omitted.
D) Sajda sahw is not required because the recitation was performed in two rak'ahs.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon position is that the first two rak'ahs are specifically designated for recitation as a wajib (or practical fard), and omitting this forgetfully requires sajda sahw but does not invalidate the prayer.

Salah — Prayer
advanced
8 min
The Specific Place of Obligatory Recitation in Fard Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qira'ah placement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on where qira'ah is wajib in fard prayer, explain the practical difference in the cause of sajdah al-sahw, and identify which position is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Prayer is valid even if you recite in the last two, but sajdah al-sahw is required—the dispute is over why.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq probes a subtle intra-Hanafi disagreement: is the obligatory recitation tied specifically to the first two rak'ahs, or merely required in any two? Though both sides agree on the prayer's validity and the need for sajdah al-sahw if omitted from the first two, they differ on the cause—and that difference reveals the Hanafi school's sophisticated hierarchy of obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the common ground
Both positions agree that if a person forgets to recite in the first two rak'ahs and recites in the last two, the prayer is valid and sajdah al-sahw is required. This is the shared foundation.
The dispute does not affect validity—only the reason for sajdah.
2
State the two positions
Position 1 (mufta bihi): Qira'ah is specifically wajib in the first two rak'ahs. Position 2: Qira'ah is wajib in any two rak'ahs, with the first two being preferred. Understand the exact wording of each.
The author clarifies there are only two opinions, not three.
3
Focus on the practical difference
The difference appears in the cause of sajdah al-sahw. On the first view, it is because one delayed the wajib from its place (ta'khir al-wajib 'an mahallihi). On the second, it is because one left a wajib (tark al-wajib). The recitation in the last two is qada' (make-up) on the first view, and ada' (performance) on the second.
Also, the level of sin differs: the first view involves a stronger breach (leaving a fard 'amali).
4
Analyze the author's resolution and tarjih
Ibn Nujaym defends the view that specification is by wujub (obligation) not iftiraḍ (pillar-level). He cites al-Bada'i', al-Tuhfah, al-Asl, and others to show the mufta bihi is that qira'ah is specifically wajib in the first two.
The author resolves a doubt: if it were fard in the first two, omission would invalidate the prayer. But it is fard 'amali, not fard qat'i—its omission does not invalidate but requires compensation.
5
Connect to the broader Hanafi usul distinction
The Hanafi school uniquely differentiates between fard (pillar, rukn) and wajib (obligatory but not a pillar). Qira'ah is wajib, not fard. This lesson illustrates how the school applies this distinction to derive specific rulings.
This distinction is a hallmark of Hanafi fiqh.

فيه بحث لأنها وإن لم تكن في محلها حقيقة لكنها في حكمها لالتحاقها بالأوليين فلا تتغير بقصده بدليل وجوب القراءة على الخليفة المسبوق لو أشار إليه الإمام أنه لم يقرأ في الأوليين فقد صرحوا بأنه إذا قرأ التحقت بالأوليين فخلت الأخريان عن القراءة فيلزمه القراءة فيما سبق به أيضاً، وبدليل عدم صحة اقتداء مسافر في الوقت بمقيم لم يقرأ في الأوليين وبدليل وجوب القراءة على المسبوق وإن لم يقرأ إمامه في الأوليين، والظاهر في توجيهه أنه مبني على القول بفرضية القراءة في الأوليين
Furthermore, despite their agreement that if he only recited in the last two rak'ahs, the prayer is valid and that he must perform sajdah al-sahw if he was forgetful according to both mentioned opinions, the benefit of the difference is only in the cause of sajdah al-sahw. According to the corrected view, its cause is changing the obligatory act from its place, and his recitation in the last two is a make-up for his recitation in the first two. According to the other view, its cause is leaving an obligatory act, and his recitation in the last two is performance, not make-up, and the matter is easy. And what is in Ghayat al-Bayan that specifying recitation in the first two is better—if he wishes he recites in them, if he wishes he recites in the last two, or in one of the first two and one of the last two—is weak because the great multitude explicitly state obligation in the first two, not preference. Rather, recitation was obligatory in two rak'ahs due to His statement: 'Recite what is easy from the Quran' (al-Muzzammil 20), which does not require repetition, so its implication is that it is obligatory in one rak'ah except that... Some said the other view) gives the impression that it is another opinion besides the two previous, while it is exactly the first one expressed as the well-known view. His saying: (So the benefit of the difference etc.) Al-Nahr said: But in the chapter on forgetfulness, it will come that delaying the obligatory act also constitutes leaving an obligatory act. It is possible that the difference appears in the levels of sin: according to the first, he sins the sin of one who leaves an obligatory act; according to the second, he sins the sin of one who leaves a practical obligatory act which is stronger among the two types of obligatory acts according to its verification. End. I say: I have a doubt that perplexed me: there is no disagreement among us regarding the obligation of recitation in prayer; the disagreement is only in specifying its location. Accordingly, the meaning of the view corrected in al-Bada'i' is that recitation is obligatory and being in the first two is another obligation. The implication of this is the invalidation of prayer by leaving it in the first two and not considering it as make-up in the last two because if he recites in the last two, he has performed the obligatory recitation. As for the obligation of its being in the first two, it has been missed and cannot be compensated, just as if he performed the opening takbir after recitation and did not recite after it. This is not like delaying a prostration to the end of the prayer, for although it involves delaying an obligatory act, not delaying is not obligatory but rather required. Our case is an obligation, and its being a practical obligation does not imply non-invalidation because it is something whose loss voids validity, like wiping the head. So it is in the strength of certainty in practice as mentioned at the beginning of the book; unless it is said that although it is in the strength of certainty, it is speculative, and the implication of leaving it is corruption, but it was not ruled as such out of caution because it is a jurisprudential detail subject to ijtihad, similar to what will come in the eight issues in extrapolating the statement of the Imam. Contemplate. What appears to me is that what is in al-Bada'i' that its place is specifically the first two rak'ahs—he intended specification by way of obligation (wujub), not obligation (iftirad). And what some said that its place is two rak'ahs without specification—his intention is that specifying the first two is better, which is what will come from Ghayat al-Bayan. So in this issue there are two opinions, not three. Evidence of that is what was mentioned in Sharh Ibn Amir Hajj 'ala al-Munya when mentioning the obligatory acts of prayer, where he said: 'In Sharh al-Tahawi li'l-Asbijabi, our companions said: Recitation is obligatory in two rak'ahs without specification of them, and the best is in the first two. Al-Quduri also held this, but in al-Tuhfah and al-Bada'i' it is stated that the correct view of our school is that the place of obligatory recitation is specifically the first two rak'ahs, and the original text referred to it where he said: If he leaves recitation in the first two, he makes it up in the last two. Al-Dhakhirah, al-Muhit al-Radawi, and others followed it. Then he mentioned in Sharh al-Munya under the obligatory acts of prayer that the fruit of the difference is the obligation or non-obligation of sajdah al-sahw if he leaves it in the first two or one of them: on the view of obligation, it is due to delaying the obligatory act from its place forgetfully; on the view of sunnah, no.' End. This is explicit in what we said. His saying: (obligation) in both (by indication) is not hidden what is in it. The better is to say: obligation in the second by indication. His saying: (because the certain etc.) Calling it certain contradicts what he first stated that it is a practical obligation, and this is not certain; rather it is speculative. Yes, it is in the strength of the certain in practice as previously. His saying: (and its reasoning that recitation etc.) There is discussion in it because although it is not in its place in reality, it is in its ruling due to its attachment to the first two, so it does not change by his intention. Evidence: the obligation of recitation on the successor who is led if the imam indicated to him that he did not recite in the first two—they explicitly state that if he recites, it attaches to the first two, so the last two become empty of recitation and he must recite in what preceded. And evidence: the invalidity of a traveler's following a resident who did not recite in the first two during the time of prayer. And evidence: the obligation of recitation on the person led even if his imam did not recite in the first two. The apparent explanation is that it is based on the view of the obligation of recitation in the first two.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the specific placement of the obligatory recitation (qira'ah) in fard prayer. The author, Ibn Nujaym, is commenting on the text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq and analyzing different positions within the Hanafi school. The core issue is whether the obligatory recitation is specifically required in the first two rak'ahs of a fard prayer, or whether it is required in any two rak'ahs, with the first two being preferred. Both agreed-upon positions maintain that if one omits recitation in the first two rak'ahs and recites in the last two, the prayer is valid but sajdah al-sahw is required. The difference lies in the reason for the sajdah: according to the corrected view (that recitation is specifically fard in the first two), the cause is changing the obligatory act from its place, and the recitation in the last two is a make-up (qada'). According to the other view (that recitation is fard in any two), the cause is leaving an obligatory act (wajib), and the recitation in the last two is performance (ada') rather than make-up. The author then presents a doubt: if recitation is fard in the first two specifically, then omitting it would invalidate the prayer, yet the school holds it valid. He resolves this by suggesting that the phrase 'specifically' in al-Bada'i' actually indicates wujub (obligatory but not fard in the strongest sense), and that the difference is really about whether it is fard 'amali (practical obligation) or fard qat'i. The practical consequence is the type of sin and the cause of sajdah. The author concludes that there are only two opinions, not three, as some sources claim. He supports this by citing multiple authorities. The passage ends with a discussion of evidence from the Quran and Hadith, and a refutation of a view from Ghayat al-Bayan that specification is merely preferred. The overall analysis shows the depth of Hanafi usul al-fiqh in determining the precise nature of obligations.

Key Terms
القراءة المفروضة (al-qira'ah al-mafrudah): The recitation of Quran that is obligatory (fard/wajib) in prayer. The text discusses whether it is specifically in the first two rak'ahs or general in two rak'ahs.
الركعتان الأوليان (al-rak'atan al-awwaliyan): The first two rak'ahs of a fard prayer. The disputed issue is whether the obligatory recitation is specifically confined to these two or applies to any two.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for errors in prayer, such as omitting a wajib or delaying a fard.
فرض عملي (fard 'amali): A practical obligation — an obligation that is treated as fard in practice (e.g., omission requires compensation) but is not a pillar in the strongest sense. In this context, qira'ah in the first two is called fard 'amali.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the corrected view (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, what is the cause of sajdah al-sahw if one omits qira'ah in the first two rak'ahs and recites in the last two?
A) Delaying the obligatory act from its place, making recitation in the last two a make-up (qada').
B) Leaving a wajib entirely, making recitation in the last two a performance (ada').
C) Omitting a sunnah, requiring no sajdah.
D) Invalidating the prayer, requiring repetition.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the obligatory recitation in fard prayer is specifically wajib in the first two rak'ahs; omitting it there does not invalidate the prayer but necessitates sajdah al-sahw.

Obligatory Recitation in Nafil and Witr
Ruling that qira'ah is fard in every rak'ah of nafil and witr, with reasoning and exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that recitation is fard in every rak'ah of nafil and witr, explain the qiyas reasoning, and identify the exception for four-rak'ah sunnah prayers.

Core Idea
Recitation is fard in every rak'ah of nafil and witr because each nafil pair is a separate prayer.

In this passage from al-Hidayah and Fath al-Qadir, we learn that in supererogatory (nafil) and witr prayers, recitation of the Quran is obligatory in every single rak'ah. This is different from obligatory prayers where recitation is only fard in two rak'ahs. The reason lies in the nature of nafil prayers: each pair of rak'ahs is considered an independent prayer unit. We will unpack this analogy and also learn an important exception for certain four-rak'ah sunnah prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage states that in every nafil (supererogatory) and witr prayer, recitation (qira'ah) is fard (obligatory) in all rak'ahs. Note that this is the general rule.
In fard (obligatory) prayers, recitation is fard only in two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is based on analogy (qiyas). The author explains that each pair (shaf') of nafil is a separate prayer by itself. Standing for the third rak'ah is like starting a new prayer with a new takbir (tahrimah).
This is the well-known (mashhur) view of the Hanafi companions.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Since the first takbir only obligates two rak'ahs, the third rak'ah requires a new intention, hence recitation becomes necessary. Evidence: one performs the opening supplication (istiftah) at the beginning of the third rak'ah.
This shows that the third rak'ah is treated as the start of a new prayer unit.
4
Identify the exception
The author notes that this analogy does not hold for four-rak'ah sunnah prayers (e.g., the sunnah before Zuhr). In these prayers, the entire four rak'ahs are one continuous prayer; standing to the third is not a new takbir. Thus, one does not recite istiftah in the third rak'ah, nor send blessings in the first sitting.
Recitation is still fard in all rak'ahs, but the prayer is a single unit.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: In nafil and witr, each rak'ah must have recitation, and the prayer is structured in pairs. In four-rak'ah sunnah prayers, recitation is required in every rak'ah, but the prayer is performed as a single unit without extra supplications in the middle.
This distinction affects how one prays and what is considered valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكل النفل والوتر) أي القراءة فرض في جميع ركعات النفل والوتر، أما النفل فلأن كل شفع منه صلاة على حدة والقيام إلى الثالثة كتحريمة مبتدأة ولهذا لا يجب بالتحريمة الأولى إلا ركعتان في المشهور عن أصحابنا، ولهذا قالوا : يستفتح في الثالثة وأما الوتر فللاحتياط كذا في الهداية. وزاد في فتح القدير ويصلي على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في كل قعدة، وقياسه أن يتعوذ في كل شفع انتهى . إلا أنه لا يتم لأنه لا يشمل السنة الرباعية المؤكدة كسنة الظهر القبلية فإن القراءة فرض في جميع ركعاتها مع أن القيام إلى الثالثة ليس كتحريمة مبتدأة بل هي واحدة ولهذا لا يستفتح في الشفع الثاني ولا يصلي في القعدة الأولى ولا يبطل خيارها بقيامها
And every nafil and witr: meaning recitation is obligatory in all rak'ahs of nafil and witr. As for nafil, because every pair of it is a separate prayer, and standing to the third is like an initiating takbir, and therefore only two rak'ahs are obligatory by the first takbir according to the well-known view of our companions, and therefore they said: one makes the opening supplication (istiftah) in the third. As for witr, out of caution, as in al-Hidayah. In Fath al-Qadir, he added: and he sends blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) in every sitting, and by analogy he should seek refuge (ta'awwudh) in every pair. End. However, it is not complete because it does not include the emphasized four-rak'ah sunnah, like the sunnah before Zuhr, for recitation is obligatory in all its rak'ahs even though standing to the third is not like an initiating takbir, but rather it is one (prayer), and therefore one does not make istiftah in the second pair nor send blessings in the first sitting, and its choice is not invalidated by its standing.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that in nafil (supererogatory) prayers and witr, recitation (qira'ah) is obligatory (fard) in every rak'ah. The reason given for nafil prayers is that each pair (shaf') is considered a separate prayer. When one stands for the third rak'ah, it is like a new initiation (tahrimah). Therefore, the first takbir only obligates two rak'ahs; for the third, a new intention is formed, necessitating recitation. This is the well-known (mashhur) view. For witr, it is out of caution (ihtiyat). The author cites al-Hidayah as the source. Then he adds a commentary from Fath al-Qadir: that in every sitting (qa'dah), one should send blessings upon the Prophet, and by analogy (qiyas) one should seek refuge (ta'awwudh) in every pair. However, the author notes that this analogy does not hold completely because it does not include the four-rak'ah emphasized sunnah (like the sunnah before Zuhr). In such prayers, although there are four rak'ahs, they are one single prayer; therefore, one does not perform istiftah in the second pair nor send blessings in the first sitting, and the option (khiyar) to break the prayer is not lost by standing. This shows an exception to the general rule for certain recommended prayers.

Key Terms
النفل (al-nafl): Supererogatory prayers that are not obligatory. In this context, it includes all voluntary prayers.
الوتر (al-witr): The witr prayer, which is wajib (obligatory) according to Abu Hanifa, and sunnah mu'akkadah according to the two companions.
شفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs in nafil prayer. Each pair is considered a separate prayer unit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is recitation obligatory in every rak'ah of nafil prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the Quran commands recitation in every rak'ah without exception.
B) Because each pair of nafil is a separate prayer, and standing to the third is like a new takbir.
C) Because the Prophet recited in every rak'ah of nafil.
D) Because it is a sunnah mu'akkadah to recite in every rak'ah.

Key Takeaway
Recitation is fard in every rak'ah of nafil and witr; however, the four-rak'ah emphasized sunnah prayers are an exception where the prayer is one continuous unit.

Recitation in the Last Two Rak'ahs: Wajib or Sunnah?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on recitation in the last two rak'ahs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on recitation in the last two rak'ahs of fard prayer, distinguish between the relied-upon view and the minority view, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Recitation in the last two rak'ahs of fard is sunnah, not wajib, per the relied-upon Hanafi position.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute: is recitation of Quran in the last two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah obligatory prayer wajib or merely sunnah? The relied-upon position (al-sahih min al-madhhab) holds it is sunnah, but a minority narration from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad considers it wajib. We will trace the evidence, the role of Companion practice, and the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) for the validity of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
State the precise question: Is recitation (qira'ah) in the last two rak'ahs (ukhrayn) of a fard prayer wajib or not? Note that this dispute is internal to the Hanafi school.
The first two rak'ahs are agreed upon as obligatory for recitation.
2
Examine the evidence for obligation
Review the primary proof: the hadith of al-musi' salatahu, where the Prophet (ﷺ) commanded recitation in every rak'ah ('Then do that in all your prayer'). Understand why this command appears to indicate obligation.
This hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Analyze the factor diverting the command
Consider the Hanafi response: the practice of the Companions, specifically the report from Ali and Ibn Mas'ud that they recited only in the first two rak'ahs and glorified (tasbih) in the last two. This practice diverts (sarf) the command from obligation to recommendation.
The investigator in Fath al-Qadir noted that this diversion is valid only if no contrary Companion report exists.
4
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Identify the two positions: (1) Zahir al-riwayah: recitation in the last two is not wajib (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). (2) Narration from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad (Nawadir): it is wajib. Determine the mufta bihi and the cautious (ihtiyat) view.
The mufta bihi is non-obligation; some later scholars recommend reciting out of caution.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Work out the practical consequence: if one omits recitation in the last two rak'ahs, according to the relied-upon position, the prayer is valid and no sajdah al-sahw is required. According to the minority view, sajdah al-sahw would be needed.
This is a clear example of how a difference in usul leads to a difference in furu'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب الوتر والنوافل ۹۹ رواية الثانية اعتبرت شرعاً كالأولى، فإيجاب القراءة فيها إيجاب فيهما دلالة. وأما قوله عليه السلام في حديث المسيء صلاته «ثم اقرأ ما تيسر معك من القرآن» ثم قال في آخره «ثم افعل ذلك في صلاتك كلها فلا يثبت به الفرض لأن القطعي لا يثبت بالظني. وإنما لم تكن القراءة في الأخريين واجبة في الفرض كما هو الصحيح من المذهب مع وجود الأمر المذكور المقضي للوجوب لوجود صارف له عنه وهو قول الصحابة على خلافه كما رواه ابن أبي شيبة عن على وابن مسعود قال: «اقرأ في الأوليين وسبح في الأخريين لكن ذكر المحقق في فتح القدير أنه يصلح صارفاً إلا إذا لم يرد عن غيرهما من الصحابة خلاف وإلا فاختلافهم في الوجوب لا يصرف دليل الوجوب عنه، فالأحوط رواية الحسن رحمه الله بالوجوب في الأخريين انتهى . وقد يقال : إن مقتضاه لزوم قراءة ما تيسر في الأخريين وجوباً لا تعيين الفاتحة كما هو الحسن فليس موافقاً لكل من الروايتين. وفي القنية : لم يقرأ في الأوليين وقرأ في الأخريين في الصلاة على قصد الثناء والدعاء لا يجزئه انتهى. مع أن المنقول في التجنيس أنه إذا قرأ الفاتحة في الصلاة على قصد الثناء جازت صلاته لأنه وجدت القراءة في محلها فلا يتغير حكمها بقصده، وهكذا في الظهيرية. ثم ذكر بعده ما في القنية عن شمس الأئمة الحلواني القراءة ليست في محلها فتغيرت بقصده كما يشير إليه تعليله في التجنيس قوله : (وكل النفل والوتر)
The book of prayer, chapter of witr and supererogatory prayers. The second rak'ah is considered legally like the first, so making recitation obligatory in it implies it is obligatory in both. As for his saying, peace be upon him, in the hadith of the one who prayed badly: 'Then recite what is easy for you from the Quran', then he said at the end: 'Then do that in all of your prayer.' So it does not establish obligation because what is certain cannot be established by what is probable. Recitation in the last two rak'ahs is not obligatory in the obligatory prayer as is the correct position of the school, despite the existence of the aforementioned command indicating obligation, because there is a factor diverting it from obligation, namely the saying of the Companions to the contrary, as reported by Ibn Abi Shaybah from 'Ali and Ibn Mas'ud: 'Recite in the first two and glorify in the last two.' But the investigator in Fath al-Qadir said that it is valid as a diverting factor only if no contrary report from other Companions exists; otherwise, their disagreement about obligation does not divert the evidence of obligation. So the more cautious is the narration of al-Hasan, may Allah have mercy on him, of obligation in the last two. End. It may be said that its requirement is the obligation to recite what is easy in the last two, not specifying al-Fatihah as in al-Hasan's view, so it does not agree with both narrations. In al-Qunyah: If one did not recite in the first two and recited in the last two with the intention of praise and supplication, it does not suffice him. End. Even though it is transmitted in al-Tajnis that if one recited al-Fatihah in prayer with the intention of praise, his prayer is valid because recitation occurred in its place, so its ruling does not change by his intention. Similarly in al-Zahiriyyah. Then he mentioned after it what is in al-Qunyah from Shams al-A'immah al-Halwani: recitation is not in its place, so it changes by his intention, as indicated by his reasoning in al-Tajnis. His saying: (And all nafl and witr).
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling of recitation (qira'ah) in the last two rak'ahs of the obligatory (fard) prayer. The author of the sharh, Ibn Nujaym, explains the different positions. The relied-upon position (al-sahih min al-madhhab) is that recitation in the last two rak'ahs is not wajib but rather sunnah. However, there is a narration from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad (a Nawadir transmission) that it is wajib. The main evidence for obligation is the hadith of the one who prayed badly (al-musi' salatahu) where the Prophet (ﷺ) commanded recitation in every rak'ah. The Hanafis respond that this hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) and cannot establish an obligation against the stronger evidence of the Companions' practice, as reported from 'Ali and Ibn Mas'ud that they recited only in the first two rak'ahs and glorified in the last two. The investigator in Fath al-Qadir notes that if there is no contrary Companion report, the Saheeh position is that it is not wajib. The second part discusses the effect of intention: if one recites in the last two with the intention of praise (thana') and supplication (du'a'), does it suffice? According to al-Qunyah, it does not, because the recitation is not in its proper place. But according to al-Tajnis, if one recites al-Fatihah with that intention, it suffices because the recitation has taken place in its proper location (the prayer) and intention does not change its ruling. The passage ends by noting a difference of opinion between al-Halwani and al-Tajnis. Teachers should emphasize that the relied-upon Hanafi position is non-obligation, but the cautious view (al-ihtiyat) is to recite in all rak'ahs. The key distinction is between the obligatory (fard) and supererogatory (nafl) prayers: in fard, only the first two rak'ahs require recitation; in nafl and witr, recitation is fard in every rak'ah (as will be explained in the next lesson).

Key Terms
القراءة (al-qira'ah): Recitation of Quranic verses in prayer; specifically here whether it is required in every rak'ah or only in the first two of fard.
الأخريين (al-ukhrayn): The last two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah obligatory prayer (e.g., Zuhr, 'Asr, 'Isha').
المذهب (al-madhhab): The established and relied-upon position of the Hanafi school (as opposed to a weak or rare narration).
الصارف (al-sarif): The factor that diverts a linguistic command from its apparent meaning (obligation) to another meaning (recommendation).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is fard, and omitting it invalidates the prayer.
B) It is wajib, and omitting it requires sajdah al-sahw.
C) It is sunnah, and the prayer is valid without it.
D) It is haram to recite in the last two rak'ahs.

Key Takeaway
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, recitation in the last two rak'ahs of fard is sunnah, not wajib, due to the Companions' practice diverting the general command.

Recitation in Nafl and Witr is Fard in Every Rak'ah
States and explains the ruling that recitation is fard in all rak'ahs of nafl and witr prayers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recitation in nafl and witr prayers and explain the reasoning based on the independent nature of each pair (shaf').

Core Idea
In nafl and witr, each pair is an independent prayer, making recitation fard in every rak'ah.

This lesson examines the ruling that recitation (qira'ah) is an obligatory component (fard) in every rak'ah of nafl (supererogatory) and witr prayers. While in fard prayers only the first two rak'ahs require recitation, the Hanafi school extends this obligation to all rak'ahs of nafl and witr due to the unique structure of these prayers. The key proof lies in the principle that each pair of nafl constitutes a separate prayer, so standing for the third rak'ah is akin to initiating a new prayer, necessitating recitation anew.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
State clearly what act is being ruled upon and what the ruling is. The act is recitation during the prayer (qira'ah) in the specific context of nafl and witr prayers. The ruling is that it is fard (obligatory) in every rak'ah of these prayers.
This is distinct from fard prayers where recitation is only fard in the first two rak'ahs.
2
Locate the Dalil (Proof)
Identify the proof the Hanafi school uses for this ruling. The proof is not a direct textual command but a qiyas (analogy) based on the nature of nafl: each pair (shaf') of nafl is an independent prayer. Therefore, when one stands for the third rak'ah, it is like making a new takbir tahrimah (opening declaration), which requires its own recitation.
This reasoning is explicitly stated in al-Hidayah and Fath al-Qadir.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah (Legal Link)
Explain how the proof leads to the ruling. The key insight: in nafl, only two rak'ahs are obligated by the first takbir. Standing for the third is a new beginning (tahrimah mubtada'ah), so each pair must have its own recitation. For witr, the ruling is based on caution (ihtiyat) due to its connection to 'Isha and its status as wajib.
The intention is to maintain the integrity of each independent prayer unit.
4
Note the Exception
The commentator notes an exception: the emphatic four-rak'ah sunnah (e.g., sunnah of Zuhr before fard) also has recitation fard in all rak'ahs, but its structure is not based on independent pairs; it is one continuous prayer. Therefore, the reasoning differs even though the ruling is the same.
This shows a nuanced application: the ruling is uniform, but the underlying principle varies.
5
Evaluate the Practical Impact
Understand the consequence of omitting recitation in any rak'ah of nafl or witr. Since recitation is a rukn (pillar), intentional or mistaken omission invalidates that rak'ah and the entire prayer if not corrected by sajdah al-sahw or repeating.
This is a critical difference from fard prayers where omitting recitation in the later rak'ahs does not invalidate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وكل النفل والوتر) أي القراءة فرض في جميع ركعات النفل والوتر، أما النفل فلأن كل شفع منه صلاة على حدة والقيام إلى الثالثة كتحريمة مبتدأة ولهذا لا يجب بالتحريمة الأولى إلا ركعتان في المشهور عن أصحابنا، ولهذا قالوا : يستفتح في الثالثة وأما الوتر فللاحتياط كذا في الهداية. وزاد في فتح القدير ويصلي على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في كل قعدة، وقياسه أن يتعوذ في كل شفع انتهى . إلا أنه لا يتم لأنه لا يشمل السنة الرباعية المؤكدة كسنة الظهر القبلية فإن القراءة فرض في جميع ركعاتها مع أن القيام إلى الثالثة ليس كتحريمة مبتدأة بل هي واحدة ولهذا لا يستفتح في الشفع الثاني ولا يصلي في القعدة الأولى ولا يبطل خيارها بقيامها الفاتحة أن ووجهه صلاة ملخصاً. إحداهما فيجب على القول بالوجوب بتأخير الواجب عن محله سهواً وعلى السنية لا ا هـ . وهو كالصريح فيما قلنا قوله : إيجاب) فيهما (دلالة) لا يخفي ما فيه والأولى أن يقال : إيجاب في الثانية دلالة قوله : (لأن القطعي الخ) تسميته قطعياً مخالف لما صرح به أولاً أنه فرض عملي وهذا ليس بقطعي، وإنما هو ظني، نعم هو في قوة القطعي في العمل كما مر قوله : (ووجهه إن القراءة الخ) فيه بحث لأنها وإن لم تكن في محلها حقيقة لكنها في حكمها لالتحاقها بالأوليين فلا تتغير بقصده بدليل وجوب القراءة على الخليفة المسبوق لو أشار إليه الإمام أنه لم يقرأ في الأوليين فقد صرحوا بأنه إذا قرأ التحقت بالأوليين فخلت الأخريان عن القراءة فيلزمه القراءة فيما سبق به أيضاً، وبدليل عدم صحة اقتداء مسافر في الوقت بمقيم لم يقرأ في الأوليين وبدليل وجوب القراءة على المسبوق وإن لم يقرأ إمامه في الأوليين، والظاهر في توجيهه أنه مبني على القول بفرضية القراءة في الأوليين، ثم عند الغروب والطلوع وقضى ركعتين لو نوى أربعاً وأفسده بعد القعود الأول أو قبله فيها إلى الشفع الثاني، وإن أريد بالنفل في كلامهم ما ليس سنة مؤكدة لم يتم أيضاً لخلوه عن إفادة حكم القراءة في السنة المؤكدة. وإنما لم تكن القعدة على رأس كل شفع فرضاً كما هو قول محمد وهو القياس لأنها فرض للخروج من الصلاة فإذا قام إلى الثالثة تبين أن ما قبلها لم يكن أوان الخروج من الصلاة فلم تبق القعدة فريضة بخلاف القراءة فإنها ركن مقصود بنفسه فإذا تركه تفسد صلاته
His saying: (And all nafl and witr) meaning: recitation is fard in all rak'ahs of nafl and witr. As for nafl, because each pair (shaf') of it is a prayer by itself, and standing for the third is like a new takbir beginning (tahrimah mubtada'ah). For this reason, only two rak'ahs are obligatory by the first tahrimah according to the well-known position of our companions, and for this they said: one performs the opening supplication (istiftah) in the third. As for witr, it is for caution (ihtiyat). This is in al-Hidayah. And he added in Fath al-Qadir: and one sends blessings on the Prophet (ﷺ) in every sitting (qa'dah), and by analogy, one should seek refuge (ta'awwudh) in every pair. End. Except that it is not complete because it does not include the emphatic four-rak'ah sunnah like the before-noon sunnah of Zuhr, for recitation is fard in all its rak'ahs even though standing for the third is not like a new tahrimah, but rather it is one, and for this reason one does not perform istiftah in the second pair, nor does one send blessings in the first sitting, nor does the option of a woman break by her standing...
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This ruling statement and its proof establish that in nafl (supererogatory) and witr prayers, recitation (qira'ah) is fard (obligatory) in every rak'ah. The commentator, Ibn Nujaym, explains the reasoning: In nafl, each pair (shaf') of rak'ahs is considered an independent prayer. Therefore, standing for the third rak'ah is like beginning a new prayer (tahrimah mubtada'ah). Consequently, only two rak'ahs are obligated by the first takbir al-tahrimah, and one recites the opening supplication (istiftah) again in the third rak'ah. This is the well-known (mashhur) position of the Hanafi school. For witr, the obligation of recitation in all rak'ahs is based on caution (ihtiyat) due to its connection with the 'Isha prayer and its status as a confirmed sunnah. The passage then discusses an objection: The emphatic four-rak'ah sunnah (e.g., sunnah of Zuhr before the fard) has recitation fard in all rak'ahs, yet standing for the third is not like a new tahrimah. The commentator notes that this objection is incomplete because the ruling for that sunnah is based on it being a single prayer, not two independent pairs. The key principle: qira'ah is a rukn (pillar) in its own right, unlike qa'dah (sitting), which is only fard for exiting the prayer. If one omits qira'ah, the prayer is invalid (fasid) because it is a rukn. Teachers should highlight the distinction between fard and nafl: in fard, only the first two rak'ahs require qira'ah as fard; in nafl, every rak'ah requires it.

Key Terms
النفل (al-nafl): Supererogatory prayer, including optional and sunnah prayers, whether confirmed (sunnah mu'akkadah) or not. In this passage, the ruling for recitation applies to all types except the emphatic four-rak'ah sunnah as noted.
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer (usually 3 rak'ahs) performed after 'Isha. In the Hanafi school, it is wajib according to some, but here it is treated as part of the discussion; recitation is fard in all its rak'ahs.
الشفع (al-shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs. In the Hanafi concept of nafl, each pair (shaf') is considered an independent prayer unit, even if multiple pairs are prayed consecutively.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is recitation (qira'ah) considered fard in every rak'ah of a nafl prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because of a specific verse in the Quran that commands recitation in every rak'ah.
B) Because each pair (shaf') of nafl is an independent prayer, so standing for the third is like a new prayer.
C) Because the Prophet (ﷺ) always recited in every rak'ah of nafl.
D) Because nafl prayers are always shorter than fard prayers.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, recitation is a rukn in every rak'ah of nafl and witr because each pair of nafl is an independent prayer and witr requires caution.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Nafl Becomes Binding Upon Commencement: The Proof from Quran
Explains the binding nature of commenced nafl prayer and the Quranic proof from Surah Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a commenced nafl prayer becomes wajib and derive it from the Quranic verse (Muhammad: 33).

Core Idea
Once you start a nafl prayer, it becomes wajib to complete it — breaking it is haram and requires qada.

This lesson dives into a core principle of Hanafi fiqh: that a voluntary act of worship, once commenced, becomes binding. We explore the Quranic basis for this ruling and its implications for prayer and fasting. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq establishes that commencement (shuru') in a nafl prayer or fast creates a legal obligation to see it through, and the Quranic prohibition of invalidating deeds is the primary evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the opening statement: 'And nafl becomes binding with commencement.' What does the author assert about the effect of starting a nafl prayer?
The ruling applies to both prayer and fasting according to some commentators, but the context primarily addresses prayer.
2
Locate the Dalil
Find the Quranic verse quoted: 'Do not invalidate your deeds' (Surah Muhammad: 33). Why is this verse relevant?
This is a direct textual proof (dalil naqli) from the Quran.
3
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah
Understand how the verse proves the obligation. The author argues that avoiding invalidation of a deed that cannot be divided into parts requires completion of the act. Thus, once started, the prayer must be completed to avoid invalidating it.
The dalala is zanni (probable) because the verse is general and may be specified, but Hanafi usul treats it as binding here.
4
Note the Hanafi Consensus
Observe that the passage states 'our companions have agreed on the obligation of qada in spoiling prayer and fasting.' This refers to the three main Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad).
There is no intra-madhhab dispute on this principle for prayer; the difference arises only for fasting in certain cases.
5
Apply the Consequences
Determine the legal outcome if a person intentionally breaks a nafl prayer without a valid excuse: it is haram and requires qada (making up the prayer).
Valid excuses like menstruation or life-threatening necessity permit breaking without sin, but qada is still required.

الإفساد لعذر فيهما وأنه لا يحل الإفساد في الصلاة لغير عذر. واختلفوا في إباحته في الصوم لغير عذر ففي ظاهر الرواية لا يباح، وفي رواية المنتقي يباح كما سيأتي في الصوم. وقوله ولو عند الغروب بيان لكونه لازماً له إذا شرع فيه في وقت مكروه وهو ظاهر الرواية، فإذا أفسده لزمه قضاؤه بخلاف الصوم إذا شرع في وقت مكروه فإنه لا قضاء عليه بالإفساد وسيأتي الفرق إن شاء الله تعالى في الصوم. وفي البدائع: وعندنا الأفضل أن يقطعها وإن أتم فقد أساء ولا قضاء عليه لأنه أداها كما وجبت، فإذا قطعها لزمه القضاء انتهى. وينبغي أن يكون القطع واجباً خروجاً عن المكروه تحريماً وليس بإبطال للعمل لأنه إبطال ليؤديه على وجه أكمل فلا يعد إبطالاً، ولو قضاه استعجال رأيت العلامة الرملي نقل ذلك عن خط العلامة المقدسي فتدبر لكن قد علمت ما فيه قوله : (إلا أنه لا يتم الخ) قد يجاب بأنهم اعتبروا والمؤكدة صلاة واحدة في حق القراءة فقط احتياطاً كما في الوتر فإنهم أوجبوا القراة في جميع ركعاته احتياطاً كما مر لاحتمال كونه سنة مؤكدة قوله: (ولا يبطل خيارها الخ) أي خيار المرأة التي قال لها زوجها اختاري نفسك وهي في سنة الظهر القبلية ولا في العمرة على ما يعلم . من الزيلعي ا هـ . والظاهر تخصيص الصلاة فقط لأن المقام لها ولأنه ينبو عن الصوم قول المصنف ولو عند الغروب والطلوع كما لا يخفى هذا، وإنما لم يذكر الاستواء لأنه وقت ضيق لا يتأتى فيه أداء الصلاة كذا نقله بعضهم عن الشلبي وفيه أن الكلام في الشروع لا في الأداء ومدة الشروع يسيرة يمكن فيه فالأولى الجواب بأن تحري
His saying: (And nafl becomes binding with commencement) meaning: prayer or fasting, as al-'Ayni said. Then he objected in al-Nahr that it is premature and why not say Hajj? Some answered that it is a specification of what differs from al-Shafi'i, unlike Hajj where there is no disagreement. End from al-Zayla'i. The apparent view is to specify prayer only because the context is for it and because the author's phrase 'even at sunset and sunrise' does not apply to fasting. This is not hidden. He did not mention midday (istiwa') because it is a time too narrow for performing prayer, as some transmitted from al-Shalabi. But the discussion is about commencement, not performance, and the time of commencement is short and possible. So the better answer is... Explanation of what becomes obligatory on the servant by undertaking it: two types: what is obligatory by speech (nadhr) and what is obligatory by action (commencement of nafl). We begin with it following the book. We say: Indeed, invalidating an action is haram by the text: 'Do not invalidate your deeds' [Muhammad 33]. So it is necessary to complete it because avoiding invalidation of an action that does not admit of part-part description can only be by completion, because what was performed occurred as an act of worship, as evidenced by the fact that if he dies after the amount performed, he becomes rewarded. And our companions have agreed on the obligation of qada (making up) in spoiling prayer and fasting, whether with an excuse like menstruation during them or without an excuse. And that it is permissible to spoil them for an excuse in both, and that it is not permissible to spoil prayer without an excuse. And they differed on its permissibility in fasting without an excuse: in the zahir al-riwayah it is not permitted, and in the riwayah of al-Muntaqa it is permitted, as will come in fasting. His saying: 'even at sunset' is an explanation that it is binding on him if he starts in a disliked time, which is the apparent narration. So if he spoils it, he must make it up, unlike fasting if started in a disliked time, for which there is no qada upon spoiling. The difference will come, insha'Allah, in fasting. In al-Bada'i': In our view, it is better to break it, and if he completes it, he acts badly but there is no qada upon him because he performed it as it was obligatory. So if he breaks it, qada becomes necessary. End. It should be that breaking is obligatory to exit from the dislike (makruh tahrimi) and it is not considered invalidation of the action because it is invalidation to perform it in a more complete manner, so it is not considered invalidation. And if he makes it up hastily... I saw al-'Allamah al-Ramli narrate that from the handwriting of al-'Allamah al-Maqdisi, so ponder. But you know what is in it. His saying: 'Except that it is not complete...' It may be answered that they considered the emphatic sunnah as one prayer only in respect of recitation, as caution, like in witr, where they made recitation obligatory in all its rak'ahs out of caution as mentioned, due to the possibility of it being an emphatic sunnah. His saying: 'And her option is not invalidated...' meaning the option of the woman whose husband said to her 'choose yourself' while she was performing the before-noon sunnah of Zuhr. The author's saying: (And nafl becomes binding with commencement) meaning prayer or fasting, as al-'Ayni said. Then he objected...
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage discusses the principle that a nafl prayer becomes binding (lazim) once commenced. The author, Ibn Nujaym, explains that the avoidance of invalidating a righteous action is based on the Quranic verse 'Do not invalidate your deeds' (Muhammad: 33). Once a person begins a nafl prayer, it is obligatory to complete it, and breaking it is haram and requires qada (making up). The Hanafi school agrees on this for both prayer and fasting, with some differences: spoiling a nafl prayer for a valid excuse (e.g., menstruation) is permissible, but spoiling it without excuse is haram. For fasting, there is a difference: according to the zahir al-riwayah, it is not permissible to break a nafl fast without excuse; according to the riwayah of al-Muntaqa, it is permissible (as will be explained later). The passage also addresses a special case: if one starts a nafl prayer in a disliked time (e.g., at sunrise or sunset), the ruling is that it is binding and if one breaks it, qada is required. However, some authorities (al-Bada'i') suggest it is better to break it in such a case to avoid the disliked time; but if one completes it, it is valid but disliked. The passage ends with a discussion about whether the term 'nafl' includes only prayer or also fasting and Hajj. The preferred view is that it applies primarily to prayer because the context is about prayer and the phrase 'at sunset and sunrise' is specific to prayer. Teachers should emphasize the general principle: once a nafl act of worship is started, it becomes binding to complete it, barring a valid excuse. The exception for fasting in a disliked time (no qada) is noted but will be elaborated in the chapter on fasting.

Key Terms
شروع (shuru'): Commencement of an act of worship (here specifically nafl prayer or fasting). Once one begins, the act becomes binding (lazim).
إبطال العمل (ibtal al-'amal): Invalidating one's action; specifically, breaking a commenced act of worship. Prohibited by the Quranic verse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person starts a nafl prayer and then breaks it intentionally without a valid excuse, what is required?
A) Nothing, because nafl prayers are voluntary.
B) Sajdah al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness).
C) Qada (making up the prayer) because it was binding once started.
D) Repeat only if broken in the first rak'ah.

Key Takeaway
A commenced nafl prayer is wajib to complete; breaking it is haram and requires qada.

Nafl in Disliked Times and the Difference on Fasting
Discusses the ruling when a nafl prayer is started in a disliked time and the intra-madhhab difference on breaking a nafl fast without excuse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the ruling of commencement to a nafl prayer started in a disliked time and compare the Hanafi positions on breaking a nafl fast without excuse.

Core Idea
Starting a nafl prayer in a disliked time is binding, but completing it is disliked; breaking a nafl fast without excuse is disputed within the Hanafi school.

This lesson addresses two interrelated issues: the effect of starting a nafl prayer during a disliked time (sunrise, sunset, etc.), and the intra-Hanafi divergence on breaking a nafl fast without a valid excuse. Both illustrate the interplay between the binding effect of commencement and the ruling of disliked times.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The passage states 'even at sunset' — meaning if one starts a nafl prayer at a disliked time, it is still binding.
Disliked times for prayer include sunrise, sunset, and when the sun is at its zenith (istiwā’).
2
Extract the Ruling for Prayer
From the text: 'If he spoils it, he must make it up' — qada is required. But also: it is better to break it (al-Bada'i') to avoid the disliked time, and completing it is disliked.
Some scholars say breaking is obligatory (wajib) to escape makruh tahrimi.
3
Compare with Fasting
The passage notes a difference: if one starts a nafl fast in a disliked time (e.g., on a Friday alone), breaking it does not require qada, unlike prayer.
The reason for the difference is explained later in the original text under the chapter on fasting.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf on Fasting Without Excuse
The text mentions two riwayahs: the zahir al-riwayah (prohibits breaking a nafl fast without excuse) and the riwayah of al-Muntaqa (permits it).
The relied-upon view is the zahir al-riwayah (prohibition), but the existence of a weak view shows the scope of ikhtilaf.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
For prayer: breaking a nafl in a disliked time is required (wajib) according to the preferred view, and qada is necessary. For fasting: the preferred view is that breaking a nafl fast without excuse is not permissible.
These nuances are important for issuing fatwa.

Source Text

لا يكون إلا بالاتمام لأن المؤدى وقع قربة بدليل أنه لو مات بعد القدر المؤدى يصير مثاباً، وقد اتفق أصحابنا على لزوم القضاء في إفساد الصلاة والصوم سواء كان بعذر كالحيض في خلالهما أو بغير عذر، وأنه يحل الإفساد لعذر فيهما وأنه لا يحل الإفساد في الصلاة لغير عذر. واختلفوا في إباحته في الصوم لغير عذر ففي ظاهر الرواية لا يباح، وفي رواية المنتقي يباح كما سيأتي في الصوم. وقوله ولو عند الغروب بيان لكونه لازماً له إذا شرع فيه في وقت مكروه وهو ظاهر الرواية، فإذا أفسده لزمه قضاؤه بخلاف الصوم إذا شرع في وقت مكروه فإنه لا قضاء عليه بالإفساد وسيأتي الفرق إن شاء الله تعالى في الصوم. وفي البدائع: وعندنا الأفضل أن يقطعها وإن أتم فقد أساء ولا قضاء عليه لأنه أداها كما وجبت، فإذا قطعها لزمه القضاء انتهى. وينبغي أن يكون القطع واجباً خروجاً عن المكروه تحريماً وليس بإبطال للعمل لأنه إبطال ليؤديه على وجه أكمل فلا يعد إبطالاً، ولو قضاه استعجال رأيت العلامة الرملي نقل ذلك عن خط العلامة المقدسي فتدبر لكن قد علمت ما فيه قوله : (إلا أنه لا يتم الخ) قد يجاب بأنهم اعتبروا والمؤكدة صلاة واحدة في حق القراءة فقط احتياطاً كما في الوتر فإنهم أوجبوا القراة في جميع ركعاته احتياطاً كما مر لاحتمال كونه سنة مؤكدة قوله: (ولا يبطل خيارها الخ) أي خيار المرأة التي قال لها زوجها اختاري نفسك وهي في سنة الظهر القبلية قول المصنف ولزم) النفل بالشروع) أي صلاة أو صوماً كذا قال العيني، وتعقبه في النهر بأنه من الشيء قبل أوانه وهلا قال أو حجاً ! وأجاب بعضهم بأنه تنصيص على ما فيه خلاف الشافعي بخلاف الحج إذ لا خلاف له فيه ولا في العمرة على ما يعلم . من الزيلعي ا هـ . والظاهر تخصيص الصلاة فقط لأن المقام لها ولأنه ينبو عن الصوم قول المصنف ولو عند الغروب والطلوع كما لا يخفى هذا، وإنما لم يذكر الاستواء لأنه وقت ضيق لا يتأتى فيه أداء الصلاة كذا نقله بعضهم عن الشلبي وفيه أن الكلام في الشروع لا في الأداء ومدة الشروع يسيرة يمكن فيه فالأولى الجواب بأن تحري
His saying: (And nafl becomes binding with commencement) meaning: prayer or fasting, as al-'Ayni said. Then he objected in al-Nahr that it is premature and why not say Hajj? Some answered that it is a specification of what differs from al-Shafi'i, unlike Hajj where there is no disagreement. End from al-Zayla'i. The apparent view is to specify prayer only because the context is for it and because the author's phrase 'even at sunset and sunrise' does not apply to fasting. This is not hidden. He did not mention midday (istiwa') because it is a time too narrow for performing prayer, as some transmitted from al-Shalabi. But the discussion is about commencement, not performance, and the time of commencement is short and possible. So the better answer is... Explanation of what becomes obligatory on the servant by undertaking it: two types: what is obligatory by speech (nadhr) and what is obligatory by action (commencement of nafl). We begin with it following the book. We say: Indeed, invalidating an action is haram by the text: 'Do not invalidate your deeds' [Muhammad 33]. So it is necessary to complete it because avoiding invalidation of an action that does not admit of part-part description can only be by completion, because what was performed occurred as an act of worship, as evidenced by the fact that if he dies after the amount performed, he becomes rewarded. And our companions have agreed on the obligation of qada (making up) in spoiling prayer and fasting, whether with an excuse like menstruation during them or without an excuse. And that it is permissible to spoil them for an excuse in both, and that it is not permissible to spoil prayer without an excuse. And they differed on its permissibility in fasting without an excuse: in the zahir al-riwayah it is not permitted, and in the riwayah of al-Muntaqa it is permitted, as will come in fasting. His saying: 'even at sunset' is an explanation that it is binding on him if he starts in a disliked time, which is the apparent narration. So if he spoils it, he must make it up, unlike fasting if started in a disliked time, for which there is no qada upon spoiling. The difference will come, insha'Allah, in fasting. In al-Bada'i': In our view, it is better to break it, and if he completes it, he acts badly but there is no qada upon him because he performed it as it was obligatory. So if he breaks it, qada becomes necessary. End. It should be that breaking is obligatory to exit from the dislike (makruh tahrimi) and it is not considered invalidation of the action because it is invalidation to perform it in a more complete manner, so it is not considered invalidation. And if he makes it up hastily... I saw al-'Allamah al-Ramli narrate that from the handwriting of al-'Allamah al-Maqdisi, so ponder. But you know what is in it. His saying: 'Except that it is not complete...' It may be answered that they considered the emphatic sunnah as one prayer only in respect of recitation, as caution, like in witr, where they made recitation obligatory in all its rak'ahs out of caution as mentioned, due to the possibility of it being an emphatic sunnah. His saying: 'And her option is not invalidated...' meaning the option of the woman whose husband said to her 'choose yourself' while she was performing the before-noon sunnah of Zuhr. The author's saying: (And nafl becomes binding with commencement) meaning prayer or fasting, as al-'Ayni said. Then he objected...
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage discusses the principle that a nafl prayer becomes binding (lazim) once commenced. The author, Ibn Nujaym, explains that the avoidance of invalidating a righteous action is based on the Quranic verse 'Do not invalidate your deeds' (Muhammad: 33). Once a person begins a nafl prayer, it is obligatory to complete it, and breaking it is haram and requires qada (making up). The Hanafi school agrees on this for both prayer and fasting, with some differences: spoiling a nafl prayer for a valid excuse (e.g., menstruation) is permissible, but spoiling it without excuse is haram. For fasting, there is a difference: according to the zahir al-riwayah, it is not permissible to break a nafl fast without excuse; according to the riwayah of al-Muntaqa, it is permissible (as will be explained later). The passage also addresses a special case: if one starts a nafl prayer in a disliked time (e.g., at sunrise or sunset), the ruling is that it is binding and if one breaks it, qada is required. However, some authorities (al-Bada'i') suggest it is better to break it in such a case to avoid the disliked time; but if one completes it, it is valid but disliked. The passage ends with a discussion about whether the term 'nafl' includes only prayer or also fasting and Hajj. The preferred view is that it applies primarily to prayer because the context is about prayer and the phrase 'at sunset and sunrise' is specific to prayer. Teachers should emphasize the general principle: once a nafl act of worship is started, it becomes binding to complete it, barring a valid excuse. The exception for fasting in a disliked time (no qada) is noted but will be elaborated in the chapter on fasting.

Key Terms
شروع (shuru'): Commencement of an act of worship (here specifically nafl prayer or fasting). Once one begins, the act becomes binding (lazim).
إبطال العمل (ibtal al-'amal): Invalidating one's action; specifically, breaking a commenced act of worship. Prohibited by the Quranic verse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person starts a nafl prayer at sunrise (a disliked time) and then breaks it to avoid the disliked time, what is the Hanafi ruling regarding qada?
A) No qada is required because it was in a disliked time.
B) Qada is required because the prayer was binding upon commencement.
C) Only sajdah al-sahw is required.
D) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated from the beginning.

Key Takeaway
Starting a nafl in a disliked time is binding, but completing it is disliked; breaking a nafl fast without excuse is forbidden in the relied-upon view, and breaking a nafl fast in a disliked time does not require qada.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Sitting in Nafl Is Not Fard at Each Pair
Disputes Muhammad's view that sitting after each pair in nafl is fard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the qa'da in nafl prayer, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between the majority and Imam Muhammad, and apply the ruling to determine validity when a worshipper omits the sitting.

Core Idea
In nafl, each pair is an independent prayer; sitting is not fard, only for exiting.

When praying nafl (supererogatory) prayers, a common question is whether one must sit and recite tashahhud after every two rak'ahs. Some, like Imam Muhammad, consider it fard (obligatory) by analogy to fard prayers. This lesson examines the majority Hanafi view that the sitting is not fard, and explains the reasoning behind the disagreement and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Begin by identifying the ruling of the majority: the sitting (qa'da) after each pair (shaf') in nafl is not fard. What is the basis for this view?
The majority includes Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and later scholars.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Muhammad holds that the sitting is fard by qiyas (analogy) to fard prayer. Understand why he argues this.
Muhammad's view is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The qiyas: in fard prayer, sitting is fard because it is the exit from prayer. In nafl, by analogy, sitting should also be fard for exiting.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The author distinguishes nafl: each pair is an independent prayer. Standing for a third rak'ah shows that the previous two were not the exit, so the sitting is not obligatory. Recitation, by contrast, is a rukn intended for itself.
This refutes the analogy by breaking the illa (cause).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if one omits the sitting and stands for a third, the prayer remains valid (no sajdah al-sahw needed). If one omits recitation in a pair, that pair is invalid.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عند الغروب والطلوع وقضى ركعتين لو نوى أربعاً وأفسده بعد القعود الأول أو قبله فيها إلى الشفع الثاني، وإن أريد بالنفل في كلامهم ما ليس سنة مؤكدة لم يتم أيضاً لخلوه عن إفادة حكم القراءة في السنة المؤكدة. وإنما لم تكن القعدة على رأس كل شفع فرضاً كما هو قول محمد وهو القياس لأنها فرض للخروج من الصلاة فإذا قام إلى الثالثة تبين أن ما قبلها لم يكن أوان الخروج من الصلاة فلم تبق القعدة فريضة بخلاف القراءة فإنها ركن مقصود بنفسه فإذا تركه تفسد صلاته .
At sunset and sunrise, and if one prayed two rak'ahs intending four and invalidated after the first sitting or before it, [the ruling extends] to the second [invalid] pair. If what is meant by nafl in their speech is not a confirmed sunnah, it is also not completed because it lacks conveying the ruling of recitation in confirmed sunnah. The sitting at the head of each pair is not fard as is the saying of Muhammad, and it is the analogy, because it is fard for exiting the prayer. So when he stands for the third, it becomes clear that what was before was not the time of exiting the prayer, so the sitting does not remain an obligation, unlike recitation, for it is an integral intended for its own sake, so if one omits it, his prayer is invalid.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the sitting (qada) at the end of every two rak'ahs in nafl prayer is fard (obligatory). Imam Muhammad holds that it is fard by qiyas (analogy) to fard prayer, arguing that the sitting is for exiting the prayer, so if one stands for a third rak'ah, the previous sitting is not needed. The author refutes this, stating that in nafl, each pair is an independent prayer, so the sitting is not a pillar. Recitation, however, is a rukn in each pair and omitting it invalidates the prayer. The ruling follows the majority: the sitting is not fard in nafl.

Key Terms
قعدة (qa'da): The act of sitting after the second rak'ah of a pair in prayer.
شفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs in prayer.
النفل (al-nafl): Supererogatory (voluntary) prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is the sitting (qa'da) at the end of each pair in nafl prayer not fard?
A) Because nafl prayer is not obligatory at all.
B) Because each pair is an independent prayer, so sitting is only for exiting the whole prayer.
C) Because the Prophet never sat in nafl.
D) Because recitation is enough to validate the prayer.

Key Takeaway
In nafl prayer, the sitting after each pair is not fard; omitting it does not invalidate the prayer, unlike omission of recitation which is a rukn.
