أو لم يقرأ فيهن شيئاً أو قرأ في الأوليين أو الاخريين وأربعاً لو قرأ في إحدى الأولين أو الأخريين) أي قضى ركعتين في هذه المسائل الثلاث وهي من المسائل المعروفة بالثمانية، والأصل فيها أن الشفع الأول متى فسد بترك القراءة تبقى التحريمة عند أبي يوسف لأن القراءة ركن زائد، ألا ترى أن للصلاة وجوداً بدونها غير أنه لا صحة للأداء إلا بها وفساد الأداء لا يزيد على تركه فلا تبطل التحريمة . وعند محمد متى فسد الشفع الأول لا تبقى التحريمة فلا . الشروع في الشفع الثاني لأن القراءة فرض في كل من الركعتين، فكما يفسد الشفع بترك القراءة فيهما يفسد بتركها في إحداهما ، وإذا فسدت الأفعال لم تبق التحريمة لأنها تعقد للأفعال وقد فسدت. وعند الامام أبي حنيفة إن فسد الشفع الأول بترك القراءة فيهما بطلت التحريمة فلا . الشروع في الشفع الثاني، وإن فسد بترك القراءة في إحداهما بقيت التحريمة فصح الشروع في الشفع الثاني إلا أن القياس ما قاله محمد لكن فسادها بترك القراءة في ركعة واحدة مجتهد فيه لأن الحسن البصري كان يقول اجتهادي غير موجب على اليقين، بل يجوز أن يكون الصحيح قوله غير أنا عرفنا صحة ما ذهبنا إليه وفساد ما ذهب إليه بغالب الرأي فلم يحكم ببطلان التحريمة الثانية بيقين بالشك. وإذا عرف هذا فنقول : إذا ترك القراءة في الأربع قضى الركعتين الأوليين فقط عندهما لبطلان التحريمة خلافاً لأبي يوسف لبقائها عنده فيقضي الشفعين، وإن ترك القراءة في الأخريين فقد أفسدهما فقط فليزمه قضاؤهما إجماعاً. وإذا ترك القراءة في الأوليين فقط لزمه قضاؤهما فقط إجماعاً لفسادهما ولم يصح الشروع في الشفع الثاني عندهما حتى لو قهقه فيه لا تنتقض طهارته، وعند أبي يوسف قد صح ولم يفسد لوجود القراءة فيه . وأشار المصنف بهذه الثلات إلى ثلاث أخرى أيضاً فتصير المسائل ستاً من الثمانية إحداها لو قرأ في الأوليين وإحدى الأخريين فعليه قضاء الأخريين إجماعاً . ثانيها لو قرأ في الأخريين وإحدى الأوليين فعليه قضاء الأوليين اجماعاً . ثالثها لو قرأ في إحدى الأخريين لا غير لزمه قضاء الأوليين عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف يقضي أربعاً، وقد قدمنا أن فساد الشفع الثاني يسري إلى الأول إذا لم يقعد بينهما، فقوله «أو قرأ في الأوليين مقيد بما إذا قعد على رأس الركعتين وإلا فعليه قضاء الأربع كما في العناية . وفي البدائع : هذا كله إذا قعد بين الشفعين قدر التشهد فأما إذا لم يقعد تفسد صلاته عند محمد قوله : وفساد الأداء لا يزيد على (تركه أي لا يكون أقوى من ترك الأداء بأن أحرم واقفاً ترك أداء كل الأفعال بأن وقف ساكتاً طويلاً لا تبطل ،التحريمة وهذا لأنها ليست لم تعقد إلا لهذا الشفع فإن بناء الشفع الثاني جائز فعلم أنها له ولغيره فبفساده لا تنتفي فائدتها بالكلية لتفسد هي كما بسطه في الفتح قوله : ( وعند أبي حنيفة إلى آخر (كلامه لا يخفي أن بهذا التقرير لم يحصل الجواب عما قرر لأبي يوسف بل جوابه منع أن فساده لا يزيد على تركه لأن الترك مجرد تأخير والفساد فعل مفسد وتمامه في الفتح قوله: (لكن) فسادها الخ قال في النهاية فإن قلت: كما أن
Or he did not recite anything in them, or he recited in the first two or the last two, and four if he recited in one of the first two or one of the last two) i.e., he makes up two rak'ahs in these three issues, which are among the well-known eight issues. The principle in them is that when the first pair becomes defective by leaving the recitation, the tahrimah remains according to Abu Yusuf because the recitation is an additional integral (rukn za'id). Do you not see that the prayer has existence without it, except that the performance is not valid except with it, and the corruption of performance does not exceed its omission, so the tahrimah is not voided. According to Muhammad, when the first pair becomes defective, the tahrimah does not remain, so there is no commencement of the second pair, because recitation is an obligation (fard) in each of the two rak'ahs. Just as the pair is defective by leaving recitation in both, it is defective by leaving it in one of them. And when the actions become defective, the tahrimah does not remain because it is contracted for the actions, and they have become defective. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if the first pair is defective by leaving recitation in both, the tahrimah becomes void, so there is no commencement of the second pair. But if it is defective by leaving recitation in one of them, the tahrimah remains, so the commencement of the second pair is valid, except that qiyas is what Muhammad said. However, its defectiveness due to leaving recitation in one rak'ah is a matter of ijtihad, because Hasan al-Basri used to say: 'my ijtihad does not necessitate certainty; it is possible that his view is correct, but we know the correctness of our view and the incorrectness of his by preponderant opinion, so we do not rule the invalidation of the second tahrimah with certainty due to doubt.' And when this is known, we say: If he left recitation in all four, he makes up only the first two rak'ahs according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) due to the invalidation of the tahrimah, contrary to Abu Yusuf because of its remaining with him, so he makes up both pairs. If he left recitation in the last two, he has only spoiled those, so he must make them up by consensus. If he left recitation only in the first two, he must make them up only by consensus due to their defectiveness, and the commencement of the second pair is not valid according to the two, so that even if he laughs (qahqaha) in it, his ablution is not nullified. According to Abu Yusuf, it has become valid and is not spoiled because of the existence of recitation in it. And the author indicated by these three another three as well, so the issues become six of the eight: first, if he recited in the first two and one of the last two, he must make up the last two by consensus. Second, if he recited in the last two and one of the first two, he must make up the first two by consensus. Third, if he recited in only one of the last two, he must make up the first two according to the two, but according to Abu Yusuf, he makes up four. And we have previously stated that the defectiveness of the second pair spreads to the first if he did not sit between them. So his statement 'or he recited in the first two' is restricted to when he sits at the end of two rak'ahs; otherwise he must make up four, as in al-'Inayah. And in al-Bada'i': all this is when he sits between the two pairs as much as tashahhud. If he did not sit, his prayer becomes invalid according to Muhammad. His statement: 'And the corruption of performance does not exceed its omission' i.e., it is not stronger than the omission of performance; if he began and stood, omitting all actions by standing silently for a long time, the tahrimah is not voided. This is because it was not contracted only for this pair, since building the second pair is permissible, so it is known that it is for this and other purposes, so by its corruption its benefit is not entirely negated so as to invalidate it, as is explained in al-Fath. His statement: 'And according to Abu Hanifa up to the end of his speech' it is not hidden that by this appraisal the answer to what was established for Abu Yusuf is not obtained; rather, his answer is to deny that its corruption does not exceed its omission, because omission is mere delay while corruption is a destructive act, and its completion is in al-Fath. His statement: 'but' its corruption etc. He said in al-Nihayah: 'for if you say: just as...'
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the famous 'eight issues' (al-masa'il al-thamaniyah) regarding recitation (qira'ah) in a nafl prayer of four rak'ahs. The key principle is that when the first pair of the prayer is spoiled due to omission of recitation, the effect on the tahrimah differs among the imams. Abu Yusuf views recitation as an additional integral (rukn za'id); the prayer can exist without it, but performance is not valid. Therefore, if the first pair is spoiled, the tahrimah remains, and the second pair can be commenced. Muhammad considers recitation a fard in each rak'ah; thus spoiling the first pair by omitting recitation in both (or even one) invalidates the tahrimah entirely, preventing commencement of the second pair. Abu Hanifa takes a middle position: if recitation is omitted in both rak'ahs of the first pair, the tahrimah is void; if omitted in only one, the tahrimah survives due to doubt (shakk) and istihsan, following the practice of Hasan al-Basri who considered the matter subject to ijtihad. The practical outcomes: if one omits recitation in all four, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad require making up only the first two; Abu Yusuf requires four. If omission is in the last two only, all agree on making up the last two. If omission is in the first two only, all agree on making up the first two, but the second pair's validity differs. The passage then lists six of the eight issues, with details on recitation in some rak'ahs. The commentator emphasizes that these rulings apply when one sits between the two pairs for the duration of tashahhud; otherwise, the entire prayer becomes one unit and if spoiled, all four must be made up.

Key Terms
قراءة (qira'ah): Recitation of Quran during prayer; its status differs among the imams: fard in each rak'ah (Muhammad) or rukn za'id (Abu Yusuf).
ركن زائد (rukn za'id): An additional integral; not essential for the existence of the prayer but required for valid performance.
المسائل الثمانية (al-masa'il al-thamaniyah): Eight well-known issues in Hanafi fiqh concerning the effect of omitting or partially reading in a four-rak'ah nafl prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, what is the effect on the tahrimah if the first pair of a four-rak'ah nafl prayer is spoiled by leaving recitation in one rak'ah?
A) The tahrimah remains intact
B) The tahrimah becomes void, preventing commencement of the second pair
C) The tahrimah remains only if the recitation was in the last rak'ah
D) The tahrimah becomes void but the second pair can still be commenced

Key Takeaway
In a four-rak'ah nafl, whether the tahrimah survives omission of recitation depends on the imam's classification of recitation; Abu Hanifa's istihsan for single-rak'ah omission is the preferred view.

Refining the Count of the Eight Problems in Nawafil Qada'
Resolves the apparent number of cases in the mas'a'il thamaniyah, showing they are actually fifteen or nine.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the well-known 'eight problems' in nawafil qada' are actually fifteen distinct cases, and state the preferred Hanafi view on the intra-madhhab dispute regarding the number of rak'ahs required.

Core Idea
The 'eight problems' are actually fifteen: nine require two rak'ahs, six require four; the preferred view is four when recitation is in one of each pair.

This passage refines a classic Hanafi fiqh topic — the eight problems (al-mas'a'il al-thamaniyyah) concerning qada' in supererogatory prayers (nawafil). The text reveals that the conventional count of eight is approximate: each of three base cases branches into two sub-cases, making nine cases requiring two rak'ahs, and together with six cases requiring four rak'ahs, the total is fifteen. The passage then examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about the ruling when recitation is performed in one of the first two and one of the last two rak'ahs, and explains why later authorities preferred the view that four rak'ahs must be made up.

Guided Path
1
Map the six base cases to their sub-cases
Identify that cases four, five, and six each split into two scenarios based on which rak'ah is involved (third/fourth or first/second). This yields nine distinct cases requiring two rak'ahs.
Case four: omitting recitation in the fourth or third rak'ah. Case five: omitting in the first or second. Case six: reciting in the third or fourth.
2
Calculate the total number of distinct cases
Add the nine cases requiring two rak'ahs to the six original cases requiring four rak'ahs. The sum is fifteen — the actual count of distinct scenarios in the 'eight problems'.
The traditional name 'eight' is a simplification.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling for mixed recitation
When a person recites in one of the first two and one of the last two rak'ahs, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (according to Muhammad's narration) rule that four rak'ahs must be made up because the tahrimah remains. Muhammad personally holds that only two are needed because the tahrimah is lifted. Abu Yusuf denied this narration from him, claiming he heard Abu Hanifa say two.
The dispute hinges on whether the tahrimah (prohibition of breaking prayer) remains when some recitation occurs.
4
Follow the resolution by later authorities
The mashayikh (later scholars like Fakhr al-Islam, Qadikhan) accepted Muhammad's narration as the 'zahir al-riwayah' (apparent/authoritative transmission) and treated it as a correct derivation (tafri') from Abu Hanifa's principles, even if Abu Yusuf's denial seems explicit. Thus the relied-upon position is that four rak'ahs are required.
This shows how ijtihad and transmission hierarchy operate within the Hanafi school.

ثم اعلم أن هذه المسائل الست تسع من حيث التصوير لأن الرابعة صادقة بصورتين ما إذا ترك في الركعة الثالثة أو ترك في الركعة الرابعة، والخامسة صادقة بصورتين أيضاً ما ترك في الركعة الأولى أو ترك في الثانية، والسادسة صادقة بصورتين أيضاً ما إذا قرأ في الثالثة أو قرأ في الرابعة، فالمسائل التي يجب فيها ركعتان تسع في التحقيق، فإن هذه المسائل وإن اشتهرت بالثمانية لكن هي في التحقيق خمسة عشر، تسع منها يلزم فيها ركعتان، وست منها يلزم فيها أربع أشار إليها بقوله . (وأربعاً لو قرأ في إحدى الأوليين وإحدى الأخريين وهو قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف على رواية محمد لبقاء التحريمة عندهما لما عرف في الأصل السابق، وعند محمد عليه قضاء الأوليين لا غير لأن التحريمة قد ارتفعت عنده . قال في الهداية : وقد أنكر أبو يوسف هذه الرواية عنه وقال : رويت لك عن أبي حنيفة أنه يلزمه قضاء ركعتين ومحمد لم يرجع عن روايته عنه انتهى . وقال فخر الإسلام واعتمد مشايخنا رواية محمد ، ويحتمل أن يكون ما حكى أبو يوسف من قول أبي حنيفة قياساً، وما ذكره محمد استحساناً ذكر القياس والاستحسان في الأصل ولم يذكره في الجامع الصغير انتهى . وذكر قاضيخان في شرح الجامع الصغير أن ما رواه محمد هو ظاهر الرواية عن أبي حنيفة . وفي فتح القدير : واعتمد المشايخ رواية محمد مع تصريحهم في الأصول بأن تكذيب الفرع الأصل يسقط الرواية إذا كان صريحاً، والعبارة المذكورة في الكتاب وغيره عن أبي يوسف من مثل الصريح على ما يعرف في ذلك الموضع فليكن لا بناء على أنه رواية بل تفريع صحيح على أصل أبي حنيفة .
Then know that these six cases are nine in terms of depiction, because the fourth applies to two scenarios: whether he omitted in the third rak'ah or omitted in the fourth rak'ah. The fifth also applies to two scenarios: whether he omitted in the first rak'ah or omitted in the second. The sixth also applies to two scenarios: whether he recited in the third or recited in the fourth. So the cases in which two rak'ahs are required are in reality nine. Indeed, these cases, although known as the eight, are in reality fifteen. Nine of them require two rak'ahs, and six of them require four. He indicated this by his statement: 'And four if he recited in one of the first two and one of the last two' — and this is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf according to Muhammad's narration, because the tahrimah remains according to them as known in the previous basis. According to Muhammad, he must make up only the first two because the tahrimah has been lifted according to him. He said in al-Hidayah: 'Abu Yusuf denied this narration from him and said: I narrated to you from Abu Hanifa that he must make up two rak'ahs, and Muhammad did not retract his narration from him.' End. And Fakhr al-Islam said: 'Our mashayikh relied on Muhammad's narration. It is possible that what Abu Yusuf related from Abu Hanifa is qiyas, and what Muhammad mentioned is istihsan. He mentioned both qiyas and istihsan in al-Asl, but did not mention it in al-Jami' al-Saghir.' End. Qadikhan stated in his commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir that what Muhammad narrated is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) from Abu Hanifa. In Fath al-Qadir: 'The mashayikh relied on Muhammad's narration despite their explicit statements in the usul that if the subordinate (far') rejects the original (asl), it invalidates the narration if explicit. The expression in the book and elsewhere from Abu Yusuf is something like explicit, as known in that context. So it should be not on the basis of narration, but rather a correct derivation (tafri') based on Abu Hanifa's principle.'
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage refines the understanding of the well-known 'eight problems' (al-mas'a'il al-thamaniyyah) regarding qada' in nawafil. The author explains that the six cases previously mentioned actually become nine in terms of depiction (taswir) because three of them have two sub-cases depending on which specific rak'ah is involved. For example, the fourth case (omitting recitation in one of the last two) can be either the third or fourth rak'ah. Thus, the total distinct scenarios requiring two rak'ahs become nine. Combined with six cases requiring four rak'ahs, the real total is fifteen, not eight. This shows that the traditional name 'eight' is approximate. The passage then addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute about the ruling when one recites in one of the first two and one of the last two. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (as per Muhammad's narration), the tahrimah remains, so four rak'ahs are required. According to Muhammad himself, only two rak'ahs are required because the tahrimah is lifted. The text reports Abu Yusuf's denial of Muhammad's narration, but the mashayikh (later authorities such as Fakhr al-Islam) relied on Muhammad's version, considering it the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwayah). Some scholars suggest that Abu Yusuf's report represents qiyas (analogy) while Muhammad's is istihsan (juristic preference). Qadikhan clarifies that Muhammad's narration is considered the sounder in terms of transmission. Fath al-Qadir explains that even if the subordinate (far') contradicts the original (asl) in transmission, in this case the mashayikh accepted Muhammad's version not as a narration from Abu Yusuf but as a correct derivation (tafri') on Abu Hanifa's principles. Thus, the preferred view is that if he recited in one of the first two and one of the last two, he makes up four rak'ahs because the tahrimah remains.

Key Terms
ثمانية (thamanīyah): Refers to the well-known 'eight problems' (al-mas'a'il al-thamaniyyah) in nawafil qada', though the actual count is more.
ظاهر الرواية (zāhir al-riwāyah): The apparent or well-known transmission from the imam, considered authoritative.
تفريع (tafrī'): A derived ruling based on the principles of the imam, even if the exact transmission is disputed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) 8
C) 9
D) 15

Key Takeaway
The well-known eight problems are actually fifteen distinct cases, with the preferred view that four rak'ahs are required when recitation is in one of the first two and one of the last two.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Qadha of Rak'ahs Due to Omitted Qa'dah or Recitation
Analyzes the ruling on qadha and the rivayah dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the number of rak'ahs required for qadha when recitation is omitted in a specific pattern, and identify the mufta bihi ruling with its justifications.

Core Idea
The mashayikh preferred Muhammad's narration despite Abu Yusuf's denial, making the mufta bihi four rak'ahs.

This lesson examines a nuanced rivayah dispute within the Hanafi school concerning the qadha of rak'ahs when one recites in both an early and a late rak'ah in Witr or Nawafil. The disagreement stems from two conflicting narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa, reported by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani respectively. The later mashayikh resolved this by relying on Muhammad's narration, deeming it as the authoritative transmission (zahir al-riwayah). Understanding this dispute is crucial for grasping how the Hanafi school evaluates conflicting rivayah and establishes the mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario
The case is when a person recites in one of the first two rak'ahs and also in one of the last two rak'ahs in Witr or Nawafil. The question is how many rak'ahs of qadha are required due to the omission of proper recitation or sitting?
2
State the two positions
According to the narration of Muhammad from Abu Hanifa, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say four rak'ahs are required because the tahrimah remains. Muhammad's own view is that only two rak'ahs are required because the tahrimah is lifted after the first sitting.
3
Understand the basis: principle of tahrimah
The dispute hinges on whether the tahrimah (prohibition of nullifying actions) continues throughout the prayer or is lifted after the first sitting. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (per Muhammad) hold it remains, so each omission/error requires compensation. Muhammad holds it is lifted, so only the first two rak'ahs are affected.
The tahrimah is a key Hanafi principle.
4
Examine the rivayah conflict
Abu Yusuf denied having narrated the four-rak'ah view from Abu Hanifa, insisting he only narrated two rak'ahs. Muhammad insisted on his narration and claimed Abu Yusuf forgot. This led to a debate about the reliability of the rivayah.
This is the famous 'six masail' where Muhammad corrected Abu Yusuf.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The mashayikh (later Hanafi authorities like Fakhr al-Islam, Qadi Khan, and Fath al-Qadir) relied on Muhammad's narration, mainly because it is found in books of zahir al-riwayah (like al-Jami' al-Saghir) and is considered directly heard from Abu Hanifa by Muhammad. Thus the operative ruling is four rak'ahs.
Preference given due to transmission strength despite Abu Yusuf's denial.

كتاب الصلاة باب الوتر والنوافل بترك القعدة فلا تتأتى هذه التفريعات عنده انتهى . ثم اعلم أن هذه المسائل الست تسع من حيث التصوير لأن الرابعة صادقة بصورتين ما إذا ترك في الركعة الثالثة أو ترك في الركعة الرابعة، والخامسة صادقة بصورتين أيضاً ما ترك في الركعة الأولى أو ترك في الثانية، والسادسة صادقة بصورتين أيضاً ما إذا قرأ في الثالثة أو قرأ في الرابعة، فالمسائل التي يجب فيها ركعتان تسع في التحقيق، فإن هذه المسائل وإن اشتهرت بالثمانية لكن هي في التحقيق خمسة عشر، تسع منها يلزم فيها ركعتان، وست منها يلزم فيها أربع أشار إليها بقوله . (وأربعاً لو قرأ في إحدى الأوليين وإحدى الأخريين وهو قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف على رواية محمد لبقاء التحريمة عندهما لما عرف في الأصل السابق، وعند محمد عليه قضاء الأوليين لا غير لأن التحريمة قد ارتفعت عنده . قال في الهداية : وقد أنكر أبو يوسف هذه الرواية عنه وقال : رويت لك عن أبي حنيفة أنه يلزمه قضاء ركعتين ومحمد لم يرجع عن روايته عنه انتهى . وقال فخر الإسلام واعتمد مشايخنا رواية محمد ، ويحتمل أن يكون ما حكى أبو يوسف من قول أبي حنيفة قياساً، وما ذكره محمد استحساناً ذكر القياس والاستحسان في الأصل ولم يذكره في الجامع الصغير انتهى . وذكر قاضيخان في شرح الجامع الصغير أن ما رواه محمد هو ظاهر الرواية عن أبي حنيفة . وفي فتح القدير : واعتمد المشايخ رواية محمد مع تصريحهم في الأصول بأن تكذيب الفرع الأصل يسقط الرواية إذا كان صريحاً، والعبارة المذكورة في الكتاب وغيره عن أبي يوسف من مثل الصريح على ما يعرف في ذلك الموضع فليكن لا بناء على أنه رواية بل تفريع صحيح على أصل أبي حنيفة وإلا فهو مشكل انتهى . وبما ذكرناه عن قاضيخان ارتفع الإشكال لتصريحه بأنها ظاهر الرواية كأنه لثبوتها بالسماع لمحمد من أبي حنيفة لا بواسطة أبي يوسف فلذا اعتمدها المشايخ . وفي غاية البيان معزياً إلى فخر الإسلام كان أبو يوسف يتوقع من محمد أن عنه كتاباً . يروي فصنف محمد هذا الكتاب أي الجامع الصغير وأسنده عن أبي يوسف إلى أبي حنيفة، فلما عرض على أبي يوسف استحسنه وقال : حفظ أبو عبد الله إلا مسائل خطأه في روايتها عنه بلغ ذلك محمداً قال : حفظتها ونسي وهي ست مسائل مذكورة في شرح الجامع الصغير انتهى ولم يبينها. وذكر العلامة السراج الهندي في شرح المغني فقال : الأولى مسألة ترك القراءة وقد علمتها الثانية مستحاضة توضأت بعد طلوع الشمس تصلي حتى يخرج وقت الظهر قال أبو يوسف : إنما رويت لك حتى يدخل وقت الظهر الثالثة المشتري من الغاصب إذا أعتق ثم أجاز المالك البيع نفذ العتق قال : إنما رويت لك أنه لا ينفد . الرابعة المهاجرة لا عدة عليها ويجوز نكاحها إلا أن تكون حبلى فحينئذ لا يجوز نكاحها قال : إنما رويت لك أنه يجوز نكاحها ولكن لا يقربها زوجها حتى تضع الحمل. الخامسة عبد بين اثنين قتل مولى لهما فعفا أحدهما بطل الدم كله عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا يدفع ربعه إلى شريكه أو يفديه بربع الدية، قالوا وفيه إشكال لأن المذكور أن أبا يوسف أنكر وقال : ما رويت لك عن أبي حنيفة ذلك وهذه الصورة ليست من نسيان الأصل رواية الفرع بخلاف ما إذا نسي الأصل ولم يجزم بالإنكار فلا ينبغي اعتبار قول محمد إلا إذا صح اعتبار ما ذكره تخريجاً على أصل أبي حنيفة ا هـ . ملخصاً اهـ. وأجاب العلامة المقدسي بقوله : أقول لعله حمله محمد على النسيان لطول العهد واشتغاله بالقضاء ا هـ. قوله : وبما ذكرناه الخ فيه بحث لأن مسائل ظاهر الرواية هي ما وجد في بعض كتب محمد كالمبسوط والزيادات والجامع الصغير سميت بذلك لأنها ثابتة عنه إما متواترة أو مشهورة وهي ا الطبقة الأولى . الثانية مسائل النوادر كالكيسانيات والهارونيات وتسمى غير ظاهر الرواية لأنها لم تثبت عن محمد ثبوتاً ظاهراً كالأولى. والطبقة الثالثة ما استنبطه المتأخرون مما لم يجدوا فيه رواية عن أصحاب المذهب كما بسطه الشيخ إسماعيل رحمه الله في صدر شرحه وحينئذ فقول قاضيخان ما رواه محمد هو ظاهر الرواية معناه أنه مذكور في كتب ظاهر الرواية وهو كذلك لأنه في الجامع الصغير، وقول المؤلف «كأنه لثبوتها بالسماع الخ ) ربما يوهم أن ظاهر الرواية ما سمعه محمد من أبي حنيفة وهذا يقتضي أن لا يكون الجامع الصغير من كتب ظاهر الرواية لأنه بواسطة أبي يوسف كما يأتي مع أنه نفسه في شرح قوله ودعا بما يشبه القرآن والسنة أنه من كتب ظاهر الرواية تأمل. ثم رأيت العلامة المقدسي ذكر نحو ما بحثته في شرحه على نظم الكنز فاعترضه بأن ما ذكره من الجواب يتوقف على أن مراد قاضيخان بظاهر الرواية غير ما ذكر في الأصل ونحوه كالجامع الصغير من كتب ظاهر الرواية، وزاد على ما قلته أن محصل كلامه هو ما يفهم من كلام الكمال من التفريع الصحيح على أصل أبي حنيفة رحمه الله وأن الإشكال في تصميم محمد على مخالفة من روى عنه لا ترتفع.
Book of Prayer, Chapter of Witr and Supererogatory Prayers: By leaving the sitting, these subdivisions are not realized according to him. Then know that these six issues are nine in terms of scenario, because the fourth applies to two cases: whether he leaves it in the third rak'ah or in the fourth rak'ah; the fifth also applies to two cases: whether he leaves it in the first rak'ah or in the second; the sixth also applies to two cases: whether he recites in the third or in the fourth. So the issues in which two rak'ahs are obligatory are nine in reality. Although these issues are famously known as eight, they are in reality fifteen: nine of them require two rak'ahs, and six require four rak'ahs, which he indicated by his statement: (And four rak'ahs if he recites in one of the first two rak'ahs and one of the last two rak'ahs, and this is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf according to the narration of Muhammad, because the tahrimah remains according to them, as known in the previous principle; while according to Muhammad, he must perform only the first two rak'ahs because the tahrimah has been lifted according to him. He said in al-Hidayah: Abu Yusuf denied this narration from him and said: I narrated to you from Abu Hanifa that he must perform two rak'ahs, and Muhammad did not retract his narration from him. End. Fakhr al-Islam said: Our mashayikh relied on Muhammad's narration, and it is possible that what Abu Yusuf narrated from Abu Hanifa is qiyas, and what Muhammad mentioned is istihsan; he mentioned qiyas and istihsan in al-Asl but did not mention it in al-Jami' al-Saghir. End. Qadi Khan mentioned in his Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir that what Muhammad narrated is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) from Abu Hanifa. In Fath al-Qadir: The mashayikh relied on Muhammad's narration despite their statement in the usul that the denial of the branch against the root invalidates the narration if it is explicit, and the phrase mentioned in the book and elsewhere from Abu Yusuf is similar to explicit, as is known in that context; so let it be not based on narration but a correct derivation from Abu Hanifa's principle, otherwise it is problematic. End. And by what we mentioned from Qadi Khan, the problem is resolved because he explicitly stated that it is zahir al-riwayah, as if it is established by Muhammad's direct hearing from Abu Hanifa without the intermediary of Abu Yusuf, so the mashayikh relied on it. In Ghayat al-Bayan, attributed to Fakhr al-Islam: Abu Yusuf expected Muhammad to have a book from him, so Muhammad authored this book, i.e., al-Jami' al-Saghir, and attributed it through Abu Yusuf to Abu Hanifa. When it was presented to Abu Yusuf, he approved it and said: Abu 'Abd Allah has preserved, except for issues in which he corrected him regarding his narration. This reached Muhammad, and he said: I have preserved them and he forgot. They are six issues mentioned in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir, end, but he did not specify them. Allamah Siraj al-Hindi mentioned in Sharh al-Mughni: The first is the issue of leaving recitation, which you know. The second: A woman with istihadah who performs wudu after sunrise and prays until the time of Zuhr exits; Abu Yusuf said: I only narrated to you that she prays until the time of Zuhr enters. The third: The buyer from a usurper, if he manumits and then the owner ratifies the sale, the manumission is effective; he said: I only narrated to you that it is not effective. The fourth: A woman who has emigrated has no 'iddah and her marriage is permissible unless she is pregnant, then her marriage is not permissible; he said: I only narrated to you that her marriage is permissible but her husband should not approach her until she delivers. The fifth: A slave owned by two men kills a master of both; if one of them pardons, all blood money is nullified according to Abu Hanifa, while the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: He must pay a quarter of the blood money to his partner or ransom himself with a quarter. They said: There is a problem here because it is mentioned that Abu Yusuf denied and said: I did not narrate to you that from Abu Hanifa. This scenario is not the case of the root forgetting the branch's narration, unlike when the root forgets and does not assert denial; so Muhammad's statement should not be considered unless it is confirmed as a derivation from Abu Hanifa's principle. End, summarized. Allamah al-Maqdisi responded: I think perhaps Muhammad attributed it to forgetfulness due to the long interval and his involvement in judicial duties. End. His statement: 'And by what we mentioned' etc. has discussion, because the issues of zahir al-riwayah are what are found in some of Muhammad's books like al-Mabsut, al-Ziyadat, and al-Jami' al-Saghir; they are called that because they are established from him either by tawatur or by widespread transmission, and they are the first layer. The second layer is the issues of nawadir like al-Kaysaniyat and al-Haruniyat, which are called non-zahir al-riwayah because they are not established from Muhammad as clearly as the first. The third layer is what later scholars derived where they found no narration from the school's founders, as elaborated by Shaykh Isma'il in the beginning of his commentary. Therefore, Qadi Khan's statement 'what Muhammad narrated is zahir al-riwayah' means it is mentioned in the books of zahir al-riwayah, and it is so because it is in al-Jami' al-Saghir. The author's statement 'as if it is established by direct hearing' may imply that zahir al-riwayah is what Muhammad heard directly from Abu Hanifa, which would mean that al-Jami' al-Saghir is not among the books of zahir al-riwayah because it is through Abu Yusuf, as will come, although he himself in his commentary on the statement 'and he prayed with something resembling the Quran and Sunnah' stated that it is among the books of zahir al-riwayah. Consider. Then I saw that Allamah al-Maqdisi mentioned something similar to my research in his commentary on Nadhm al-Kanz, and he objected that the response he mentioned depends on Qadi Khan's intended meaning of zahir al-riwayah being different from what is mentioned in al-Asl and similar works like al-Jami' al-Saghir among the books of zahir al-riwayah. He added to what I said that the gist of his statement is what is understood from al-Kamal's statement about correct derivation from Abu Hanifa's principle, and that the problem with Muhammad's insistence on contradicting the one from whom he narrated does not disappear.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute. It discusses the ruling on the number of rak'ahs to be performed (qadha) when one omits the sitting (qa'dah) or recitation in Witr and supererogatory prayers, with a focus on a disagreement regarding a narration from Abu Hanifa. The text explains that in reality there are nine scenarios requiring two rak'ahs and six requiring four, though commonly referred to as eight. The core dispute is: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (according to Muhammad's narration) say that the tahrimah (prohibition of nullifying actions) remains, so if one recites in both an early and a late rak'ah, four rak'ahs are required. Muhammad, however, says that the tahrimah is lifted, so only the first two rak'ahs need to be performed. The passage then delves into a meta-dispute about the authenticity of Muhammad's narration: Abu Yusuf denied having narrated that view from Abu Hanifa, but Muhammad insisted he did. The mashayikh (later Hanafi scholars) relied on Muhammad's narration, treating it as zahir al-riwaya (apparent/well-known transmission). The text recounts the famous six mas'ala (six issues) where Abu Yusuf corrected Muhammad's narration, but Muhammad claimed Abu Yusuf forgot. It explains that the mashayikh accepted Muhammad's narration because it was based on direct hearing from Abu Hanifa (without intermediary) according to some accounts, or because it is found in books of zahir al-riwaya. The passage concludes with a discussion of the layers of Hanafi transmissions: zahir al-riwaya (tawatur/mashhur), nawadir (rare), and later derivations. It resolves that Muhammad's narration is accepted because it is in al-Jami' al-Saghir, a book of zahir al-riwaya.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The prohibition of nullifying actions after beginning prayer; it ends with the final taslim.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known transmissions from Muhammad al-Shaybani in his six major books, established by tawatur or widespread acceptance.
الست مسائل (al-sitt masai'l): Six specific issues where Muhammad al-Shaybani claimed Abu Yusuf forgot the correct narration from Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) of the Hanafi school, how many rak'ahs must be performed if one recites in both one of the first two and one of the last two rak'ahs in Witr?
A) Two rak'ahs
B) Four rak'ahs
C) Eight rak'ahs
D) Six rak'ahs

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school for the qadha of rak'ahs when recitation is omitted in a specific pattern is four rak'ahs, based on the mashayikh's reliance on Muhammad's rivayah.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Do Not Pray After a Prayer the Like of It: The Hanafi Ruling on Repeating Prayers
Commentary on hadith prohibiting repetition of same prayer type

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on repeating a fard prayer in congregation and distinguish the cases where repetition is makruh tahrimi, wajib, or allowed.

Core Idea
Repeating a prayer in the same manner is makruh; but if the first was deficient, repetition becomes wajib.

The hadith 'Do not pray after a prayer the like of it' appears to prohibit any repetition, but the Hanafi school demonstrates that it cannot be taken at face value. Through careful analysis of the Companions' practice and the principle of takhsis, they derive a nuanced ruling that balances the prohibition with the necessity of correcting deficiencies. This lesson unpacks the key distinctions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent contradiction
The hadith seems to prohibit all repetition, but we observe clear exceptions (e.g., sunnah followed by fard of same rak'at count). Recognize that the general meaning cannot be applied universally.
2
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
When a general text (amm) cannot apply to all instances, it must be restricted to its most specific meaning (a'amm al-khusus). Determine what specific case the hadith targets.
3
Examine the Hanafi interpretation
The prohibition is limited to repeating a prayer in the same congregation manner without a valid reason, as derived from the practice of Ibn 'Umar and others.
4
Distinguish the four cases
Learn the four scenarios: (1) valid first prayer in jam'ah repeated in jam'ah → makruh; (2) repetition at makruh times → makruh; (3) certain deficiency → wajib; (4) uncertainty due to waswasa → makruh.
5
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
See how the Shafi'i school takes the hadith absolutely, leading to different practical rulings. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text

ولا يصلي بعد صلاة مثلها هذا لفظ الحديث كما في كتب الفقه وجعله في فتح القدير وغاية البيان أثراً عن عمر رضي الله عنه . وقال عبد الله بن مسعود : لا يصلي على إثر صلاة مثلها. وهذا الحديث خص منه البعض لأنه يصلي سنة الفجر ثم الفرض وهما مثلان، وكذا يصلي سنة الظهر أربعاً ثم يصلي الفرض أربعاً، وكذا يصلي السنة ركعتين في السفر ثم يصلي الفرض ركعتين، فلما لم يمكن إجراؤه على العموم وجب حمله على أخص الخصوص كما هو الحكم في العام إذا لم يمكن العمل فقال محمد في الجامع الصغير : المراد منه أن لا يصلي بعد أداء الظهر نافلة ركعتان بقراءة بعمومه . وركعتان بغير قراءة يعني لا تصلي النافلة كذلك حتى لا تكون مثلاً للفرض بل يقرأ في جميع ركعات النفل . قال قاضيخان في شرح الجامع الصغير : ولو حمل على النهي عن تكرار الجماعة في المسجد أو على النهي عن قضاء الفرائض مخافة الخلل في المؤدي كان حسناً فإن ذلك مكروه انتهى . واستدل في فتح القدير للأول بما في أبي داود عن سليمان بن يسار قال : أتيت ابن عمر على البلاط وهم يصلون قلت : ألا تصلي معهم ؟ قال : قد صليت إني سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول : لا تصلوا صلاة في يوم مرتين . وروى مالك في الموطأ حدثنا نافع أن رجلاً سأل ابن عمر إني أصلي في بيتي ثم أدرك الصلاة مع الإمام أفأصلي معه؟ فقال ابن عمر : نعم . فقال : أيتهما أجعل صلاتي ؟ فقال ابن عمر : ليس ذلك إليك إنما ذلك إلى الله يجعل أيتهما شاء. فهذا من ابن دليل على أن الذي روي عن سليمان بن يسار عنه إنما أراد كلتاهما على وجه الفرض أو إذا صلى في جماعة فلا يعيد وفيه نفي لقول الشافعية انتهى . فالحاصل أن تكرار الصلاة إن كان مع الجماعة في المسجد على هيئته الأولى فمكروه وإلا فإن كان في وقت يكره التنفل بعد الفرض فمكروه كما بعد الصبح والعصر، وإلا فإن كان الخلل في المؤدى، فإن كان ذلك الخلل متقاً إما بترك واجب أو بارتكاب مكروه فغير مكروه بل واجب كما قدمناه مراراً. وصرح به في الذخيرة وقال : إنه لا يتناوله النهي، وإن كان ذلك الخلل غير محقق بل نشأ عن وسوسة فهو مكروه. وفي مآل الفتاوى : ولو لم يفته شيء من الصلوات وأحب أن يقضي جميعا الصلوات التي صلاها متداركاً لا يستحب له ذلك إلا إذا كان غالب ظنه فساد ما صلى لورود النهي عنه ، وما حكي عن أبي حنيفة أنه قضى صلاة عمره فإن صح النقل فنقول : كان يصلي المغرب والوتر أربع ركعات بثلاث قعدات انتهى. وذكر في النهاية أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لما صلى الفجر ضحى النهار بعد ليلة التعريس قال له أصحابه من الغد: ألا نعيد صلاة الأمس ؟ فقال : إن الله ينهاكم عن الربا أفيقبله منكم !؟ كذا ذكره فخر الإسلام. وبما قررناه ظهر أن ذكر المصنف في المختصر لفظ الحديث مع أن عمومه ليس بمراد مما لا ينبغي .
And he does not pray after a prayer the like of it. This is the wording of the hadith as in fiqh books. Al-Fath al-Qadir and Ghayat al-Bayan made it an athar from Umar (may Allah be pleased with him). And Abdullah ibn Mas'ud said: Do not pray after a prayer the like of it. This hadith has been partially excepted because one prays the sunnah of Fajr then the fard, and they are two likes, and likewise one prays the sunnah of Zuhr four then the fard four, and likewise one prays the sunnah two rak'ahs in travel then the fard two rak'ahs. So when it is not possible to apply it generally, it becomes necessary to carry it upon the most specific of particularizations as is the rule for the general when it cannot be implemented. So Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: The intent of it is that one should not pray after performing Zuhr a supererogatory (nafl) prayer of two rak'ahs with recitation in all of it, and two rak'ahs without recitation—meaning do not pray the nafl in such a way that it becomes a like of the fard, but rather you recite in all the rak'ahs of the nafl. Qadikhan said in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir: If it is carried upon the prohibition of repeating the congregation in the mosque, or upon the prohibition of making up the fara'id (obligatory prayers) out of fear of imperfection in the performed prayer, that would be good, for that is makruh. End. And in Fath al-Qadir, evidence for the first is given from Abu Dawud from Sulayman ibn Yasar: I came to Ibn 'Umar at the paved area while they were praying. I said: Will you not pray with them? He said: I have already prayed. I heard the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) say: Do not pray a prayer twice in one day. And Malik narrated in al-Muwatta: Nafi' told us that a man asked Ibn 'Umar: I pray in my house and then catch up with the congregation with the imam, shall I pray with him? Ibn 'Umar said: Yes. The man said: Which of them shall I count as my prayer? Ibn 'Umar said: That is not up to you; that is up to Allah; He will make whichever of them He wishes. So from Ibn 'Umar this indicates that what was narrated from Sulayman ibn Yasar about him meant both of them as fard, or if he prayed in congregation then he does not repeat. And in it is a refutation of the Shafi'is. End. The conclusion is that repeating a prayer, if it is with congregation in the mosque in the same manner as the first, is makruh; otherwise, if it is at a time when supererogatory (nafl) prayer after fard is makruh, it is makruh, such as after Fajr and 'Asr; otherwise, if there is imperfection in the performed prayer, then if that imperfection is certain, either by leaving an obligatory (wajib) or committing a makruh, then it is not makruh, rather it is obligatory (wajib) as we have stated many times. And it is explicitly stated in al-Dhakhira and said: The prohibition does not include it. And if that imperfection is not certain but arose from waswasa (whispers), then it is makruh. And in Ma'al al-Fatawa: If one has not missed any of the prayers and wishes to make up all the prayers he performed consecutively, it is not recommended for him to do so unless his predominant thought is that what he prayed was corrupt because of the prohibition. And what is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he made up (qada') prayers of his entire life, if the transmission is sound, we say: He used to pray Maghrib and Witr as four rak'ahs with three sittings. End. And in al-Nihaya: When the Prophet (ﷺ) prayed Fajr in the forenoon after the night of staying (al-ta'rees), his companions said the next day: Shall we not repeat yesterday's prayer? He said: Allah forbids you from Riba, would He accept it from you? Thus mentioned Fakhr al-Islam. And by what we have established, it becomes clear that the author's mention in al-Mukhtasar of the wording of the hadith, while its generality is not intended, is something not appropriate.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe into the ruling of repeating prayers, focusing on the hadith 'Do not pray a prayer like it after a prayer.' The author establishes that the hadith cannot be taken generally because there are clear exceptions: one prays the sunnah of Fajr then the fard, both two rak'ahs, and similarly for Zuhr (four rak'ahs each) and travel prayers (two rak'ahs each). So the prohibition must refer to specific types of repetition. Imam Muhammad specifies it means not to pray a nafl of two rak'ahs with recitation like the fard after Zuhr. Qadikhan suggests it refers to repeating congregation or making up fara'id. The discussion then cites Ibn 'Umar's practice to show that repeating a prayer with congregation is possible if the first was alone, refuting the Shafi'i position that it is impermissible. The conclusion summarizes four cases: (1) repeating a prayer with congregation in the same manner is makruh; (2) repeating at a time when nafl is makruh (e.g., after Fajr/'Asr) is makruh; (3) if the first prayer had a certain deficiency (missing a wajib or committing makruh), repeating becomes wajib; (4) if the deficiency is uncertain due to waswasa, repeating is makruh. Finally, the story of the Prophet after the night of al-Ta'rees shows that repeating a valid prayer out of scrupulousness is not accepted. The author criticizes the matn author for quoting the hadith generally when its general application is not intended. The commentary consistently follows Hanafi methodology: it does not reject the hadith but restricts its application through specific exceptions, using the principle that when a general cannot operate fully, it is carried to its most specific meaning.

Key Terms
لا يصلي بعد صلاة مثلها (lā yuṣallī ba‘da ṣalātin mithlahā): A hadith meaning 'Do not pray after a prayer the like of it' — misunderstood by some to prohibit all repetition, but the Hanafis interpret it restrictively.
تكرار الصلاة (takrār al-ṣalāh): Repeating a prayer after having already performed it, either individually or in congregation.
خلل في المؤدي (khalal fī al-mu'addā): Defect or imperfection in the prayer performed, such as missing a wajib or committing a makruh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, repeating a fard prayer with congregation is makruh tahrimi when:
A) The first prayer was performed alone.
B) The first prayer was deficient.
C) The first prayer was performed in congregation and the repetition is in the same manner.
D) The repetition occurs after 'Asr.

Key Takeaway
The hadith 'Do not pray a prayer twice' is not absolute; Hanafis restrict it to cases where both prayers are identical in congregation, allowing repetition when the first was alone or deficient.

Ruling on Repeating a Prayer in Congregation (I'adah al-Salah)
Analyzes the hadith prohibition and conditions for repeating prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between makruh and wajib repetition of congregational prayer, based on the presence of a defect in the first prayer.

Core Idea
Repeating a prayer in congregation is makruh unless the first prayer had a certain defect, in which case it becomes wajib.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a common question: if you have already prayed, can you join a congregation for the same prayer? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced answer based on a hadith and the practice of Ibn Umar. We will analyze the position and the counter-argument of the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the basic ruling: repeating a prayer in congregation in the same form as the first is makruh (disliked). But if the first prayer had a certain defect (leaving a wajib or committing a makruh), repetition becomes wajib (obligatory).
Note the key distinction: no defect = makruh; defect = wajib.
2
Identify the opponent's view
The Shafi'i school holds that repeating any prayer in congregation is absolutely prohibited based on the literal interpretation of the hadith 'Do not pray a prayer twice in one day.'
This is a general prohibition from their perspective.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i evidence is the hadith itself, taken at face value. They do not allow exceptions.
They consider the hadith as 'amm (general) with no takhsis.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school interprets the hadith as specific to repeating the fard prayer in the same form in congregation, not absolute. They cite the practice of Ibn Umar who allowed a man who prayed alone to join the congregation for the same prayer.
This is a form of takhsis al-amm bi al-urf or by qawl al-sahabi.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi allows repetition when the first prayer was defective (wajib), and considers it merely makruh otherwise. Shafi'i prohibits all repetition in congregation.
This has direct implications for a person who wishes to join a congregation after already praying.

كتاب الصلاة باب الوتر والنوافل
قدرته على القيام ابتداء وبناء وراكباً خارج المصر مومياً إلى أي جهة توجهت دابته وبنى
عمر
فقال :
إجراؤه على العموم وجب حمله على أخص الخصوص كما هو الحكم في العام إذا لم يمكن العمل فقال محمد في الجامع الصغير : المراد منه أن لا يصلي بعد أداء الظهر نافلة ركعتان بقراءة بعمومه . وركعتان بغير قراءة يعني لا تصلي النافلة كذلك حتى لا تكون مثلاً للفرض بل يقرأ في جميع ركعات النفل . قال قاضيخان في شرح الجامع الصغير : ولو حمل على النهي عن تكرار الجماعة في المسجد أو على النهي عن قضاء الفرائض مخافة الخلل في المؤدي كان حسناً فإن ذلك مكروه انتهى . واستدل في فتح القدير للأول بما في أبي داود عن سليمان بن يسار قال : أتيت ابن عمر على البلاط وهم يصلون قلت : ألا تصلي معهم ؟ قال : قد صليت إني سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول : لا تصلوا صلاة في يوم مرتين . وروى مالك في الموطأ حدثنا نافع أن رجلاً سأل ابن عمر إني أصلي في بيتي ثم أدرك الصلاة مع الإمام أفأصلي معه؟ فقال ابن عمر : نعم . فقال : أيتهما أجعل صلاتي ؟ فقال ابن عمر : ليس ذلك إليك إنما ذلك إلى الله يجعل أيتهما شاء. فهذا من ابن دليل على أن الذي روي عن سليمان بن يسار عنه إنما أراد كلتاهما على وجه الفرض أو إذا صلى في جماعة فلا يعيد وفيه نفي لقول الشافعية انتهى . فالحاصل أن تكرار الصلاة إن كان مع الجماعة في المسجد على هيئته الأولى فمكروه وإلا فإن كان في وقت يكره التنفل بعد الفرض فمكروه كما بعد الصبح والعصر، وإلا فإن كان الخلل في المؤدى، فإن كان ذلك الخلل متقاً إما بترك واجب أو بارتكاب مكروه فغير مكروه بل واجب كما قدمناه مراراً. وصرح به في الذخيرة وقال : إنه لا يتناوله النهي، وإن كان ذلك الخلل غير محقق بل نشأ عن وسوسة فهو مكروه. وفي مآل الفتاوى : ولو لم يفته شيء من الصلوات وأحب أن يقضي جميعا الصلوات التي صلاها متداركاً لا يستحب له ذلك إلا إذا كان غالب ظنه فساد ما صلى لورود النهي عنه ، وما حكي عن أبي حنيفة أنه قضى صلاة عمره فإن صح النقل فنقول : كان يصلي المغرب والوتر أربع ركعات بثلاث قعدات انتهى. وذكر في النهاية أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لما صلى الفجر ضحى النهار بعد ليلة التعريس قال له أصحابه من الغد: ألا نعيد صلاة الأمس ؟ فقال : إن الله ينهاكم عن الربا أفيقبله منكم !؟ كذا ذكره فخر الإسلام. وبما قررناه ظهر أن ذكر المصنف في المختصر لفظ الحديث مع أن عمومه ليس بمراد مما لا ينبغي .
قوله : (فإن كان ذلك الخلل محققاً الخ يفيد بإطلاقه أنه لو صلى الفريضة منفرداً عذر أنه له إعادتها مع الجماعة في سائر الأوقات لارتكاب المكروه لم أر من صرح به فليتأمل، لكن يخالفه ما ذكروه في الفصل الآتي من التفصيل من أنه لو صلى ركعة فأقيمت يقطع ويقتدي إلى آخر ما يأتي إلا أن يحمل ذاك على ما إذا كانت صلاته منفرداً مع العذر المسوغ لترك الجماعة وهو بعيد
Book of Prayer, Chapter on Witr and Supererogatory Prayers: ... The summary is that repeating prayer, if it is with congregation in the mosque in its first form, is disliked. Otherwise, if it is in a time when supererogatory prayer after the obligatory is disliked, as after Fajr and Asr, then it is disliked. Otherwise, if there is a defect in the performed prayer: if that defect is certain, either by leaving an obligatory act or committing a disliked act, then it is not disliked, rather obligatory, as we have mentioned repeatedly. It is stated in al-Dhakhirah that it is not included in the prohibition. If that defect is not certain but arises from waswasa, then it is disliked.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the ruling on repeating the same prayer in congregation. The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq presents the Hanafi position, supported by the hadith of Ibn Umar and the clarification of the intent behind the prohibition. The initial hadith 'Do not pray a prayer twice in one day' is interpreted as referring to repeating a prayer as a fard (obligatory) repetition, not general. The Hanafi view distinguishes between repeating in congregation (makruh) and repeating when the first prayer had a defect (obligatory to correct). The Shafi'i position is refuted. The commentary explains conditions under which repetition is permissible or obligatory, with evidences from the sunnah and practice of the sahaba.

Key Terms
إعادة الصلاة (i'adah al-salah): Repeating a prayer that has already been performed, specifically the same obligatory prayer.
تكرار الجماعة (tikrar al-jama'ah): Performing a prayer in congregation after having already prayed it, either alone or with another congregation.
مكروه (makruh): A disliked act that is not prohibited but is discouraged. In this context, it is makruh tanzih (close to halal) except when obligatory.
الخلل (al-khalal): A defect or deficiency in the prayer, such as leaving a wajib or committing a makruh.
وسوسة (waswasah): Whisperings or doubts from Shaytan that cause uncertainty about the validity of the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When the first prayer was done without wudu
B) When the first prayer had a certain defect, like leaving a wajib
C) When the prayer time is about to end
D) When one prayed alone and then found a congregation

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on i'adah al-salah is conditioned on the presence of a certain defect in the first prayer; otherwise, it is merely makruh.

Praying Nawafil While Sitting with Ability to Stand
Establishes the ruling and reward for sitting voluntary prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying nafl while sitting with ability to stand, cite the primary evidence (hadith and consensus), and distinguish between ability and inability regarding reward.

Core Idea
Praying nafl sitting with ability is valid but yields half the reward of standing; full reward is for those unable to stand.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a common point of confusion: the hadith 'whoever prays sitting has half the reward of the one standing' applies specifically to supererogatory prayers when one is able to stand. The Hanafi school, relying on consensus and the practice of the Prophet, affirms permissibility but with reduced reward. Understanding this distinction is essential for correct fiqh application and for avoiding misconceptions about obligatory prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing supererogatory (nafl) prayers while sitting despite ability to stand. The ruling is permissible (ja'iz) but with half reward compared to standing.
The author introduces this as a point where nafl differs from fard and wajib.
2
Locate the primary evidence
Two main proofs: (1) consensus (ijma') of scholars, (2) hadith from Imran ibn Husayn in Sahih Bukhari: 'Whoever prays standing is better, and whoever prays sitting has half the reward of the one standing.'
Also cited is Aisha's hadith in Sahih Muslim about the Prophet praying much of his prayer sitting in his later years.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit wording 'half the reward' shows both validity and reduced merit. The majority interpret this as specific to nafl with ability; for inability, reward is full. For fard, sitting with ability invalidates the prayer.
The consensus restricts the hadith to nafl; this is the Hanafi position.
4
Address the apparent contradiction
A variant narration mentions 'lying down' giving half reward of sitting. The Hanafi response dismisses this as shadhdh (irregular) because it contradicts established rulings; lying down for nafl with ability is not valid.
Al-Akmal's objection and the response in the text clarify that this variant cannot be applied to nafl with ability.
5
Consolidate the ruling
Thus, the mufta bihi position: sitting for nafl with ability yields half reward; for inability, full reward. For fard/wajib, sitting with ability invalidates the prayer and is sinful.
This distinction is crucial for correct practice and fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب الوتر والنوافل
قوله ( ويتنفل قاعدا مع قدرته على القيام ابتداء وبناء بيان أيضاً لما خلف فيه النفل الفرائض والواجبات وهو جوازه بالقعود مع القدرة على القيام، وقد حكي فيه إجماع العلماء . وفي صحيح مسلم عن عائشة رضي الله عنها أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لم يمت حتى كان يصلي كثيراً من صلاته وهو جالس. وروى البخاري عن عمران بن الحصين مرفوعاً «من صلى قائماً فهو أفضل ومن صلى قاعداً فله نصف أجر القائم» وقد ذكر الجمهور كما نقله النووي أنه محمول على صلاة النفل قاعداً مع القدرة على القيام، وأما إذا صلاه مع عجزه فلا ينقص ثوابه عن ثوابه قائماً، وأما الفرض فلا يصح قاعداً . مع القدرة على القيام ويأثم ويكفر إن استحله، وإن صلى قاعداً لعجزه أو مضطجعاً لعجزه فثوابه كثوابه .اهـ. وتعقبه الأكمل في شرح المشارق بأنه ورد في بعض رواياته ومن صلى نائماً - أي مضطجعاً ـ فله نصف أجر القاعد» ولا يمكن حمله على النفل مع القدرة إذ لا يصح مضطجعاً اللهم إلا أن يحكم بشذوذ هذه الرواية. وفي النهاية انعقد الإجماع على أن صلاة القاعد لعذر بعجزه عن القيام مساوية لصلاة القائم في الفضيلة والأجر انتهى. وفيه نظر لما نقله النووي عن بعضهم أنه على مع عجزه يعمل في جميع النفل وما ترتب على ذلك من الثمانية دليل على هذا التأويل قوله : (وأما إذا صلاه الخ) قال في الفتح واستدلوا له بحديث البخاري في الجهاد إذا مرض العبد أو سافر له مثل ما يعمل مقيماً صحيحاً قوله : (ولا يمكن حمله الخ قال في الفتح ولا نعلم الصلاة نائماً تسوغ إلا في الفرض حالة العجز عن القعود وهذا حينئذ يعكر على حملهم الحديث على النفل وعلى كونه في الفرض لا يسقط من أجر القائم شيء، والحديث الذي استدلوا به على خلاف ذلك أي حديث البخاري في الجهاد إنما يفيد كتابة مثل ما كان يعمله مقيماً صحيحاً وإنما عاقه المرض عن أن شيئاً أصلاً وذلك لا يستلزم احتساب ما صلى قاعداً بالصلاة قائماً لجواز احتسابه نصفاً ثم يكمل له كل عمله . من ذلك وغيره فضلاً وإلا فالمعارضة قائمة لا تزول إلا بتجويز النافلة قائماً ولا أعلمه فقهنا قوله : ( وفيه نظر الخ) أقول : هذا النظر ظاهر لأن ما نقله النووي عن بعضهم هو المتبادر من الحديث لوجوه : الأول كلمة «من» فإنها عامة في كل مصل الثاني قوله من صلى نائماً» وهو موجود في صحيح البخاري. الثالث أن المذكور في صحيح البخاري أن عمران رضي الله تعالى عنه كانت به بواسير فسأل النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم فذكر الحديث. وبهذا الوجه مع اللذين قبله يبعد حمله
Book of Prayer, Chapter on Witr and Supererogatory Prayers: His statement: 'And he may perform supererogatory prayer sitting, with the ability to stand, initially and continuously' is also an explanation of what differentiates supererogatory from obligatory and required prayers, namely its permissibility while sitting despite ability to stand. Scholarly consensus is narrated on this. In Sahih Muslim from Aisha that the Prophet (peace be upon him) until he died used to pray much of his prayer sitting. Bukhari narrated from Imran ibn Husayn raised: 'Whoever prays standing is better, and whoever prays sitting has half the reward of the one standing.' The majority, as transmitted by al-Nawawi, interpret it as referring to supererogatory prayer while sitting with ability to stand. As for praying out of inability, his reward is not diminished. As for obligatory prayer, it is not valid sitting if able to stand, and he sins and becomes an unbeliever if he considers it permissible. If he prays sitting due to inability or lying down due to inability, his reward is like that of standing.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the permissibility and reward of praying supererogatory (nafl) prayers while sitting even if one is able to stand. The author presents the Hanafi position based on consensus (ijma') and hadith. The hadith of Imran ibn Husayn is interpreted by the majority to apply to nafl with ability, not to obligatory prayers or cases of inability. The text also discusses an objection by al-Akmal regarding a variant narration mentioning lying down, but the Hanafi view maintains that lying down is not valid for nafl with ability. The discussion includes the principle that the reward for a voluntary good deed is multiplied by Allah's grace, but the hadith specifies half reward for sitting. For those who are unable, the reward is complete as per the hadith of jihad (sickness/travel). The analysis concludes that the variant narration cannot be applied to nafl with ability, as it would contradict agreed upon rulings.

Key Terms
التنفل قاعداً (al-tanafful qa'idan): Performing supererogatory prayers while sitting, even though one is able to stand.
القيام (al-qiyam): Standing in prayer; for nafl it is recommended but not obligatory; for fard it is a pillar if able.
الأجر (al-ajr): The reward from Allah for performing the prayer. For sitting prayer, half of standing prayer's reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Full reward equal to standing
B) Half the reward of standing
C) No reward because it is invalid
D) Double the reward of standing

Key Takeaway
Praying supererogatory prayers while sitting with ability is permissible but yields half the reward; obligatory prayers require standing and sitting invalidates them.

Ruling on Voluntary Prayers While Sitting: Permissibility and Reward
Ruling with proof and scholarly discussion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing voluntary prayers while sitting, distinguish between the able and incapable scenarios, and explain the evidence from the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn.

Core Idea
Voluntary prayer while sitting is permissible; reward is half for the able, full for the incapable.

This lesson examines a distinctive ruling of the Hanafi school: voluntary prayers (nafl) can be performed while sitting even if one is able to stand. The core issue is the reward: does it decrease? We will explore the textual evidence from the Prophet's practice and explicit hadith, and see how the Hanafi scholars reconcile different narrations and opinions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the legal classification is. In this passage, the act is performing voluntary prayer (nafl) while sitting. The ruling is permissible (ja'iz) with a distinction between the able and the incapable.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the main proof cited. The author uses the hadith from Imran ibn Husayn: 'Whoever prays standing is better, and whoever prays sitting has half the reward of the standing one.' Also the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet often prayed sitting.
Hadith is from Sahih Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith yield the ruling? The explicit statement of half reward is taken as general (amm) for the able, but the context (Imran ibn Husayn had hemorrhoids) indicates the hadith was about one who is unable. The majority interpret it for the able to distinguish from the incapable.
4
Note the ikhtilaf on reward for the incapable
Some scholars (like al-Nihaya) claim consensus that reward is equal to standing for the incapable. Others argue the hadith implies half even for the able, and for the incapable full reward is given due to other evidence (hadith of illness/travel). The author leans toward half for able, full for incapable.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school: Voluntary prayer sitting is permissible; for the able, reward is half that of standing; for the incapable, reward is equal to standing. This is based on combining the hadith evidence and the principle that necessity removes the reduction.
Zahir al-Riwayah supports this.

قوله ( ويتنفل قاعدا مع قدرته على القيام ابتداء وبناء بيان أيضاً لما خلف فيه النفل الفرائض والواجبات وهو جوازه بالقعود مع القدرة على القيام، وقد حكي فيه إجماع العلماء . وفي صحيح مسلم عن عائشة رضي الله عنها أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لم يمت حتى كان يصلي كثيراً من صلاته وهو جالس. وروى البخاري عن عمران بن الحصين مرفوعاً «من صلى قائماً فهو أفضل ومن صلى قاعداً فله نصف أجر القائم (۱) وقد ذكر الجمهور كما نقله النووي أنه محمول على صلاة النفل قاعداً مع القدرة على القيام، وأما إذا صلاه مع عجزه فلا ينقص ثوابه عن ثوابه قائماً، وأما الفرض فلا يصح قاعداً . مع القدرة على القيام ويأثم ويكفر إن استحله، وإن صلى قاعداً لعجزه أو مضطجعاً لعجزه فثوابه كثوابه .اهـ. وتعقبه الأكمل في شرح المشارق بأنه ورد في بعض رواياته ومن صلى نائماً - أي مضطجعاً ـ فله نصف أجر القاعد» (۲) ولا يمكن حمله على النفل مع القدرة إذ لا يصح مضطجعاً اللهم إلا أن يحكم بشذوذ هذه الرواية. وفي النهاية انعقد الإجماع على أن صلاة القاعد لعذر بعجزه عن القيام مساوية لصلاة القائم في الفضيلة والأجر انتهى. وفيه نظر لما نقله النووي عن بعضهم أنه على يعمل في جميع النفل وما ترتب على ذلك من الثمانية دليل على هذا التأويل قوله : (وأما إذا صلاه الخ) قال في الفتح واستدلوا له بحديث البخاري في الجهاد إذا مرض العبد أو سافر له مثل ما يعمل مقيماً صحيحاً (۱) قوله : (ولا يمكن حمله الخ قال في الفتح ولا نعلم الصلاة نائماً تسوغ إلا في الفرض حالة العجز عن القعود وهذا حينئذ يعكر على حملهم الحديث على النفل وعلى كونه في الفرض لا يسقط من أجر القائم شيء، والحديث الذي استدلوا به على خلاف ذلك أي حديث البخاري في الجهاد إنما يفيد كتابة مثل ما كان يعمله مقيماً صحيحاً وإنما عاقه المرض عن أن شيئاً أصلاً وذلك لا يستلزم احتساب ما صلى قاعداً بالصلاة قائماً لجواز احتسابه نصفاً ثم يكمل له كل عمله . من ذلك وغيره فضلاً وإلا فالمعارضة قائمة لا تزول إلا بتجويز النافلة قائماً ولا أعلمه فقهنا قوله : (وفيه نظر الخ) أقول : هذا النظر ظاهر لأن ما نقله النووي عن بعضهم هو المتبادر من الحديث لوجوه : الأول كلمة «من» فإنها عامة في كل مصل الثاني قوله من صلى نائماً» وهو موجود في صحيح البخاري. الثالث أن المذكور في صحيح البخاري أن عمران رضي الله تعالى عنه كانت به بواسير فسأل النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم فذكر الحديث. وبهذا الوجه مع اللذين قبله يبعد حمله (۱) رواه البخاري في كتاب التقصير باب ۱۷ الترمذي في كتاب المواقيت باب ١٥٧. النسائي في كتاب قيام الليل باب ۲۱ ابن ماجه في كتاب الإقامة باب ١٤١. (۲) رواه الترمذي في كتاب الصلاة باب ١٥٧ ابن ماجه في كتاب الإقامة باب ١٤١. النسائي في كتاب الليل باب ٢٠. الموطأ في كتاب الجماعة حديث ۲۰ أحمد في مسنده (۲/ ١٦٢، ١٩٣) (٦/ ٦١، ۷۱). (۳) رواه البخاري في كتاب الجهاد باب ١٣٤. أحمد في مسنده (٤/ ٤١٠، ٤١٨). وذكر في المجتبي بعد ما نقل الحديث قالوا : وهذا في حق القادر ، أما العاجز فصلاته بإيماء أفضل . من صلاة القائم الراكع الساجد لأنه جهد المقل انتهى ولا يخفى ما فيه بل الظاهر المساواة كما في النهاية وقد عد من خصائصه أن نافلته قاعداً القدرة على القيام كنافلته قائماً تشريفاً له ، ويشهد له ما في صحيح مسلم عن عبد الله بن عمر وقال : حدثت أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : إن صلاة الرجل قاعداً نصف الصلاة قال: فأتيته فوجدته يصلي قاعداً فوضعت يدي على رأسه فقال : ما لك يا عبد الله بن عمرو ؟ قلت: حدثت يا رسول الله أنك قلت صلاة الرجل قاعداً على نصف الصلاة وأنت تصلي قاعداً قال : أجل ولكني لست كأحد منكم انتهى .
His saying: (He may perform voluntary prayers while sitting despite ability to stand, initially and in continuation) is also an explanation of what distinguishes supererogatory prayers from obligatory and necessary ones, namely its permissibility while sitting despite ability to stand. Consensus of scholars has been reported on this. In Sahih Muslim from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) until he died used to pray much of his prayer while sitting. And al-Bukhari narrated from Imran ibn Husayn raised: 'Whoever prays standing is better, and whoever prays sitting has half the reward of the standing one.' The majority, as al-Nawawi reported, hold that this is interpreted as voluntary prayer while sitting despite ability to stand. As for if he prays it while unable, his reward is not diminished from the reward of the standing one. As for obligatory prayer, it is not valid while sitting if able to stand, and he sins and becomes a disbeliever if he considers it permissible. If he prays sitting due to inability, or lying down due to inability, then his reward is like his reward. The Akmal in his commentary on al-Mashariq objected that in some narrations it has 'and whoever prays sleeping (i.e., lying down) has half the reward of the sitting one.' It cannot be interpreted as voluntary prayer while able, since lying down is not valid for voluntary prayer unless one rules that this narration is anomalous. In al-Nihaya, consensus is reported that the prayer of one sitting due to inability is equivalent to the prayer of the standing one in virtue and reward. This is questionable due to what al-Nawawi reported from some that it applies to all voluntary prayers... The eight? is evidence for this interpretation... His saying: (As for if he prays it...) Al-Fath said they used as evidence the hadith of al-Bukhari in Jihad: 'When a servant falls ill or travels, he gets the like of what he used to do when resident and healthy.' His saying: (It cannot be interpreted...) Al-Fath said: We do not know that sleeping prayer is permissible except in obligatory prayer when unable to sit, and this then contradicts their interpretation of the hadith as voluntary and that in obligatory prayer nothing of the reward of the standing is forfeited. The hadith they used as evidence, i.e., the hadith of al-Bukhari in Jihad, only indicates writing of the like of what he used to do when resident and healthy, and only illness prevented him from doing anything at all, and that does not necessitate counting what he prayed sitting as like prayer standing, because it could be counted as half and then his entire work is completed for him out of favor... Otherwise the contradiction remains unresolved except by allowing voluntary prayer standing, and I do not know that our fiqh allows it. His saying: (And there is consideration...) I say: This consideration is apparent because what al-Nawawi reported from some is the obvious meaning of the hadith for several reasons: First, the word 'whoever' is general for every prayer. Second, his saying 'whoever prays sleeping' is found in Sahih al-Bukhari. Third, what is mentioned in Sahih al-Bukhari that Imran (may Allah be pleased with him) had hemorrhoids and asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) and he mentioned the hadith. With this and the previous two points, interpreting it (as only for the incapable) is far-fetched. And it is mentioned in al-Mujtaba after quoting the hadith: They said: This is for the one who is able; as for the incapable, his prayer with gestures is better than the prayer of the one standing, bowing and prostrating, because it is the effort of the destitute. End. And it is not hidden what is in it; rather the apparent is equality as in al-Nihaya. And it is counted among his special characteristics that his voluntary prayer while sitting with ability to stand is like his voluntary prayer standing, as an honor for him. Evidence for this is what is in Sahih Muslim from Abdullah ibn Amr: He said: It was narrated to me that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The prayer of a man sitting is half of prayer.' He said: I came to him and found him praying sitting, so I placed my hand on his head. He said: 'What is the matter with you, O Abdullah ibn Amr?' I said: It was narrated to me, O Messenger of Allah, that you said the prayer of a man sitting is half of prayer, and you are praying sitting. He said: 'Yes, but I am not like any one of you.' End.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is an expansion on the ruling in Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding performing voluntary prayers (nafl) while sitting even when one is capable of standing. The author explains that this is a distinction between supererogatory and obligatory prayers: voluntary prayers may be performed sitting, with evidence from the consensus of scholars and hadith. He cites the hadith from Aisha that the Prophet often prayed sitting, and the hadith from Imran ibn Husayn that one who prays sitting gets half the reward of the one standing. The majority interpret this as referring to voluntary prayer while able. The author then discusses the reward of one who prays sitting due to inability, stating it is equal to standing reward, based on another hadith about illness and travel. He addresses an objection from al-Akmal regarding a variant narration that mentions lying down, and shows it is anomalous. He critiques the claim of consensus that the reward is equal, arguing that the more apparent meaning of the hadith indicates that even sitting with ability reduces reward to half, but for the incapable it is full. He supports this with the context of Imran ibn Husayn's question due to his ailment. The passage thus clarifies the fiqh of voluntary prayer postures and the evidence behind the Hanafi position that sitting is permissible but standing is better for the able.

Key Terms
تنفل (tanafful): Performing supererogatory (nafl) prayers beyond the obligatory ones.
قاعد (qāʿid): Sitting posture in prayer.
قائم (qāʾim): Standing posture in prayer.
فرض (farḍ): Obligatory prayer; must be performed standing if able, otherwise invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn, what is the reward of a person who prays sitting while able to stand?
A) Full reward, same as standing.
B) Half the reward of a standing person.
C) No reward because it is invalid.
D) Double reward because of effort.

Key Takeaway
Voluntary prayer while sitting is permissible; standing is better and yields full reward, while sitting yields half reward for the able but full reward for the incapable.

Difference Between Sunnah of Fajr and Tarawih Regarding Sitting
States the ruling on sitting for sunnah Fajr vs tarawih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing the sunnah of Fajr and tarawih while sitting without excuse, and explain the basis for the distinction.

Core Idea
The sunnah mu'akkada of Fajr cannot be performed sitting without excuse; tarawih can, but it is not recommended.

This lesson examines a specific difference in the Hanafi school between two voluntary prayers: the sunnah of Fajr and tarawih. While both are sunnah, their level of emphasis affects the ruling on performing them sitting down. The passage from Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the relied-upon position and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Identify the act: performing a voluntary prayer (sunnah of Fajr or tarawih) while sitting without an excuse. State the ruling: for sunnah Fajr, it is not permissible (makruh tahrimi); for tarawih, it is permissible but not recommended.
2
Identify the Basis for the Distinction
The distinction is based on the level of emphasis (ta'kid). The sunnah of Fajr is mu'akkada (strongly confirmed) without dispute, while tarawih is lower in emphasis. Sitting contradicts the emphasis of a mu'akkada sunnah.
3
Note the Authority
The ruling is attributed to Qadi Khan in his Fatawa and upheld by Husam al-Din. It is considered the most correct view (al-ashah) in the later Hanafi fatwa tradition.
This is a later fatwa, not from Zahir al-Riwayah.
4
Understand the Limitation
The passage notes 'all of this is regarding the beginning'. This means the ruling applies to starting the prayer sitting, not to continuing after having begun standing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أطلق في التنفل فشمل السنة المؤكدة والتراويح لكن ذكر قاضيخان في فتاواه من باب التراويح الأصح أن سنة الفجر لا يجوز أداؤها قاعداً من غير عذر، والتراويح يجوز أداؤها قاعداً من غير عذر والفرق أن سنة الفجر مؤكدة لا خلاف فيها والتراويح في التأكيد دونها انتهى. وقد نقلناه في سنة الفجر في موضعها من رواية الحسن وهكذا صححه حسام الدين ثم قال : الصحيح أنه لا يستحب في التراويح لمخالفته للتوارث وعمل السلف وهذا كله في الابتداء.
He gave a general ruling in voluntary prayers so it included the confirmed sunnah and tarawih, but Qadi Khan mentioned in his Fatawa in the chapter of tarawih: The most correct is that the sunnah of Fajr is not permissible to perform sitting without an excuse, while tarawih is permissible to perform sitting without an excuse. The difference is that the sunnah of Fajr is confirmed (mu'akkada) without dispute, while tarawih is lower in confirmation. End. And we have transmitted it in the sunnah of Fajr in its place from the narration of al-Hasan, and thus Husam al-Din corrected it. Then he said: The correct view is that it is not recommended in tarawih because it contradicts the inherited practice and the action of the predecessors. And all of this is regarding the beginning.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage states a specific ruling within the Hanafi school: the sunnah mu'akkada of Fajr (the two rak'ahs before Fajr) cannot be performed sitting without a valid excuse, whereas tarawih prayers can be performed sitting without excuse. The difference is based on the level of emphasis: sunnah mu'akkada is strongly confirmed, and sitting without excuse would contradict its emphasis, while tarawih is less emphasized. This ruling is attributed to Qadi Khan and supported by Husam al-Din. However, it is noted that even for tarawih, sitting is not recommended because it goes against the practice of the early Muslims. The author makes clear these rulings apply to the initial commencement of the prayer, not continuation.

Key Terms
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkada): The emphasized supererogatory prayer that is regularly performed by the Prophet; here the sunnah of Fajr.
تراويح (tarawih): Night prayers during Ramadan, consisting of 20 rak'ahs according to Hanafi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for performing the sunnah of Fajr prayer while sitting without an excuse?
A) Permissible and reward is full.
B) Not permissible according to the most correct view.
C) Permissible only if there is hardship.
D) Must be performed lying down.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school strictly prohibits sitting for the sunnah of Fajr without excuse due to its strong emphasis, while tarawih is more lenient but still not recommended.
