Abu Hanifa's Istihsan on Sitting in Nafl Prayer After Starting Standing
Explains Abu Hanifa's istihsan and the two companions' qiyas on sitting after starting standing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on sitting without excuse in nafl prayer after starting standing, explain the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and the two companions, and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Starting a nafl prayer standing does not obligate standing throughout; sitting without excuse is valid but less rewarding.

This lesson addresses a dispute within the Hanafi school. When a person begins a voluntary prayer standing and then sits down without a valid excuse, is the prayer valid? Imam Abu Hanifa says yes, using istihsan, while his two disciples say no, by qiyas. Understanding this dispute reveals the role of istihsan in Hanafi thought and the distinction between obligations arising from commencement versus explicit vows. By the end, you'll be able to apply the mufta bihi view and appreciate the reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and both positions
Identify the exact act: starting a nafl prayer standing, then sitting without excuse. State that Abu Hanifa deems it valid (sahih), while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) deem it invalid (batil).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Explain the companions' qiyas
The two companions analogize commencement to a vow (nadhr). Just as a vow to pray standing obligates standing, starting a prayer standing obligates standing for the entire prayer. The illa is that commencement creates an obligation to complete as begun.
Review the qiyas panel in the toolbox for the full analogy.
3
Explain Abu Hanifa's istihsan
Abu Hanifa distinguishes commencement from a vow. In a vow, standing is explicitly conditioned; in voluntary prayer, the intention is only to pray, not specifically to stand throughout. Standing is a sunnah, not an obligation. Once the sitting part is performed, it is valid because the prayer itself does not require standing for the entire duration.
The istihsan overrides the qiyas due to the difference in explicit undertaking.
4
Identify the tarjih and mufta bihi
The author confirms that Abu Hanifa's view is correct (الصحيح الأول) and is relied upon for fatwa, as noted in al-Muhit and Ghayat al-Bayan.
Authority weight: zahir riwayah; tarjih by later Hanafi scholars.
5
Note the practical consequence
A person who starts a nafl prayer standing and sits without excuse has a valid prayer but loses the extra reward of standing. If he had a vow, he would need to repeat.
The dispute only applies to nafl, not fard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قوله وبناء» بأن شرع فيه قائماً ثم قعد من غير عذر فهو قول أبي حنيفة. وهذا استحسان وعندهما لا يجزئه وهو قياس لأن الشروع معتبر بالنذر، وله أنه لم يباشر القيام فيما بقي ولما باشر صحة بدونه بخلاف النذر لأنه التزمه نصاً حتى لو لم ينص على القيام لا يلزمه القيام عند بعضهم كما لو نذر صلاة لأنه في النفل وصف زائد فلا يلزمه إلا شرط. وعند البعض يلزمه القيام لأن إيجاب العبد معتبر بإيجاب الله وأينما أوجبها الله تعالى أوجبها قائما، والصحيح الأول كالتتابع في الصوم كذا في المحيط وغاية البيان . على صلاة النفل خاصة من غير عذر فالأولى المصير إلى ما قدمناه عن الفتح من احتمال صلاته نصفاً وإكمالها له فضلاً. وفي الكشاف في تفسير قوله تعالى لا يستوي القاعدون من المؤمنين﴾ [النساء : ] الآية . فإن قلت : قد ذكر الله سبحانه مفضلين درجة واحدة ومفضلين درجات فمن هم؟ قلت : أما المفضلون درجة واحدة فهم الذي فضلوا على القاعدين الأخراء، وأما المفضلون درجات فالذين فضلوا على القاعدين الذين أذن لهم في التخلف اكتفاء بغيرهم لأن الغزو فرض كفاية ا هـ . قلت : ففي الآية دليل على أن العامل أفضل من التارك لعذر وهذا لا ينافي في ما مر من حديث البخاري في الجهاد لإمكان حمل ما هناك على كتابه أصل الثواب وما هنا على زيادة المضاعفة بسبب المشقة نظير ما قيل في أن الإخلاص تعدل ثلث القرآن ونحو ذلك والله أعلم قوله : (وله) أي للإمام أبي حنيفة رحمه الله المصلي لم يباشر القيام فيما بقي أي فيما قعد فيه أي لم يشرع فيه قائماً بعد فلا يلزمه القيام ،فيه ولما أي وللذي باشره من الصلاة بصفة القيام أو للذي باشره من الصلاة النافلة مطلقاً صحة بدون القيام بخلاف النذر وحاصله منع كون الشروع موجب موجباً غير أصل ما شرع فيه بناء
And as for his saying 'and in continuation' meaning that he started it standing then sat without excuse: that is the view of Abu Hanifa. This is istihsan, while according to the two companions it is not valid, and this is qiyas because the commencement is considered like a vow. His (Abu Hanifa's) proof: He did not perform the standing in what remained, and because he performed the prayer with validity without it, unlike the vow because he undertook it explicitly, such that if he did not stipulate standing, it is not obligatory upon him according to some, just as if he vowed a prayer, because standing in supererogatory prayer is an extra attribute, so he is only obliged by the condition. According to others, standing is obligatory because the servant's obligation is considered by Allah's obligation, and wherever Allah made it obligatory, He made it standing. The correct view is the first, like continuity in fasting. This is in al-Muhit and Ghayat al-Bayan. Specifically for voluntary prayer without excuse, it is better to revert to what we previously mentioned from al-Fath that his prayer is considered half and completed for him as a favor. And in al-Kashshaf in the interpretation of the verse: 'Not equal are those who sit among the believers' (al-Nisa: 95). If you say: Allah mentioned those preferred one degree and those preferred several degrees: who are they? He said: As for those preferred one degree, they are those who are preferred over the other sitters. As for those preferred several degrees, they are those preferred over the sitters who were permitted to stay behind because others sufficed, since fighting is a communal obligation. End. I say: In this verse there is evidence that the doer is better than the one who abandons due to an excuse, and this does not contradict the previous hadith of al-Bukhari on jihad, because it is possible to interpret that as writing the original reward, and here as an increase in multiplication due to hardship, similar to what is said about sincerity equaling one-third of the Quran and the like. And Allah knows best. His saying: (And his proof) i.e., for Imam Abu Hanifa: The worshipper did not perform the standing in what remained, i.e., in what he sat for, meaning he did not commence it standing thereafter, so standing is not required of him. And 'because' meaning that what he performed of the prayer with the attribute of standing, or what he performed of the voluntary prayer absolutely, is valid without standing, unlike the vow. The summary is the prevention of considering the commencement as necessitating something beyond the original thing he started.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage addresses a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding a person who begins a voluntary prayer standing and then sits down without a valid excuse. According to Abu Hanifa (using istihsan), the prayer remains valid, and the person is not required to remain standing because the obligation of standing was only for the part already performed; the remaining part can be done sitting. However, the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold by qiyas that the prayer is invalid because beginning the prayer with an intention to stand obligates standing throughout, similar to a vow. The author explains the reasoning: Abu Hanifa argues that the commencement is not like a vow because if one merely starts a nafl prayer without stipulating standing, standing is not required. The analogy of fasting with continuity is mentioned. The correct view (as in al-Muhit) is the first (Abu Hanifa's). The passage then includes a discussion of the Quranic verse about sitting and striving, which supports the idea that doing something is better than abstaining even with excuse, but this does not contradict the hadith about jihad because that deals with original reward. The author concludes by reiterating Abu Hanifa's proof that the commencement does not impose extra obligations beyond the original act.

Key Terms
استحسان (istiḥsān): A juristic preference that allows departing from qiyas for a stronger reason; here, Abu Hanifa uses istihsan to validate the prayer.
قياس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning; here, the two companions use qiyas comparing commencement to a vow.
نذر (nadhr): A vow to perform an act of worship; it makes the act obligatory as specified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Reward of Nafl Prayer While Sitting and the Prophet's Exception
The passage establishes the ruling of nafl prayer while sitting, citing the hadith and the Prophet's exception, and then addresses intra-Hanafi distinctions for emphasized sunnah and tarawih.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the reward of nafl prayer while sitting for a capable person, identify the Prophet's exception, and distinguish the rulings for emphasized sunnah (Fajr) and tarawih regarding sitting without excuse.

Core Idea
Nafl prayer sitting gives half reward, but for the Prophet it is full; emphasized sunnah like Fajr cannot be performed sitting without excuse.

The passage from Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the ruling on performing voluntary prayers while sitting. It cites a hadith from Sahih Muslim where the Prophet explains that his own sitting prayer receives full reward due to his special status, while for others it is half. The author then addresses the scope of 'nafl' and highlights distinctions made by later Hanafi jurists regarding the emphasized sunnah of Fajr and tarawih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling and its proof
The hadith 'Prayer of a man sitting is half of prayer' is the primary evidence. This establishes the general rule for nafl prayer for one who is able to stand.
2
Understand the Prophet's exception
The hadith shows the Prophet himself prayed sitting while able, but he stated 'I am not like any of you,' indicating his full reward is a special characteristic (khasa'is).
3
Analyze the scope of 'nafl'
The author notes the ruling includes all supererogatory prayers, but then relates the distinction from Qadikhan regarding emphasized sunnah (Fajr) and tarawih.
4
Apply the distinction: Fajr sunnah vs. tarawih
Qadikhan states the sunnah of Fajr may not be performed sitting without excuse, while tarawih may be. Husam al-Din corrects that tarawih sitting is not recommended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب الوتر والنوافل
النصف من صلاة القائم مع العذر وعليه حمل الحديث فلا إجماع إلا أن يريد به إجماع أئمتنا . وذكر في المجتبي بعد ما نقل الحديث قالوا : وهذا في حق القادر ، أما العاجز فصلاته بإيماء أفضل من صلاة القائم الراكع الساجد لأنه جهد المقل انتهى ولا يخفى ما فيه بل الظاهر المساواة كما في النهاية وقد عد من خصائصه أن نافلته قاعداً القدرة على القيام كنافلته قائماً تشريفاً له ، ويشهد له ما في صحيح مسلم عن عبد الله بن عمر وقال : حدثت أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : إن صلاة الرجل قاعداً نصف الصلاة قال: فأتيته فوجدته يصلي قاعداً فوضعت يدي على رأسه فقال : ما لك يا عبد الله بن عمرو ؟ قلت: حدثت يا رسول الله أنك قلت صلاة الرجل قاعداً على نصف الصلاة وأنت تصلي قاعداً قال : أجل ولكني لست كأحد منكم انتهى . أطلق في التنفل فشمل السنة المؤكدة والتراويح لكن ذكر قاضيخان في فتاواه من باب التراويح الأصح أن سنة الفجر لا يجوز أداؤها قاعداً من غير عذر، والتراويح يجوز أداؤها قاعداً من غير عذر والفرق أن سنة الفجر مؤكدة لا خلاف فيها والتراويح في التأكيد دونها انتهى. وقد نقلناه في سنة الفجر في موضعها من رواية الحسن وهكذا صححه حسام الدين ثم قال : الصحيح أنه لا يستحب في التراويح لمخالفته للتوارث وعمل السلف وهذا كله في الابتداء. وفي الكشاف في تفسير قوله تعالى ﴿لا يستوي القاعدون من المؤمنين﴾ [النساء: 95] الآية . فإن قلت : قد ذكر الله سبحانه مفضلين درجة واحدة ومفضلين درجات فمن هم؟ قلت : أما المفضلون درجة واحدة فهم الذين فضلوا على القاعدين الأخراء، وأما المفضلون درجات فالذين فضلوا على القاعدين الذين أذن لهم في التخلف اكتفاء بغيرهم لأن الغزو فرض كفاية ا هـ . قلت : ففي الآية دليل على أن العامل أفضل من التارك لعذر وهذا لا ينافي في ما مر من حديث البخاري في الجهاد لإمكان حمل ما هناك على كتابة أصل الثواب وما هنا على زيادة المضاعفة بسبب المشقة نظير ما قيل في أن الإخلاص تعدل ثلث القرآن ونحو ذلك والله أعلم
The Book of Prayer, Chapter of Witr and Supererogatory Prayers. Half of the prayer of the standing person with excuse, and upon this the hadith is interpreted; there is no consensus unless he means by it the consensus of our imams. It is mentioned in al-Mujtaba after transmitting the hadith: They said: This applies to the one who is able, but for the incapable, his prayer by gesture is better than the prayer of the standing, bowing, and prostrating, because it is the effort of the impoverished. End of quote. It is not hidden what is in it; rather, apparently it is equal as in al-Nihayah. And it has been counted among his special characteristics that his nafl prayer while sitting despite ability to stand is like his nafl prayer while standing, as an honor for him. This is witnessed by what is in Sahih Muslim from Abdullah ibn Amr, who said: I was told that the Messenger of Allah said: 'The prayer of a man sitting is half of prayer.' He said: I came to him and found him praying sitting, so I placed my hand on his head. He said: 'What is the matter, O Abdullah ibn Amr?' I said: I was told, O Messenger of Allah, that you said: The prayer of a man sitting is half of prayer, and you are praying sitting. He said: 'Yes, but I am not like any of you.' End of quote. He made it absolute regarding nafl, so it includes the emphasized sunnah and tarawih, but Qadikhan mentioned in his Fatawa, in the chapter of tarawih: The most correct is that the sunnah of Fajr may not be performed sitting without excuse, and tarawih may be performed sitting without excuse. The difference is that the sunnah of Fajr is emphasized without difference of opinion, and tarawih is lesser in emphasis. End of quote. We have transmitted it in the sunnah of Fajr in its place from the narration of al-Hasan, and thus Husam al-Din corrected it, then said: The correct view is that it is not recommended in tarawih because it contradicts the transmitted practice and the practice of the salaf. All this applies to the beginning. And in al-Kashshaf, in the interpretation of His statement: 'Not equal are those who sit among the believers' [Quran 4:95]. If you say: Allah has mentioned those favored by one degree and those favored by many degrees; who are they? I say: As for those favored by one degree, they are those who are favored over the other sitters. As for those favored by degrees, they are those who are favored over the sitters who were permitted to remain behind due to sufficiency by others, because jihad is fard kifayah. End of quote. I say: In this verse is evidence that the doer is better than the one who abandons due to an excuse. This does not contradict what has passed in the hadith of Bukhari on jihad, because it is possible to carry what is there on the writing of the original reward, and what is here on the increase of multiplication due to hardship, analogous to what is said that sincerity equals one-third of the Quran and the like. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof discussing the reward of performing nafl prayer while sitting for one who is able to stand. The author begins by noting that the hadith 'the prayer of a man sitting is half of prayer' is interpreted as applying to one who has an excuse, otherwise there is no consensus except among the Hanafi imams. He then cites a narration from Sahih Muslim where Abdullah ibn Amr questions the Prophet about praying sitting despite saying sitting is half reward, and the Prophet responds that he is not like any of them, indicating that the Prophet's nafl prayer while sitting is equal to standing prayer due to his special virtue. The author then addresses the scope of 'nafl' , stating that it includes emphasized sunnah and tarawih. However, Qadikhan's fatwa distinguishes that the sunnah of Fajr cannot be performed sitting without excuse, while tarawih may be, because tarawih is less emphasized. Husam al-Din corrected that it is not recommended in tarawih due to conflicting with transmitted practice. Finally, the author interprets Quran 4:95 to support that the doer is better than the one who remains due to excuse, harmonizing it with the hadith by explaining that the hadith refers to original reward while the verse refers to multiplication due to hardship.

Key Terms
التنفل (al-tanafful): Supererogatory prayers, including sunnah mu'akkadah, mustahabb, and tarawih.
السنة المؤكدة (al-sunnah al-mu'akkadah): Emphasized sunnah prayers that the Prophet regularly performed, like the sunnah of Fajr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on performing the sunnah of Fajr while sitting without an excuse?
A) It is permissible with half reward.
B) It is not permissible.
C) It is recommended.
D) It is equal to standing.

Key Takeaway
The reward of nafl prayer while sitting is half for those able to stand, except for the Prophet; emphasized sunnah like Fajr cannot be performed sitting without excuse.

Starting Nafl Standing Then Sitting: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on nafl standing then sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on starting nafl standing then sitting, explain the qiyas vs istihsan reasoning, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Starting nafl standing obligates standing by qiyas; but istihsan permits sitting.

What happens when you start a voluntary (nafl) prayer standing, but then decide to sit down without any valid excuse? Is your prayer still valid? The Hanafi school has a famous internal disagreement. In this lesson, we analyse the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), and see which view is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of each side: Abu Hanifa says the prayer is valid (sahih) with half reward; the Sahibayn say it is invalid (batil) and must be repeated.
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is the Sahibayn's view per Fath al-Qadir.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The two students (Sahibayn) are the 'opponents' within the school. They hold that once one starts standing, standing becomes obligatory; sitting invalidates.
Their proof is qiyas (analogy) to a vow (nadh).
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Sahibayn reason: commencing the prayer (shuru') is like making a vow. If one vows to pray standing, one must stand. Here, starting the prayer standing is a tacit vow to complete it standing. Therefore, sitting breaks that vow and invalidates the prayer.
This is a qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) because the commonality (illa) is the binding effect of shuru'.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa rejects the illa. He argues that in nafl, standing is a supererogatory quality, not a binding condition. The opening takbir does not specify standing. Moreover, there is a specific concession (rukhsah) in nafl to sit. This is istihsan – a stronger consideration that overrides the qiyas.
Abu Hanifa also distinguishes this from a sick person who gains ability during prayer; that person's tahrimah was for sitting, so standing is permissible.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: According to the Sahibayn, the person must repeat the prayer completely (qada). According to Abu Hanifa, the prayer is valid but reward is halved – no repetition needed. The preponderant (mufta bihi) view is that of the Sahibayn.
Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir ruled the Sahibayn's opinion as stronger.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وله) أي للإمام أبي حنيفة رحمه الله المصلي لم يباشر القيام فيما بقي أي فيما قعد فيه أي لم يشرع فيه قائماً بعد فلا يلزمه القيام ،فيه ولما أي وللذي باشره من الصلاة بصفة القيام أو للذي باشره من الصلاة النافلة مطلقاً صحة بدون القيام بخلاف النذر وحاصله منع كون الشروع موجباً موجباً غير أصل ما شرع فيه بناء على صلاة النفل خاصة من غير عذر فالأولى المصير إلى ما قدمناه عن الفتح من احتمال صلاته نصفاً وإكمالها له فضلاً. ورجح الثاني في فتح القدير بحثاً بأن الصلاة عبارة عن القيام والقراءة إلى آخرها فهو الركن غير أنه يجوز تركه إلى القعود رخصة في النفل فلا ينصرف المطلق إلا إليه. قيدنا قائما بكونه شرع قعد لأنه لو كان على عكسه فإنه يجوز اتفاقاً وهو فعله كما روت عائشة أنه كان يفتتح التطوع قاعداً فيقرأ ورده حتى إذا بقي عشر آيات ونحوها قام إلى آخره، ثم أما حالة القراءة وهكذا كان يفعل في الركعة الثانية . وذكر في التجنيس أن الأفضل أن يقوم فيقرأ شيئاً ثم يركع ليكون موافقاً للسنة، ولو لم يقرأ ولكنه استوى قائماً ثم ركع جاز، وإن لم يستو قائماً وركع لا يجزئه لأنه لا يكون ركوعاً قائماً ولا ركوعاً قاعداً .انتهى وليس هو بناء القوي على الضعيف لأن القعود والقيام في النفل سواء، والفرق لمحمد هذا بين وبين قوله ببطلان صلاة المريض إذا قدر على القيام في أثناء صلاته أن تحريمة المتطوع لم تنعقد للقعود ألبتة بل للقيام لأنه أصل . هو قادر عليه، ثم جاز له شرعاً تركه بخلاف المريض لأنه لم يقدر على القيام فما انعقد إلا للمقدور وهو القعود.
His saying: (and for him) i.e., for Imam Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him: The one praying did not directly perform the standing in what remained, i.e., in what he sat in, meaning he did not start it standing thereafter, so standing is not obligatory for him. And 'for what' i.e., for what he directly performed of prayer with the quality of standing, or for what he directly performed of nafl prayer absolutely, validity without standing, unlike oath. The summary is prevention of the commencement being a cause for something other than the original act that he commenced. So specifically for nafl prayer without excuse, it is better to refer to what we presented from al-Fath of the probability of his prayer being half and its completion being virtue for him. And the second opinion was preponderated in Fath al-Qadir by investigation: Prayer is the term for standing, recitation, etc., up to the end; it is the pillar, except that it is permissible to leave it to sitting as a concession in nafl, so the absolute does not refer except to it. We restricted 'standing' to the one who started then sat, because if it were the opposite, it is agreed permissible, and it is his action, as Aisha narrated that he would open the supererogatory sitting, recite his wird, until when ten verses or so remained, he would stand to the end, then as for the state of recitation, and thus he would do in the second rak'ah. It is mentioned in al-Tajnis that the best is to stand and recite something, then bow, to be in accordance with the sunnah. If he did not recite but stood erect and then bowed, it is permissible. If he did not stand erect and bowed, it does not suffice him, because it is neither a bowing of a standing person nor a bowing of a sitting person. End of quote. It is not building the strong on the weak, because sitting and standing in nafl are equal. The distinction for Muhammad between this and his statement that the prayer of a sick person is invalid if he can stand during his prayer is that the tahrimah of the one performing nafl did not contract for sitting at all, but for standing, because it is the original. He is able to perform it, then it is legally permissible for him to leave it, unlike the sick person, because he was not able to stand, so it only contracted for what was possible, i.e., sitting.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a person who starts a nafl prayer standing and then sits down without a valid excuse. Abu Hanifa rules that such a prayer is valid (by istihsan), because the commencement (tahrimah) was for standing, but sitting is a concession in nafl, and since the person has already performed part standing, the remaining action is valid while sitting. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule that it is invalid (by qiyas), because they analogize it to a vow: just as if one vows to pray standing, he must stand, similarly, once the person started standing, he has committed himself to complete it standing. Abu Hanifa distinguishes that in nafl, standing is not an inherent obligation; it is a supererogatory quality, and the commencement did not obligate standing. The author then presents the preponderance from Fath al-Qadir, which supports the Sahibayn's view, arguing that the prayer's pillar includes standing, but sitting is a concession. He further explains that if one starts sitting and then stands, it is agreed permissible, citing the Prophet's practice. The author also clarifies the distinction between this case and a sick person who gains ability during prayer: the sick person's tahrimah was for sitting, so if he stands, his prayer remains valid; but for the healthy person, tahrimah was for standing, so sitting invalidates it according to the Sahibayn, but Abu Hanifa says the concession for sitting applies.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): A method of reasoning that abandons a clear qiyas for a stronger consideration, such as ease or practice.
الشروع (al-shuru'): The act of beginning the prayer with tahrimah; it creates a commitment to complete the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn in the case of starting nafl standing then sitting without excuse?
A) Abu Hanifa says it is invalid, Sahibayn say it is valid.
B) Abu Hanifa uses istihsan, Sahibayn use qiyas.
C) Abu Hanifa says it is makruh, Sahibayn say it is haram.
D) All agree it is valid with full reward.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, if a person starts a nafl prayer standing and then sits without excuse, the preponderant view (Sahibayn) is that the prayer is invalid; however, Abu Hanifa rules it valid by istihsan.
